1001 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sparks


(13528)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


39 Conn. App. 502; 664 A.2d 1185; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 434


June 5, 1995, Argued  
September 26, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of two counts of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4). Defendant claimed on appeal that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress two out-of-court identifications; improperly instructed the jury; and improperly denied his motion for judgment of acquittal.


OVERVIEW: Witnesses described defendant and identified defendant while sitting in a police cruiser, identified defendant from a photographic display, and made in court identifications. Defendant filed a motion for judgment of acquittal on the ground that the evidence was insufficient to establish beyond a reasonable doubt the identity of defendant as the perpetrator of the offense. The trial court denied the motions. The trial court convicted defendant of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-133(4). On review, the court affirmed. The court found the record was sufficient to permit the review of defendant's unpreserved claim in regard to the trial court's failure to define the term "firearm" as set forth in § 53a-3(19). The court held that the trial court properly charged the jury as to the crime of robbery in the first degree under § 53a-3(19) where the existence of an actual firearm was not an essential element of robbery in the first degree. The court found that defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal was properly denied where the evidence was sufficient for the jury to have determined the identification of defendant as the perpetrator of the crime.


OUTCOME: The court held against defendant, and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1002 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rodriguez


(13900)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


39 Conn. App. 579; 665 A.2d 1357; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 433


February 16, 1995, Argued  
September 26, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of robbery in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree and larceny in the second degree, and with the crimes of burglary in the third degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, conspiracy to commit burglary in the third degree, and larceny in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Stanley, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of robbery in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree, larceny in the second degree, burglary in the third degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, conspiracy to commit burglary in the third degree, and larceny in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, among other contentions, that certain evidence should have been suppressed and that there was insufficient evidence to support the convictions. The court reversed because the search of defendant's pockets was unconstitutional but remanded because the evidence supporting the convictions was otherwise sufficient. The court reviewed the existence of probable cause to arrest defendant for the robbery only as of the time of the arrest for possession of drug paraphernalia because it was the search of defendant's pockets that led to the initial arrest for possession of drug paraphernalia. Viewed in their totality, the facts did not support a finding that there was probable cause to arrest defendant for either possession of narcotics paraphernalia or the burglary. The strength of the evidence acquired from the pockets and from the process of the subsequent arrest was such that the court could not conclude that it did not contribute to the conviction. Nevertheless, defendant was not entitled to an acquittal because there was sufficient evidence to support the convictions even without reliance on the evidence that should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for a new trial.

 

1003 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Sanborn v. Greenwald


(13372)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


39 Conn. App. 289; 664 A.2d 803; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 404


April 25, 1995, Argued  
September 12, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for legal malpractice, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Hammer, J., granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff client brought an action for legal malpractice against defendant attorney in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland (Connecticut), alleging negligent drafting of a modification to a divorce decree and failure to warn of its legal consequences. The trial court granted the attorney's motion for summary judgment based on the three-year limitations period of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-577, and the client appealed.


OVERVIEW: The client brought suit seven years after the attorney's last representation of her, but within three years of the date on which he last discussed the issue with her. The client contended on appeal that the attorney's continuing course of conduct tolled limitations, and that § 52-577 was unconstitutional. The court stated that there was no tolling of statutes of limitations for the failure of an attorney to tell a client that a document drafted by the attorney could be inaccurate, and that the doctrine of continuing course of conduct was better suited to claims where the situation kept evolving after the act complained of was complete, such as medical malpractice, rather than one where the situation could not change, such as legal malpractice arising from negligent drafting. The court concluded that when the state constitution was adopted, there was a common law right to sue for legal malpractice and a six-year statutory limitation on the assertion of the right, but determined that the legislature had not tampered with the cause of action but merely amended the procedural aspect of enforcing the right, and that § 52-577 as applied to the client was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment to the attorney.

 

1004 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Edwards


(13223)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


39 Conn. App. 242; 665 A.2d 611; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 411


June 6, 1995, Argued  
September 12, 1995, decision released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Edwards, 235 Conn. 924, 666 A.2d 1186, 1995 Conn. LEXIS 402 (1995)
Appeal denied by State v. Edwards, 235 Conn. 925, 666 A.2d 1186, 1995 Conn. LEXIS 403 (1995)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Edwards v. Warden, State Prison, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2128 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 23, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder, conspiracy to commit murder, attempt to commit murder and carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Hartmere, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss the first count of the information, and the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Guess, 39 Conn. App. 224, 665 A.2d 126, 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 412 (1995)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted defendant and a co-defendant of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm. Defendant and the co-defendant shot and killed the victim by firing weapons from behind a bush as two rival drug gangs battled for control of a public housing project in New Haven.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to sever his joint trial, improperly instructed the jury on reasonable doubt, improperly admitted his mug shot into evidence, and improperly denied his motion for judgment of acquittal of the lesser-included offense of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm. Defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to support the conviction. Substitute information had charged defendant and a co-defendant with the crimes of murder, conspiracy to commit murder, attempted murder, and carrying a pistol without a permit. A jury convicted them of the lesser-included offense of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm. The court found no error in the rulings of the trial court with respect to severance, jury instructions, and the evidentiary rulings. However, based on the plain error doctrine, the court sua sponte raised the issue whether manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm was a lesser-included offense of murder. The court held that it was not and reversed the judgment and remanded the case for entry of judgment of conviction of manslaughter in the first degree.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to render a judgment of conviction of manslaughter in the first degree.

 

1005 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Giordano v. Giordano


(12570)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


39 Conn. App. 183; 664 A.2d 1136; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 403


May 25, 1995, Argued  
September 5, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application for a prejudgment attachment of certain of the defendant's real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Hodgson, J., granted the application, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) that granted plaintiffs' application for a prejudgment attachment of certain of defendant's real property, and for other relief.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought action against defendant, their grandfather, alleging sexual molestation and emotional distress. Plaintiffs also filed an application for a prejudgment remedy requesting that defendant's real property be attached in a certain amount. Plaintiffs submitted affidavits in support of the application for a prejudgment remedy, listing the injuries they allegedly sustained as a result of the defendant's conduct. The trial court granted the application and the court affirmed. The court concluded that the amount of a prejudgment remedy awarded for emotional distress was not necessarily speculative. The court also found that the award in this case was a reasonable estimate of the amount of damages that plaintiffs would recover if they prevailed at trial. Accordingly, the court rejected defendant's claims that his right to due process had been violated. The court also held that the statute of limitations afforded victims of child molestation an increased time period within which to file an action was rationally related to a legitimate state interest and was sufficiently based on reasons related to the accomplishment of that goal to withstand constitutional scrutiny.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision of the trial court that granted plaintiffs' application for a prejudgment attachment of certain of defendant's real property, and for other relief. The court found that the amount of a prejudgment remedy awarded to plaintiffs for emotional distress was not speculative, and that the award was a reasonable estimate of the amount of damages plaintiffs would recover if they prevailed at trial.

 

1006 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pettway


(12386)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


39 Conn. App. 63; 664 A.2d 1125; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 390


May 26, 1995, Argued  
August 29, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree and robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, where the court, Sylvester, J., granted the defendant's motion for acquittal on the charge of conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Sylvester, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment which was entered by the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two (Connecticut), in which he was found guilty of conspiracy to commit robbery and robbery in the first degree. He claimed that identification evidence should have been suppressed, that he was denied a fair trial, that the jury instructions were improper, and that evidence was erroneously excluded.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that defendant and an accomplice approached the victim, who was pumping gas at a service station, told him that they had a gun, and took $ 260 from him. Within twenty minutes of the robbery police had apprehended defendant and the victim made a positive identification. Although the show-up identification was suggestive because defendant was the only suspect, the court found that it was necessary so that the victim could identify his assailants while his memory was still fresh. Considering the victim's opportunity to view defendant, the lighting, timeframe, and the victim's voice recognition of defendant, the court found that the identification was reliable. Although the trial judge made an inappropriate comment about machine gun fire in front of the jury, the court determined that the proceedings were not tainted. The court found that the trial court properly refused to accept evidence about clothes defendant was wearing when he entered the jail because there was no basis to believe that he was wearing the same cloths on the previous day. The court found that the jury instructions adequately stated the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1007 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Bower v. D'Onfro


(12161)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


38 Conn. App. 685; 663 A.2d 1061; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 363


January 12, 1995, Argued  
August 8, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained by the named plaintiff in an automobile accident allegedly caused by the negligence of the defendants, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the matter was withdrawn as to the named defendant; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Gray, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiffs against the defendant Bradley D. Ausmus et al., from which the defendant Bradley Ausmus et al. appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of New Haven (Connecticut), which awarded money damages in favor of plaintiff for injuries sustained in an automobile accident caused by the negligence of defendants.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was injured when she was thrown from the car in which she was a passenger and struck by another car. Plaintiff brought suit against both drivers but settled with the driver of the car in which she was riding. The trial court found that defendants, the driver and the owner of the car that struck plaintiff, were negligent and awarded money damages in favor of plaintiff. Defendants appealed and claimed that the trial court improperly refused to permit testimony and evidence of plaintiff's failure to wear a seat belt on the basis of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-100a(c)(4). Defendants asserted that the statute was unconstitutional. The court held that defendants did not meet their burden of proving that the statute was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt and upheld the statute as constitutional. Defendants also contended that the trial court erred in awarding prejudgment interest under the offer of judgment statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a. The court agreed because it found that plaintiff was not entitled to interest because the judgment did not meet the requirements of § 52-192a. The court reversed the judgment in part and remanded the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in part and remanded the case with direction to render a judgment without any prejudgment interest because it found that the trial court erred in awarding prejudgment interest. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment.

 

1008 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sherman


(13649)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


38 Conn. App. 371; 662 A.2d 767; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 327


October 25, 1994, Argued  
July 11, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Leuba, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his judgment of conviction in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut) for murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that prosecutorial misconduct deprived him of his constitutional right to a fair trial and that the trial court improperly admitted into evidence the State's expert opinion testimony and excluded from evidence the opinion of defendant's expert as to time of death. The court affirmed, finding that the challenged conduct of the prosecution either was not improper or, if inappropriate, did not so infect the trial with unfairness as to make the resulting conviction a denial of due process. The court reached the same conclusion after considering the instances of alleged impropriety cumulatively. In the context of the lengthy trial, the aggregate effect of the State's misconduct could not be said to have undermined the fairness of or have affected the outcome of the trial. Because the jury was in a position to weigh the probative value of the testimony without abandoning common sense and sacrificing independent judgment, the court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the expert testimony of the State into evidence. The trial court also did not abuse its discretion in excluding the opinion of defendant's expert as to time of death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1009 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Robinson


(11350)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


38 Conn. App. 598; 662 A.2d 1295; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 361


January 11, 1995, Argued  
June 29, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number seven, and tried to the jury before Dunnell, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction rendered by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven, geographical area number seven (Connecticut), after a jury found him guilty on two counts of second degree assault, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-60. Defendant claimed that he was denied a fair trial and argued that the State's use of two peremptory challenges during voir dire violated his right to equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Although defendant was shackled during his trial, the court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by ordering the security measures and causing defendant to be restrained because defendant had a history of violent behavior and had directed this behavior toward the court and sheriffs. The trial court attempted to conceal the restraints from the sight of the jury. Defendant asserted that the second and 38th veniremember were dismissed such that equal protection was violated. Defendant did not object until the peremptory dismissal of the 38th veniremember. The trial court found that the State had a valid reason for challenging this veniremember and ruled that defendant's objection to the second veniremember was not timely. The court recognized that purposeful discrimination which would form the basis of a Batson challenge might not become apparent until several veniremembers had been questioned and a pattern emerged, therefore, the court found that defendant could preserve his right to a Batson hearing by alerting the trial court and the state when a member of a cognizable group was challenged.


OUTCOME: The court remanded for a determination as to whether defendant waived his right to a Batson hearing under the standard articulated in this case. The court directed the trial court to hold a Baton hearing on the juror in question if it determined that defendant preserved his right.

 

1010 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


FEDERAL DEPOSIT INS. CO. v. VOLL


(13863)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


38 Conn. App. 198; 660 A.2d 358; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 286


April 27, 1995, Argued  
June 13, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mortgage on certain real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Hauser, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for judgment of strict foreclosure and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court Pittman, J., granted, in part, the plaintiff's motion for a deficiency judgment and rendered judgment against the defendant Zoltan Guttman, from which the defendant Zoltan Guttman appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mortgagor appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) in a foreclosure action wherein a deficiency judgment was rendered against him and in favor of plaintiff mortgagee. He argued that that the State's deficiency judgment statute violated the State constitution's guarantee of trial by jury. He also argued that the mortgagee's action was barred by laches.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagor and another individual executed a mortgage deed to a bank on property they owned. They defaulted on their obligations to make payments on the promissory note that was secured by the mortgage. The bank commenced a foreclosure action but was declared insolvent. The Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation (FDIC), the mortgagee, was appointed receiver and conveyed the bank's assets to a bridge bank, which pursued the foreclosure. It demanded that the mortgagor and other defendants disclose any defenses, which they did not do. Various delays occurred in the proceedings. The FDIC eventually moved for a judgment of strict foreclosure. No defendant opposed the motion or raised any defenses. Judgment of foreclosure was entered and the FDIC's motion for a deficiency judgment was granted. The mortgagor appealed the deficiency judgment. The court ruled that a deficiency hearing was part of an equitable proceeding and, as such, did not entitle the mortgagor to a jury trial. It was not an independent action on a debt. Many of the delays in the proceedings resulted from defendants' conduct but many were unavoidable. The mortgagor did not raise the defense of laches until his appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1011 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Zaleta v. Town of Fairfield


(13419)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


38 Conn. App. 1; 658 A.2d 166; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 257


February 6, 1995, Argued  
May 23, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the defendant from the decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the fourth district awarding disability benefits to the plaintiff, brought to the workers' compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; decision directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer sought review of the judgment of the Workers' Compensation Review Board, which affirmed the Workers' Compensation Commissioner for the Fourth District (Connecticut), which awarded disability benefits to plaintiff employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee was hired as a firefighter after passing a physical examination in which no evidence of heart disease or hypertension was revealed. Subsequently, the employee was diagnosed as hypertensive and treated with medication. A formal hearing was held before the Commissioner, who found in favor of the employee. The Commissioner found that the employee's claim was timely because hypertension was an occupational disease and thus governed by the three year statute for filing that type of claim. The Board affirmed the decision of the Commissioner. On appeal, the employer claimed that the Board improperly determined that the employee's hypertension was an occupational disease and, therefore, subject to the three year statute of limitations provided in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-294c. On review, the court reversed the decision of the Board. The employee produced no evidence to establish that hypertension was an occupational disease entitling him to the benefit of the three year statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Board and the case was remanded with direction to sustain the employer's appeal.

 

1012 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Feliciano v. Feliciano


(12933)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


37 Conn. App. 856; 658 A.2d 141; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 248


December 5, 1994, Argued  
May 16, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and referred to Hon. Simon S. Cohen, state trial referee; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief; thereafter, the defendant's motion for modification of child support was referred to Alan E. Steele, family support magistrate, who granted the motion; subsequently, the court, Santos, J., approved the magistrate's decision without a hearing, and the state appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the State of Connecticut, appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford, New Britain (Connecticut), which approved an order of a magistrate that modified a support order by increasing the amount of child support that defendant father was obligated to pay to plaintiff mother based on a pro rata share of the benefits received under the Federal Aid to Families with Dependent Children (AFDC) program.


OVERVIEW: The magistrate granted the State's motion to modify the parties' support order, but limited the support to a pro rata share of the AFDC benefits received on the basis that to require the father to pay support not only for his own child, but also for the mother's other two children would violate his constitutional right to due process and equal protection under U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV. The trial court affirmed, but the court reversed. The trial court's failure to adhere to the Child Support and Arrearage Guidelines because of the child's receipt of AFDC benefits was an abuse of discretion. The guidelines expressly provided that public assistance grants were not to be included in the calculation of child support. The father's due process and equal protection rights were not violated by requiring him to pay more than his child's pro rata share of AFDC benefits because the AFDC program had been amended to require that a family applying for benefits include a child who was receiving support payments. The court declined to address the argument that the father was denied his rights under Conn. Const. art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which limited the father's obligation to pay child support to a pro rata share of the family's AFDC benefits, and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1013 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Webb


(12946)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


37 Conn. App. 722; 657 A.2d 711; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 220


February 21, 1995, Argued  
May 2, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex and tried to the jury before Clifford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut), that convicted him of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm. The crime was defined by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55a. On appeal, defendant contended, inter alia, that the trial court improperly instructed the jury on the law of self-defense.


OVERVIEW: The court found that defendant's claim of improper jury instruction was based on an allegation that the trial court had used a wholly objective standard of self-defense. A subjective and objective analysis was required. The jury had to decide whether or not defendant believed that an attack was imminent, and, then, it had to decide whether or not that belief was reasonable. The court found that the issue was not preserved below for appellate review; thus, for review, the issue had to meet four case-law criteria one of which was that the alleged constitutional violation clearly exist and clearly deprive defendant of a fair trial. Per the court, the trial court's instructions in toto properly included the subjective and objective aspects of the law on self-defense, and, ergo, the third criterion for review was not met as the alleged violation did not clearly exist. On a separate issue, the court rejected the claim that defendant's prior convictions for larceny and conspiracy to commit robbery and assault should not have been admitted as impeachment evidence albeit at least one prior conviction was more than 10-years old, and Connecticut courts usually followed Fed. R. Evid. 609(b).


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1014 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rodriguez


(11449)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


37 Conn. App. 589; 658 A.2d 98; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 201


January 18, 1995, Argued  
April 25, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and larceny in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Hartmere, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of robbery in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut) that upon a jury verdict convicted him of robbery in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(2)


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery. On appeal, the court affirmed his conviction. The court held that defendant was entitled to object to racially based exclusions of jurors through peremptory challenges, even though he and the rejected juror were not of the same race. However, the juror's negative encounters with police constituted a neutral ground that rebutted the inference of discrimination. Moreover, the State reconsidered the challenge and would have changed its course of conduct, but the rejected juror was no longer available. Defendant was properly denied access to police internal affairs files because he failed to show that the files might have contained any material relevant to the case or useful for impeachment purposes. The State's line of questioning regarding fingerprint cards did not warrant a mistrial because a curative instruction was given and there the one card admitted into evidence was relevant to the issue of identity. The "hesitate to act" formulation used in a jury instruction as to the definition of proof beyond a reasonable doubt did not violate defendant's right to due process of law because it did not decrease the state's burden.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1015 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burgos


(13628)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


37 Conn. App. 404; 656 A.2d 238; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 173


December 5, 1994, Argued  
April 4, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was intoxicated at the time he killed the victim. He contended that the trial court erred by improperly instructing jurors on the concurrence principle, the effect of intoxication intent, and on the defense of extreme emotional disturbance. The trial court held that (1) the trial court's instructions, as a whole, informed the jury that it had to find that defendant had the requisite intent for murder at the time he assaulted the victim and they precluded the jury from improperly convicting him on the basis of intent formed after the acts were committed; (2) the trial court's instructions on intoxication did not mislead the jury and properly informed them that voluntary intoxication was significant only when it went so far as to have affected defendant's mind and made him incapable of forming a rational intent or of controlling his will; and (3) defendant's contention as to the trial court's instructions on the defense of extreme emotional disturbance were not properly preserved and did not warrant extraordinary review because improper jury instructions on that defense were not constitutional in nature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1016 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Merdinger


(11082)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


37 Conn. App. 379; 655 A.2d 1167; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 161


November 8, 1994, Argued  
March 28, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with eight counts of the crime of failure to pay wages, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Norwalk and tried to the jury before Hickey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Norwalk (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of eight counts of the crime of failure to pay wages.


OVERVIEW: An employee did not receive a weekly paycheck and after she ceased working for the restaurant she attempted to collect her past due wages on several occasions without success. There were occasions when defendant was present when the employee asked for her back wages. On appeal, the court held that the statutory requirements for regular payment of wages within a prescribed period were clear and unambiguous, and the jury reasonably could have found that defendant had notice as a field supervisor for the wage regulation division of the department of labor personally hand delivered a copy of § 31-71b to defendant. The court held that the statute properly did not require a mens rea and imposed strict criminal liability and that defendant benefited from the labors of the employees of the restaurant and should reasonably have been expected to conform to the wage payment laws. The court held that the jury was entitled to find that defendant was the employee's employer on the basis of his status as president and sole stockholder of the corporation over a 22-year period.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1017 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. George


(12119)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


37 Conn. App. 388; 656 A.2d 232; 1995 Conn. App. LEXIS 162


November 30, 1994, Argued  
March 28, 1995, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number twelve, and tried to the jury before Barry, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of risk of injury to a child, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, following a jury trial for risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53:21, from a judgment of the Superior Court (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: Defendant had left his 17-month-old child unattended in a vehicle in a parking lot. The police warned him against such conduct. Later that same day, defendant left the child alone in his apartment while he went out to a bar. Defendant was convicted under that portion of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21, which criminalized conduct that reflected a deliberate indifference to, acquiescence in, or the creation of situations inimical to a minor's moral or physical welfare constituted criminal liability. Defendant challenged his conviction for causing risk of injury to a child on grounds the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court disagreed and affirmed the conviction. The court held that the creation of a prohibited situation was sufficient to trigger criminal liability. Even if the statute failed to provide definite notice as to the prohibited conduct, fair warning or other notice that such acts were prohibited would serve to surmount a vagueness challenge. The court found that defendant clearly had fair warning that law proscribed his conduct. Police told him earlier that same day that leaving a child unattended could result in his arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

The court further held that defendant did not properly preserve for review his claim that the trial court improperly precluded him from presenting evidence of the witness' bias because he failed to take an exception at trial. State v. Carswell


(12688)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


36 Conn. App. 336; 650 A.2d 924; 1994 Conn. App. LEXIS 425


September 30, 1994, Argued  
December 13, 1994, decision released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit murder and assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the jury before Nigro, J.; verdict of guilty of attempt to commit murder; thereafter, the court dismissed the charge of assault in the first degree and rendered judgment of guilty of attempted murder, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) of attempt to commit murder and assault in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal attempt to commit murder and assault in the first degree. Fix to six minutes after defendant shot the victim, the victim informed police of defendant's build, his apparel, hairstyle and hair color, and his name. While recuperating in the hospital, the victim selected defendant's photograph from a police array, and later identified defendant as his assailant at trial. Defendant filed a motion to suppress the out of court identification, which the trial court denied. Defendant was convicted and appealed. The court held that the photographic array compiled by officers was neither unduly suggestive nor did it violate his right to due process. The court held that because all photographs in the array were obtained from the same source, and arranged such that all photographs were visible at one time, the array provided for a fair identification. In affirming the conviction, the court held that defendant failed to meet his burden to demonstrate that the identification resulted from the use of a procedure that violated his rights under the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) reserved three questions for the court's review relating to the interpretation and constitutionality of Public Acts 1993, No. 93-77 (P.A. 93-77), which amended Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 38a-290 and 38a-336.

Dutch Point Credit Union v. Caron Auto Works


12322


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


36 Conn. App. 123; 648 A.2d 882; 1994 Conn. App. LEXIS 354


April 29, 1994, Argued  
September 27, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a judgment declaring unconstitutional the statute allowing the sale of abandoned motor vehicles without providing actual notice to lienholders of record, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Allen, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lienholder filed a declaratory judgment action against defendants, a car repair and storage facility and the commissioner of motor vehicles, seeking declaration that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-150 was unconstitutional. The lienholder, who also sought damages from the car repair facility, appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) in favor of defendants.


OVERVIEW: The lienholder was the first lienholder of record on an automobile that was involved in an accident and towed to the car repair and storage facility at the request of the police. The car was estimated to have a value of $ 300 after the accident and, after the owner abandoned it, it was repaired and sold, pursuant to § 14-150, for approximately $ 2800, thereby extinguishing the lienholder's interest. The court found that § 14-150 was unconstitutional because it denied the lienholder due process of law. Pursuant to the statute, vehicles with a value of $ 500 or less could be sold by garage owners who stored such vehicles and were not paid, so long as the garage owner notified the owner of the vehicle, if known, advertises the sale in a local newspaper three times. The court ruled that notice by publication was insufficient to apprise the lienholder of his rights in such a situation. However, the car repair and storage facility did not have to pay the lienholder damages because the court determined that there was no evidence indicating that it had acted unreasonably or in bad faith when it sold the vehicle according to the provisions set forth in § 14-150.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed in part and remanded with directions to declare the statute at issue unconstitutional.

Miller v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


12575


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


36 Conn. App. 98; 647 A.2d 1050; 1994 Conn. App. LEXIS 352


March 31, 1994, Argued  
September 20, 1994, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Miller v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals of Westport, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1229 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 15, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the defendant denying the plaintiff's application for a variance on certain of his real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, and tried to the court, Ryan, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Miller v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals, 1993 Conn. Super. LEXIS 557 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 5, 1993)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged a decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which dismissed his appeal from a decision by defendant, a town zoning board of appeals, that denied his application for a variance on his parcel of real estate.


OVERVIEW: The property owner purchased two adjacent residential lots, and later sold one lot. He attempted to sell the second lot, and the potential buyer was informed that the lot did not comply with Westport, Conn. Zoning Regulations § 12-3 because it could not accommodate a 150-foot square within the lot. It could only accommodate a square of 144.47 feet. The owner sought a variance, which the board denied because any hardship was self-created by the owner. The trial court affirmed the finding that the hardship was self-created and also found that the merger doctrine, found in Westport, Conn. Zoning Regulations § 6-3.2, applied to the two lots. The trial court held that the lot had merged with the lot previously sold by the owner. On appeal, the court held that the properties had never merged. In order for the merger provision to take effect the result of the combined lots must have more nearly permitted the 150-foot square within the lot. The trial court created an uneven 150-foot hexagon rather than a square, and there was no proof that the combination of the lots would have accommodated a square larger than 144.47 feet, the size of the square that the single lot could accommodate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case with the direction that it be remanded to the town's zoning board of appeals for a determination of whether the property owner's lot warranted a variance.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgments of conviction entered by the Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which were rendered following his Alford plea to arson in the first degree, burglary in the third degree, and larceny in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his convictions for arson, burglary, and larceny. Defendant alleged that his guilty plea should not have been accepted by the trial court and he was improperly convicted of arson. The court found that the record supported a finding that defendant made a knowing and voluntary guilty plea. The court then turned to defendant's assertion that the arson statute did not apply to abandoned buildings. The court noted that arson in the first degree required that a person with intent to destroy or damage a building, as defined in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-100, start a fire, or cause an explosion. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-111. The court further noted that Conn. Gen. Stat § 53a-100 defined building to include anything within the "ordinary meaning" of that word, as well as anything specifically enumerated in the statute or any other structures. The court found that it was clear that an abandoned or unoccupied building was still a building under the arson statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court convicting defendant pursuant to his plea.

October Twenty-Four, Inc. v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n


12655


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


35 Conn. App. 599; 646 A.2d 926; 1994 Conn. App. LEXIS 319


April 25, 1994, Argued  
August 23, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the named defendant granting an application filed by the defendant Tomasso Brothers, Inc., for site plan approval for the construction of an office complex, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain and tried to the court, Berger, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff adjoining property owner to development (property owner) appealed the decision of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain (Connecticut), which granted defendant developer's motion to dismiss the property owner's appeal of the decision of defendant town planning and zoning commission's (commission) approval for the developer's site plan application for an office park.


OVERVIEW: The developer had sought approval for an office park in the technical park zone. The developer contended that because the commission failed to render a decision within 65 days of the receipt of the application, the site plan was approved by operation of law. The court affirmed, finding that under the town's zoning regulations the site plan application in the technical park zone did not require a public hearing and that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-7d(b) applied. All decisions had to be made within 65 days of the application date. Although the commission decided to hold a public hearing, the time limit under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-7d(a) did not apply because a public hearing was not required. Section 8-7d(a) made no reference to situations where public hearings were not required but were held at the discretion of the commission. Attendance at commission meetings after the automatic approval date was not a waiver or estoppel because the developer never consented to an extension of time, nor did it intentionally relinquish its right to automatic approval by attending the meetings. The court held that § 8-7d)(b) was not unconstitutional because there was no automatic right of appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the developer in the property owner's action that challenged the commission's approval of the developer's site plan application for an office park.

Aetna Life & Casualty Co. v. Braccidiferro


11058


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


34 Conn. App. 833; 643 A.2d 1305; 1994 Conn. App. LEXIS 240


November 3, 1993, Argued  
June 28, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application to vacate an arbitration award, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the defendant filed a motion to confirm the award; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, DeMayo, J.; judgment denying the application to vacate and granting the motion to confirm, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurance company appealed the judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted defendant insured's motion to confirm and denied the insurance company's application to vacate an arbitration award in favor of the insured. The arbitration panel rejected the insurance company's claim that the insured's underinsured motorist claim was barred by a two year limitation under the policy.


OVERVIEW: On April 1, 1986, the insured was injured in an automobile accident. On April 25, 1989, the other driver's insurer agreed to pay the insured the driver's policy's full liability limits. On May 5, 1989, the insured submitted a written claim for underinsured motorist benefits to her insurance company, which disclaimed liability because the claim was not presented within two years of the accident, as required by the terms of the insured's policy. The court held that the 1993 Conn. Acts 93-77, which increased the minimum period for filing a claim for underinsured motorist benefits from two to three years, applied, that a question of fact remained as to whether that time period was tolled, and that the Act was not unconstitutional. The court determined that the Act did not violate Conn. Const. art. I, § 1 or the Contracts Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, and that, even though it applied retroactively, it did not deprive the insurance company of due process of law because it did not create a substantive right of action. The court remanded the case for a determination of whether the three-year period was tolled, with directions to affirm if it was tolled and reverse if it was not.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for a determination of whether the minimum three-year period for claiming underinsured motorist benefits was tolled pursuant to the provisions of the Act. If the trial court found that the three- year period was tolled, the judgment was affirmed. In the event the trial court found that the time period was not tolled, the judgment was reversed and the cause remanded with directions to grant the application to vacate.

Herzig v. Horrigan


12450


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


34 Conn. App. 816; 644 A.2d 360; 1994 Conn. App. LEXIS 236


May 2, 1994, Argued  
June 3, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the alleged breach of a lease agreement, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain, where the court, Berger, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court, granted the plaintiff's motion to garnish certain of the defendant's personal property; subsequently, the court, Holzberg, J., granted the motions filed by the named defendant and the state of Connecticut, the third party garnishee, to dissolve the garnishment, and the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After plaintiff lessor was granted a judgment in his action against defendant tenant for breach of the parties' lease and after the lessor's motion to garnish the tenant's lottery winnings was granted, defendant, the State of Connecticut, and the tenant filed motions to dissolve the garnishment. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain (Connecticut) granted the motions. The lessor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The lessor obtained a summary judgment in a certain amount against the tenant for his failure to pay rent. According to the lessor, the only asset of the tenant amenable to execution was the tenant's lottery prize, which was payable in 20 annual installments. The lessor attempted to garnish those payments by serving a property execution on several State officers, each of whom refused to honor the execution. In affirming the judgment that granted the State's motion to dissolve the garnishment, the court ruled that the doctrine of sovereign immunity prevented the lessor from garnishing the lottery winnings of the tenant while they were in the possession of the State. Noting that Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-350e and 52-350f did not explicitly permit a property execution pursuant to a money judgment to be served on the State or enforced against property of the judgment debtor in possession of the state and that the construction of a statute in derogation of the doctrine of sovereign immunity had to be strict, the court ruled that when, as here, the statute was silent as to the abrogation of the doctrine, sovereign immunity was not abrogated and the lessor's garnishment was barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

 

1033 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Defrancesco


12700


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


34 Conn. App. 741; 643 A.2d 271; 1994 Conn. App. LEXIS 233


April 5, 1994, Argued  
June 1, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with three counts of illegal possession of a dangerous animal, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, geographical area number five, and tried to the court, Gormley, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut) that convicted defendant of three counts of illegal possession of a dangerous animal in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 26-40a.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant asserted that the trial court improperly rendered the judgment of conviction because the possession of a Bengal cat, jungle cat, and hybrid bobcat was not specifically prohibited by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 26-40a, and, in the alternative, the statute was void for vagueness. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 26-55 stated that an animal that resulted from the crossbreeding of any species was considered the wild animal of that species and could not be possessed. Because the crossbreed of a bobcat and a domestic cat was a hybrid bobcat, defendant's possession of the hybrid bobcat was prohibited by the statute. The court stated that the statute gave defendant fair warning that the statute prohibited such possession. Because the statute specifically prohibited bobcats, a person of ordinary intelligence had a reasonable opportunity to know that the possession of a hybrid bobcat was prohibited. However, the court found the statute was unconstitutionally vague as applied to the jungle cat and the Bengal cat.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction pertaining to the jungle cat and the Bengal cat was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to render judgment of not guilty as to each of those counts. The judgment of conviction relating to the hybrid bobcat was affirmed.

State v. Cavell


10605


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


34 Conn. App. 276; 641 A.2d 426; 1994 Conn. App. LEXIS 151


November 8, 1993, Argued  
May 10, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and with the crime of kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to a jury before Spada, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of sexual assault in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which, following a jury trial, convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-70a.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raped the victim in his car. At trial, defendant objected to the State's introduction as rebuttal evidence of the existence of semen stains on the seat. The court affirmed defendant's conviction because the fact of intercourse had not been disputed, so that the evidence was not relevant until defendant disputed the victim's testimony as to where the assault occurred. Furthermore, the trial court did not err in denying defendant the right to develop expert surrebuttal testimony because defendant had not been unduly surprised by the testimony and had not suggested a definite period of continuance to obtain the evidence. The trial court's exclusion of a defense expert witness because of a violation of a sequestration order did not prejudice defendant because defendant was able to obtain another expert who testified in the same manner that the first expert would have testified and defendant had no right to have any particular expert testify. Finally, the court held that it was not plain error for the trial court to instruct the jury that evidence of a specific trait of nonviolence was not itself sufficient to raise reasonable doubt of guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of sexual assault in the first degree.

 

1035 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Fischel v. Tkpk, Ltd.


12176


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


34 Conn. App. 22; 640 A.2d 125; 1994 Conn. App. LEXIS 108


January 12, 1994, Argued  
April 5, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the alleged breach of a lease agreement, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, Housing Session at Bridgeport, where the court, Melville, J., granted the plaintiffs' application for an attachment on certain real property owned by the defendant Michelle C. Minogue, and on certain personal property owned by the defendant Thomas Minogue, and the defendant Michelle C. Minogue et al. appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant guarantors sought review of judgment of the Superior Court at Fairfield (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff landlords' application for the prejudgment remedy (PJR) of attachment on certain real property owned by the guarantors.


OVERVIEW: The landlords entered into a commercial real estate lease with defendant tenant. Payment and performance of the lease was guaranteed by the guarantors. When the tenants defaulted and abandoned the leased premises, the landlords demanded payment from the guarantors. The guarantors refused and the landlords filed an application for PJR. The trial court granted the application for attachment. The guarantors appealed. The court noted that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-278d(a) provided that a trial court could issue a PJR if it determined that there was probable cause to sustain the validity of a plaintiff's claim, and that a trial court's role was to determine probable success by weighing probabilities. The court stated that its role in reviewing a finding of probable cause was equally limited to a determination whether the trial court's conclusion was reasonable. The court concluded that there was a reasonable probability that the landlords would be able to prove the validity of the transaction at trial, consequently there was probable validity of the claim and that nothing more was required of a plaintiff to prevail in an application for PJR.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment granting the landlords' application for the prejudgment remedy of attachment with respect to property of the guarantors who guaranteed the payment and performance of a commercial lease executed by defendant tenant.

State v. Grant


11630


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


33 Conn. App. 647; 637 A.2d 1116; 1994 Conn. App. LEXIS 63


November 29, 1993, Argued  
March 1, 1994, Decision Released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sale of cocaine by a person who is not drug-dependent and conspiracy to sell cocaine, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and tried to the jury before Hartmere, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of conspiracy to sell cocaine, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut), which, upon a jury's verdict, convicted defendant of conspiracy to sell cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of conspiracy to sell cocaine based upon an undercover narcotics operation. Defendant sought to impeach on of the prosecution's' chief witness with drug treatment records. The trial court denied him access to those records. Additionally, the trial court did not conduct an in camera inspection of the records. Defendant argued that the trial court denied him his right of confrontation by denying him the access to the requested records. The court agreed and held that the trial court should have conducted a hearing to determine whether the treatment records affected the witness' testimonial capacities. However, the court found that the error was harmless because the witness' testimony was mere cumulative given the numerous charges and other evidence against defendant. Defendant's remaining argument that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress an inculpatory statement made to the police was overruled because he had failed to prove that the statement was involuntarily made.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of conspiracy to sell cocaine, was affirmed.

State v. Turner


11190


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


33 Conn. App. 616; 637 A.2d 3; 1994 Conn. App. LEXIS 58


December 13, 1993, Argued  
February 15, 1994, Decision Released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of assault of a victim sixty years of age or older in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before Melville, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut) for assault on a victim aged 60 or older in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-60b.


OVERVIEW: The jury reasonably could have found that the victim was sitting in a metal folding chair on the sidewalk in front of his son's house when defendant walked toward him. Defendant had been fired from his job for hitting the victim at their job. When defendant approached, the victim folded his chair and swung it at him. Defendant punched the victim in the face, knocking him down, then kicked him twice, causing serious injuries. Reversing, the court held that the trial court erred in its instruction to the jury on self-defense. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-19(c)(1), the "provocation exception" to the general rule of self-defense, the prosecutor was required to prove dual intent on the part of defendant: (1) the intent to cause physical injury or death; and (2) the intent to provoke. In this case, the trial court told the jury that defendant's use of force would be unjustified if he intentionally provoked the victim. That statement satisfied the second element of the provocation exception, intent to provoke, but not the first, that defendant intended to cause the victim injury or death when he provoked him.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the case.

State v. Reis


11572

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of criminal possession of a pistol or revolver, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arguing and wrestling with the victim when he shot the victim in the foot. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for criminal possession of a pistol or revolver. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion or unconstitutionally restrict defendant's right of cross-examination in excluding evidence of the dollar amount of the civil action filed against him by the victim. The court held that the trial court properly refused to directly grant defendant's witness immunity without authority to do so. The court found no abuse of discretion in the exclusion of an unavailable witness's uncorroborated declaration against penal interest, which was untrustworthy because it was given a significant time after the shooting and was made in response to questioning by an investigator with whom the witness did not share a close relationship. The court did not reach the issue of whether Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217(b) mandated a two-year non-suspendable sentence because the sentencing comments showed that the trial court believed the term of incarceration was justified by the facts, including defendant's prior convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Writ of habeas corpus denied Simpkins v. United States Postal Serv., 185 F.3d 881, 1999 U.S. App. LEXIS 2831 (Fed. Cir., 1999)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Correia v. Rowland, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2916 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 10, 2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Correia v. Warden, State Prison, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2923 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 16, 2011)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Correia, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2583 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 25, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree and with the the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before O'Keefe, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of the first-degree crimes of kidnapping, robbery, and sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant used a gun to force his way into the victim's car. Defendant locked a passenger in the trunk, took the victim's money, and ordered her to drive to a field where he raped her. The victim identified defendant from a photographic array. The court affirmed defendant's convictions for kidnapping, robbery, and sexual assault in the first degree. The court held that, absent a limiting instruction, the trial court was not required to instruct the jury to take, as true, a prior inconsistent statement given by the victim on the night of the attack. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to admit the statement, which the victim admitted to giving, as a full exhibit because further evidence of the inconsistency was cumulative. The court concluded that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to waive his presence at trial because he did not request a less suggestive in-court identification procedure. The court held that defendant was not entitled to a mistrial because the State's comment that he was trying to twist the evidence was not one that the jury would have interpreted as a comment on his failure to testify.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Sailor


11681


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


33 Conn. App. 409; 635 A.2d 1237; 1994 Conn. App. LEXIS 16


November 8, 1993, Argued  
January 11, 1994, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and conspiracy to distribute narcotics, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district Of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Miano, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who pled nolo contendere to the charge of possession of narcotics with the intent to sell and conspiracy to distribute narcotics after the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) denied the motion to suppress, sought review of the conviction and the denial of the motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress the evidence of the drugs seized by the police during a warrantless search of his automobile. Defendant argued the police lacked probable cause for the search. In the court's view of the case, the court did not reach the issue of whether the search was supported by probable cause because the contraband seized was in plain view prior to the seizure. The police were engaged in lawful behavior when they engaged in surveillance of the area. Additionally, the police never stopped or detained defendant's car prior to viewing the plastic bag which contained the narcotics. The police officers had the right to be on the public street, stand beside defendant's car and peer into the car. Because the police had probable cause to believe that the evidence seized had a reasonable relationship to the criminal behavior under investigation, the trial court properly denied the motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which denied defendant's motion to suppress, was affirmed. Defendant's conviction was also affirmed.

State v. Reddick


10500


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


33 Conn. App. 311; 635 A.2d 848; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 483


September 20, 1993 Argued  
December 28, 1993, Decision Released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him for robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for first degree robbery in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4). The court affirmed his conviction. The trial court properly permitted the state's key witness to make an in-court identification. The witness stated that she could not identify the perpetrator at trial. The state showed her photographs from which the witness had previously identified defendant. Thereafter, defendant approached the witness and she identified him as the perpetrator. Such a procedure was within the trial court's discretion. The procedure for in-court identifications was not of constitutional magnitude. The trial court did not err by failing to order the state to produce the transcript of testimony given by a witness from a previous trial, as the statement was not subject to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 752 because the state did not possess the transcript. "Possession by the state" did not extend to the entire state as a whole to include a court reporter's transcript. The evidence sufficiently supported the jury's conclusion that defendant participated in the crime Such a determination was a question for the jury, which was in the position to judge the witness's credibility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's first degree robbery conviction.

State v. Sawyer


No. 9728


Appellate Court of Connecticut


32 Conn. App. 854; 632 A.2d 372; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 418


October 6, 1993, Submitted  
October 12, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Byrne, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court, which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, from which the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Supreme Court, which reversed the judgment of this court and remanded the case for further proceedings.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with the crime of murder in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut). The jury returned a verdict of guilty of the lesser-included offense of manslaughter in the first degree. Defendant appealed. The court originally reversed the trial court's judgment; the State appealed to the Supreme Court of Connecticut, which reversed the judgment of the court and remanded the case for further proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The only issue for the court's decision was the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(3), which defined manslaughter in the first degree as, with an extreme indifference to human life, recklessly engaging in conduct creating a grave risk of death to another. Defendant contended that this offense was indistinguishable from Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-56(a)(1), defining manslaughter in the second degree as recklessly causing the death of another. Affirming the conviction, the court held that defendant's failure to raise the constitutionality of § 53a-55(a)(3) at trial, or to object to the instruction given, left the record inadequate for a fair consideration of whether the statute was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him, precluding review. Defendant acknowledged that the essential elements of each lesser included offense were properly charged. His failure to object to the instructions at trial undercut his claim that they clearly deprived him of a fundamental constitutional right and a fair trial. The court found that the claim was not sufficiently egregious to be reviewable as plain error under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 4185.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for manslaughter in the first degree.
