State v. Brokaw


No. 11114


Appellate Court of Connecticut


32 Conn. App. 505; 629 A.2d 1170; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 377


January 12, 1993, Argued  
August 17, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of cocaine with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and possession of cocaine, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number seven, where the court, Stengel, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of possession of cocaine with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which denied defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence and convicted defendant of possession of cocaine with intent to sell by a person who was not drug-dependent.


OVERVIEW: An informant told a detective that defendant would be at a bar at a specific time with possession of cocaine for sale and that a truck belonging to defendant's son would be outside. The informant also stated that he had purchased cocaine from defendant in the bar on a regular basis, most recently within the prior two weeks. When defendant noticed the three officers approaching him, he turned to his left to evade them and pulled from his pocket a clear plastic bag containing what appeared to be narcotics. The police officers arrested defendant and retrieved the plastic bag from a trash can, which proved to contain cocaine. On appeal, the court held that defendant was not seized in violation of his constitutional rights because the approach of three unidentified people did not create an unconstitutional seizure. The court held that the prosecutor's challenged conduct, while of questionable propriety, was not so prejudicial as to taint the entire proceeding and deprive defendant of a fair trial. The court held that an officer's testimony that he had previously encountered defendant in a municipal building did not amount to evidence of defendant's prior arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Tucker v. Pace Invs. Assocs.


No. 11303


Appellate Court of Connecticut


32 Conn. App. 384; 629 A.2d 470; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 365


June 2, 1993, Argued  
August 10, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of Practice Book §§ 504 through 510, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Corrigan, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss the first count of the complaint, and the plaintiff appealed to this court, which dismissed the appeal; thereafter, the plaintiff filed a substitute complaint alleging, inter alia, abuse of process; subsequently, the court, Wagner, J., granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgagee challenged the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted the motion for summary judgment of defendants, a bank, the bank's attorney, the bank's grantee, and a mortgagor, and entered judgment dismissing plaintiff's substitute complaint alleging abuse of process and civil rights violations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a substitute complaint against defendants, alleging violations of § 1983. The trial court dismissed plaintiff's § 1983 claims for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Plaintiff filed another substitute complaint alleging abuse of process. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment based on the statute of limitations and res judicata. The trial court granted defendants summary judgment on the ground that plaintiff's action was barred by a three-year statute of limitations. Plaintiff challenged the dismissal of his § 1983 claims and the grant of summary judgment. The court concluded that a higher court's disposition of plaintiff's due process claims in an earlier proceeding served as an absolute bar to plaintiff's § 1983 claims. The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to defendants on the abuse of process claim on the ground of res judicata. The facts underlying an earlier proceeding concerning appointment of rent receivers, which was resolved adversely to plaintiff, were related to the abuse of process claim in time, space, origin, or motivation, and the abuse of process claim could have been made in the earlier case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which granted defendants' motion for summary judgment and entered judgment dismissing plaintiff's substitute complaint.

 

1046 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Linares


No. 10910


Appellate Court of Connecticut


32 Conn. App. 656; 630 A.2d 1340; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 389


October 28, 1992, Argued  
July 23, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of interfering with the General Assembly, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Clifford, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Parker, J., on a plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of interfering with the Connecticut General Assembly, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2-1d(a)(2)(C) and § 2-1d(a)(2)(E). The conviction resulted from a plea of nolo contendere after defendant's motion to dismiss the information was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's arrest occurred after she and others unfurled a banner and shouted "gay rights, lesbian rights" during the governor's state of the state address. Defendant and others were removed from the gallery by the capitol police and later arrested. The chanting and the removal of defendant interrupted the governor's speech for approximately two minutes. The trial court concluded that the gallery, where the incident occurred, was a limited public forum, and that the statute was directed toward behavior, not the content of the expression. Both the state and defendant implicitly agreed that the facts, as given by the state, were sufficient to support defendant's conviction had she been tried, if the statute was constitutional. The court reasoned that if a statute, which implicated the First Amendment, could have been applied to a number of other persons and situations to inhibit free speech, it was facially invalid even if it could have had some legitimate applications. The court concluded that § 2-1d(a)(2)(E) was unconstitutional as overbroad because the proscriptions of subparagraph (E) were unlimited and could not have been made to conform to due process requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for interfering with the Connecticut General Assembly under the first section of the statute. The court reversed defendant's conviction under the latter section of the statute and remanded the case with direction to render judgment resentencing defendant accordingly.

State v. Lee


Nos. 10836, 10837


Appellate Court of Connecticut


32 Conn. App. 84; 628 A.2d 1318; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 337


May 3, 1993, Argued  
July 20, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit assault in the first degree, risk of injury to a child and reckless endangerment in the first degree, and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with possession of cocaine with intent to sell and improper use of a motor vehicle registration, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Schaller, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, in the first case, of risk of injury to a child and reckless endangerment in the first degree, and verdict and judgment of guilty in the second case, from which the defendant filed separate appeals to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Under consolidated informations, the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut) convicted defendant of possession of a narcotic substance with intent to sell (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b)), improper use of a motor vehicle registration (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-147(c)), risk of injury to a child (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21), and reckless endangerment in the first degree (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-63). Defendant filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: Based on a jury's verdict, the trial court convicted defendant of possession of a narcotic substance with intent to sell, improper use of a motor vehicle registration, risk of injury to a child, and reckless endangerment in the first degree. In affirming the trial court's judgment, the court rejected defendant's argument that a search of his car violated his state and federal constitutional rights to be free from unreasonable searches. The court found no merit in defendant's argument that the narcotics found as a result of the search should have been excluded because the state failed to establish that the evidence was in an unchanged condition. The court rejected defendant's argument that the trial court's denial of his request to remove counsel and for a continuance denied him his due process rights. Lastly, the court found no merit in defendant's claim that the trial court improperly consolidated the two informations filed against him and the resulting prejudice was beyond the curative power of the trial court's instructions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1048 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Lutynski v. B.B. & J. Trucking


No. 11300


Appellate Court of Connecticut


31 Conn. App. 806; 628 A.2d 1; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 317


February 22, 1993, Argued  
July 6, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained in a motor vehicle accident as a result of the defendant's alleged negligence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Murray, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiff; thereafter, the court denied the plaintiff's motion for interest and attorney's fees, and the defendant's motion for a reduction of the plaintiff's award by the amount of benefits received through collateral sources, and the plaintiff appealed and the defendant cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which entered judgment for plaintiff in his negligence action against defendant truck owner, but denied his motion for interest and attorney's fees. The truck owner cross-appealed from the denial of his motion to reduce the amount of plaintiff's award by the amount received from collateral sources.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was seriously hurt when a truck belonging to the owner, and being driven by one of the owner's employees, crashed into plaintiff's car. While the trial court entered a judgment in favor of plaintiff in his negligence action against the owner, it denied his motion for prejudgment interest and attorney's fees. The trial court also denied the owner's motion to reduce the amount of plaintiff's award. Both parties appealed, and the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that plaintiff made an offer of judgment that encompassed an offer to settle the entire case, and the owner failed to accept this offer. Because the amount ultimately awarded to plaintiff by the jury exceeded the offer of judgment, the trial court was compelled under the express language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a to award plaintiff interest on the amount of his recovery. However, the owner was not entitled to have the amount of the award reduced by the amounts paid to plaintiff by his insurance providers. The amount paid by plaintiff to secure his medical benefits exceeded the amount he received, and thus the trial court properly refused to reduce the economic damages awarded.


OUTCOME: As to plaintiff's appeal, the court reversed the portion of the judgment denying the motion for interest and otherwise affirmed. As to the owner's cross-appeal, the court affirmed the judgment.

 

1049 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Felsman v. Zoning Comm'n of Bridgeport


No. 11083


Appellate Court of Connecticut


31 Conn. App. 674; 626 A.2d 825; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 284


April 5, 1993, Argued  
June 22, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the defendant denying the plaintiff's application for a special permit for the construction of an apartment building, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Dean, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which, on the granting of certification, the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant zoning commission sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which sustained plaintiff applicant's appeal from the commission's denial of his application for a special exception to permit the construction of a 12-unit apartment building with 30 on-site parking spaces in a residence C zone.


OVERVIEW: The applicant was denied a special exception on the ground that granting the petition would result in an overuse of the property. The trial court sustained his appeal on the merits but also ruled sua sponte that Bridgeport, CT, Zoning Reg. ch. 8, § 2(c) was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment but held that the trial court improperly found that the standards set forth in the zoning regulation did not pass the constitutional test necessitating ascertainable standards. There was nothing in the record to support the zoning commission's stated reason for denying the special exception, overuse of the property. The proposed use was permitted, all of the provisions of the zoning regulations were complied with, and there was more parking provided that was required. The applicant failed to raise the issue of unconstitutional vagueness during the proceedings or to demonstrate that the regulations were vague as applied to the facts. The zoning commission could exercise discretion to determine whether the general standards in the regulation had been met in the special permit process. The trial court improperly held, sua sponte, that the regulation was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment allowing the applicant a special exception.

State v. Battista


No. 10999


Appellate Court of Connecticut


31 Conn. App. 497; 626 A.2d 769; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 254


February 16, 1993, Argued  
June 1, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of sexual assault in a spousal or cohabiting relationship, and two counts of the crime of reckless endangerment in the second degree, and with the crimes of injury or risk of injury to a child, unlawful restraint in the second degree, threatening, and assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number seventeen, and tried to the jury before Sheldon, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of sexual assault in a spousal or cohabiting relationship, reckless endangerment in the second degree, unlawful restraint in the second degree and threatening, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.E


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which, after a jury trial, convicted him of sexual assault in a spousal or cohabiting relationship, unlawful restraint in the second degree, reckless endangerment in the second degree, and threatening.


OVERVIEW: Defendant forced his wife to have sexual intercourse with him. He also hit her, threw her about, and threatened to kill her, and he threw their infant son into his crib. As a result, defendant was convicted of numerous offenses. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that: (1) defendant failed to preserve for review his claim that the state's evidence was insufficient to sustain his convictions; (2) because it was not clear from the jury's verdict on which definition of "use of force," Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70b(a)(2)(B), the jury based defendant's conviction, he did not satisfy his burden of showing a clear constitutional violation; (3) defendant's claim that the prosecutor's argument constituted misconduct and deprived him of his right to a fair trial was not reviewable under the "exceptional circumstances" doctrine; (4) defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel was more properly pursued on a petition for a new trial or on a petition for a writ of habeas corpus than on direct appeal; and (5) the trial court properly admitted testimony on battered women's syndrome for rehabilitative purposes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of sexual assault in a spousal or cohabiting relationship, unlawful restraint in the second degree, reckless endangerment in the second degree, and threatening.

State v. Torres


No. 10922


Appellate Court of Connecticut


31 Conn. App. 443; 625 A.2d 239; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 251


January 11, 1993, Argued  
May 25, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of marijuana with intent to sell and possession of drug paraphernalia, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the court, O'Keefe, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence, thereafter the defendant was presented to the court, R. O'Connell, J., on a plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut), which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance with intent to sell, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(b), and possession of drug paraphernalia, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-267(a), following the denial of his motion to suppress evidence and subsequent nolo contendere plea.


OVERVIEW: On an anonymous tip that defendant was transporting marijuana in a 1977 Ford Thunderbird with Massachusetts plates and was returning within a few hours, a trooper and a dog trained to sniff out narcotics went to an interstate, where such a vehicle was seen. After learning that the license number was not in the computer, the trooper pulled defendant over. Defendant identified himself, and the dog alerted at the truck of the car. When no drugs were found in the trunk, the trooper reasoned that the odor was carried by the wind from the front of the car. A cellophane envelope containing marijuana was found under the battery. The court declined to review defendant's claims that the police unconstitutionally "seized" him and his car, and that the dog sniff was unconstitutional, because the claims were made for the first time in his reply brief. Further, the record was inadequate to review the claims. The trial court did not make factual findings on those issues for the court to review. Finally, the trial court properly found that probable cause existed to search the entire car because the dog sniff was found to be reliable and several details of the informant's tip were corroborated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1052 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fields


No. 10978


Appellate Court of Connecticut


31 Conn. App. 312; 624 A.2d 1165; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 232


January 8, 1993, Argued  
May 18, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the first degree, assault of a victim sixty or older in the third degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree, larceny in the second degree and larceny in the fourth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Barnett, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of burglary in the first degree, assault of a victim sixty or older in the third degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, after a jury trial, from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), for burglary in the first degree, assault of a victim 60 or older in the third degree, and unlawful restraint in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered an elderly victim's house and choked her until she lost consciousness. She later discovered that $ 600 and her earrings were missing. After defendant was convicted of burglary in the first degree, assault of a victim 60 or older in the third degree, and unlawful restraint in the first degree, he appealed. The court affirmed the convictions. The jury could have concluded that the victim was exposed to a substantial risk of injury. The state presented the jury with ample evidence to conclude reasonably that defendant entered the house intending to commit larceny. The trial court denied a motion to suppress his sneakers as tangible evidence. The trial court properly ruled that the police searched his apartment and seized the sneakers with his freely given consent. A claim that defendant's later inculpatory sworn statement to the police resulted from police misconduct in obtaining the sneakers lacked merit. The trial court properly denied a motion to suppress the victim's in-court identification. The victim's initial identification was not the result of a suggestive identification procedure. There was no constitutional infirmity in the identification process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for burglary in the first degree, assault of a victim 60 or older in the third degree, and unlawful restraint in the first degree.

 

1053 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Orsi v. Senatore


No. 10363


Appellate Court of Connecticut


31 Conn. App. 400; 626 A.2d 750; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 252


October 8, 1992, Argued; October 9, 1992, Argued  
April 29, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for, inter alia, a judgment declaring that certain procedures used by the defendant in removing children from foster care for placement with family members were unconstitutional, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Juvenile Matters at Plainville, and tried to the court, Brenneman, J.; judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff brought an action for a judgment declaring that certain procedures used by defendant, the Commissioner of Children and Youth Services, in removing children from foster care for placement with family members were unconstitutional. Plaintiff appealed from a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which entered judgment for defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought an action against defendant, the Commissioner of the Department of Children and Youth Services, following defendant's proposed removal of a child from foster care, alleging that certain procedures used by defendant were unconstitutional. The trial court found that plaintiff lacked standing and entered judgment in favor of defendant. On appeal, the court concluded that the case presented exceptional circumstances and that an action could be commenced by plaintiff, a next friend, for the purposes of protecting the child's interests, even though he already had counsel and a guardian ad litem to protect those interests. However, because the count was brought on the child's behalf, the declaratory judgment action belonged to the child, not to plaintiff. The constitutional right of the child, a liberty interest in safety, established the necessary foundation for both the procedural due process and equal protection claims asserted by the child. The court concluded that the procedures by which defendant removed a child from a foster home and returned him to the home of a family member violated the child's constitutional right to procedural due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case to the trial court with direction to render judgment declaring that the existing procedures by which the Department of Children and Youth Services removes a child from a foster home in which he or she has resided for one year or more and places the child with a family member are unconstitutional.

State v. Patterson


Nos. 10752, 10855


Appellate Court of Connecticut


31 Conn. App. 278; 624 A.2d 1146; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 225


December 7, 1992, Argued  
April 22, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of marijuana with intent to sell and possession of marihuana, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Nigro, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the case was tried to the jury before Sylvester, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of possession of marijuana with intent to sell, and judgment revoking the defendant's probation, from which the defendant filed separate appeals to this court, which were consolidated.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgments of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which denied his motion to suppress evidence, convicted him of possession of marijuana with intent to sell in violation of General Statutes § 21a-277(b), acquitted him of possession of marijuana in violation of General Statutes § 21a-277(b), revoked his outstanding probation, and sentenced him immediately.


OVERVIEW: At voir dire, the trial judge informed the parties that he would be in chambers if needed and left. On appeal from his conviction, defendant argued that the trial court erred in ruling that the State had not discriminatorily employed a peremptory challenge, in failing to set aside inconsistent verdicts, and in evoking his probation. In reversing, the court held that the trial judge, in accord with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-82f and the state constitution, had the duty to preside in person over voir dire and his failure to do so deprived defendant of the right to a public trial by an impartial jury. The court found that it was not possible to address defendant's argument regarding the exercise of peremptory challenges due to the trial judge's absence, which the court ruled was not harmless error and was not cured by defendant's apparent waiver because the right of the excluded juror to serve was also at stake. The court ruled that defendant's acquittal of a lesser included offense did not mandate reversal because consistency in verdicts was not required and that the trial court erred in revoking probation without due process under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-32 and Conn. Prac. Book § 943.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the trial court and remanded for a new trial.

Grace Community Church v. Bethel


No. 11312


Appellate Court of Connecticut


30 Conn. App. 765; 622 A.2d 591; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 161


January 13, 1993, Argued  
March 30, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a judgment declaring certain of the defendants' zoning regulations to be unconstitutional, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the court, Fuller, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff church appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut), which ordered the planning and zoning commission to grant the church a special permit but rejected the church's claims that defendant city's zoning regulations were in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I, XIV.


OVERVIEW: The church optioned residential zoned property and applied to the city for a special permit, which was granted after a public hearing. The neighbors sought judicial review. The commission denied the permit. The church appealed and filed a separate constitutional challenge. The superior court ordered a permit to be issued but denied relief on the constitutionality claim. The church appealed. The court found that the superior court had correctly concluded that it lacked jurisdiction for declaratory relief because the claim was not based on an actual controversy. The possibility of future church expansion failed to overcome the mootness doctrine because, if expansion occurred, there was time to appeal. The special permit procedure had not violated U.S. Const. amend. I because the restrictions were necessary for the important purpose of safety and welfare in residential areas. The zoning ordinance was content-neutral and applied to clubs, community centers, and nursery schools. The church's equal protection rights were not violated because the church was not similarly situated to the surrounding one-family residences.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's decision to reject the church's claims that the city's zoning regulations were unconstitutional.

Burns v. Board of Educ.


No. 11284


Appellate Court of Connecticut


30 Conn. App. 594; 621 A.2d 1350; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 132


January 13, 1993, Argued  
March 16, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained by the named plaintiff as a result of the defendants' alleged negligence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Rush, J., granted the defendants' motion for partial summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a high school student and his mother as next friend, appealed a partial summary judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) that defendants, a city, the city's board of education, and the city's superintendent of schools, were immune from liability for negligence with respect to the high school student's injuries sustained when he slipped and fell on ice on public school grounds.


OVERVIEW: The student was walking across the high school courtyard when he slipped and fell on a sheet of ice. He fractured his left elbow. The area was not sanded or salted. There were no warnings issued to the students about its condition. The school's policy was that the head custodian was to inspect the area and order sanding and salting as necessary. Plaintiffs filed an action in four counts seeking damages for the student's injuries. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment as to all counts except the count for nuisance, which was directed against the city and the board of education. Defendants argued that they were protected from liability by governmental immunity. The trial court granted the motion and plaintiffs appealed. The court noted that the decision whether to salt or sand the area around the high school was not made by the superintendent. Even if the superintendent had possessed a duty with regard to maintaining conditions on the high school grounds, it would have been a discretionary rather than a ministerial duty. As such, it would have fallen within the ambit of governmental immunity. Moreover, the foreseeable victim exception did not apply to the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the partial summary judgment.

 

1057 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sweeney


No. 10534


Appellate Court of Connecticut


30 Conn. App. 550; 621 A.2d 304; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 103


October 26, 1992, Argued  
March 9, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of more than one kilogram of marihuana with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and conspiracy to distribute marihuana, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Purtill, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of possession of less than four ounces of marihuana and conspiracy to distribute marihuana, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted her of possession of less than four ounces of marihuana and conspiracy to distribute marihuana. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied her motion to suppress evidence seized as a result of a financial records warrant because it failed to state with particularity the items to be seized.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the phrases "but not limited to" and "other records used as means and instrumentalities" were so generic and vague as to violate the U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court disagreed and found that the warrant and accompanying affidavit were sufficiently particular to guard against this danger. The affidavit specifically described the results of the initial search and described many of the items found, relating to the possession and sale of drugs, in the course of that search. Moreover, the language "including but not limited to" was not overbroad when viewed in light of the totality of the case. First, the warrant impliedly limited the seizure of records similar to those specifically outlined in the warrant and the affidavit. Second, the seizure of records was specifically limited, by the language and other records used as means and instrumentalities of the crimes, to records relating to the crimes listed in the warrant and affidavit. The warrant did not allow an unrestrained rummaging for evidence of any crime. It instructed the officers to seize only those items indicating activity associated with the illegal possession and distribution of marihuana.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for possession of less than four ounces of marihuana and conspiracy to distribute marihuana.

Connecticut Nat'l Bank v. Oxenhandler


No. 11245


Appellate Court of Connecticut


30 Conn. App. 541; 621 A.2d 300; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 105


January 5, 1993, Argued  
March 9, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the alleged breach of a brokerage services agreement, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the defendants filed a counterclaim; thereafter, the court, Gill, J., granted the plaintiffs' motion for judgment of default and rendered judgment thereon; subsequently, the court, Freed, J., granted the plaintiffs' motion for judgment and rendered judgment for the plaintiffs; thereafter, the court, M. Hennessey, J., denied the defendants' motion to open the judgment and the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiffs, a bank and a brokerage, to recover damages for the alleged breach of a brokerage services agreement, defendant, a brokerage services account holder, appealed from decisions of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted plaintiffs' motions for judgment of default and for judgment and denied the account holder's motion to open the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The account holder agreed that he would be personally liable to the brokerage for any indebtedness owed on his brokerage accounts. The account holder's bank refused to make payment for stock that the brokerage purchased on behalf of the account holder. The stock was liquidated at a loss. Plaintiffs brought an action for the deficiency. A default judgment was entered against the account holder. He filed an uncertified motion that was not acted on by the trial court; later, he filed a motion to open 22 months after judgment was entered on his default. The court affirmed the judgment against the account holder. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-212(a) and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 377 required a motion to open to be brought within four months of any judgment rendered on a default. Because he was defaulted for failure to appear for trial, judgment could be rendered without notice to him under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 364 (a). The earlier motion did not trigger the stay provisions of Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. §§ 4009, 4046. Plaintiffs did not receive notice of that motion and it was not effective to request that the judgment be opened.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of plaintiffs.

State v. Plude


No. 10931


Appellate Court of Connecticut


30 Conn. App. 527; 621 A.2d 1342; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 109


January 11, 1993, Argued  
March 9, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with eleven counts each of the crimes of sexual assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Ford, J., granted in part, the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment acquitting the defendant of seven counts each of sexual assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury on a substitute information charging the defendant with four counts each of the crimes of sexual assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child; verdict and judgment of guilty of three counts each of sexual assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which found him guilty of three counts each of sexual assault in the second degree, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71(a)(1), and risk of injury to a child, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a high school teacher when he became sexually involved with a student. The victim finally confided in another teacher regarding her relationship with defendant. On appeal, the court affirmed the sexual assault and risk of injury to a child convictions. The court held that the defense of emancipation did not exist in criminal matters; therefore, the trial court properly rejected the defense. At trial, defendant failed to object to the jury instructions that on appeal he claimed had denied him a fair trial. Accordingly, one of the elements that defendant had to prove to prevail on that argument was that a constitutional violation clearly existed and clearly deprived defendant of a fair trial. Defendant did not meet that burden. The court found that the jury charge as a whole fairly presented the issues, that no reasonable possibility existed that the jury was misled by the charge, and that the trial court fairly and properly differentiated between the elements of the offenses charged in the information. Defendant did not have to know or have reason to know that the victim was under age 16 in order to be found guilty under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71(a)(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

1060 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rivera


No. 10362


Appellate Court of Connecticut


30 Conn. App. 224; 619 A.2d 1146; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 46


September 30, 1992, Argued  
February 2, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of rioting at a correctional institution, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Miano J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him of rioting at a correctional institution in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-179b(a). Defendant claimed that § 53a-179b(a) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad, and that the evidence was insufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that his conduct violated § 53a-179b.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was identified as having been among those inmates at the front of the group that marched prior to the riot. Defendant refused to obey an order to clear the yard and refused to heed an officer's attempt to prevent the escalation of the inmates' activities. The trial court found that by refusing to cooperate with the attempts to maintain calm, and by marching with the inmates, defendant aided, abetted, assisted, and took part in the disorder in violation of § 53a-179b, which was therefore not unconstitutionally vague. Moreover, § 53a-179b was specifically directed at two groups: those who led or planned disturbances at a correctional institution and those who followed in the proscribed activity. Section 53a-179b, as construed by the courts, did not reach a substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct. Therefore, defendant's overbreadth argument failed. Finally, the evidence was sufficient to prove that defendant's conduct violated § 53a-179b. The trial court reasonably could have believed officers' testimony that defendant repeatedly failed to obey the orders to clear the yard, and that defendant was seen marching at the front of the group before the riot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for rioting at a correctional institution.

 

1061 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Joyce


No. 9896


Appellate Court of Connecticut


30 Conn. App. 164; 619 A.2d 872; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 43


September 14, 1992, Argued  
January 26, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of arson in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of arson in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of arson in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-111(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed arson conviction, claiming that: (1) the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress the results of a test performed on his clothing; (2) the trial court improperly refused to admit evidence implicating a third party as the perpetrator; and (3) there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction. Upon review, the court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that: (1) the trial court's finding that defendant had no reasonable expectation of privacy in his clothing was adequately supported by the evidence, and thus the trial court correctly denied the defendant's motion to suppress the results of the analysis of his clothing; (2) because the evidentiary ruling was properly within the trial court's discretion, defendant's state and federal due process rights were not violated by the exclusion of evidence that a third party might have committed the crime; and (3) the jury could have reasonably concluded that the cumulative effect of the evidence established that defendant was the perpetrator, and there was sufficient evidence for the jury to find, beyond a reasonable doubt, that the firefighters were exposed to a risk of substantial injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's arson conviction.

State v. Velez


No. 11326


Appellate Court of Connecticut


30 Conn. App. 9; 618 A.2d 1362; 1993 Conn. App. LEXIS 13


October 27, 1992, Argued  
January 12, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Informations charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of narcotics with intent to sell, failure to appear in the first degree, possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle, possession of a sawed-off shotgun, attempt to commit murder and attempt to commit assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham at Putnam, where the cases were consolidated and the defendant was presented to the court, Noren, J., on pleas of guilty of possession of narcotics with intent to sell, failure to appear in the first degree, possession of a sawed-off shotgun, and attempt to commit assault in the first degree; thereafter, the court nolled the remaining charges and rendered judgments of guilty in accordance with the pleas, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham at Putnam (Connecticut) upon guilty pleas to criminal attempt to commit assault in the first degree, failure to appear in the first degree, possession with intent to sell a narcotic substance by a person who is not drug-dependent, and possession of a sawed-off shotgun.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty in a plea canvass proceeding in which the state attorney recited the facts alleged against him and the trial court recited the elements of the offenses charged. Defendant was convicted, and on appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the Due Process Clause did not require the trial court to advise defendant, or ensure that his attorney had advised him, of the relationship between the facts, as alleged, and the elements of the crimes to which he pleaded guilty. The court declined to review defendant's claim that such a separate law-fact analysis was required by Conn. Gen. Practice Book § 711 because defendant failed to raise the claim to the trial court and the claim was not of constitutional magnitude. The court noted that defendant made no claim that any essential element of any offense was omitted by the trial court or that any necessary fact was omitted by the state's attorney during the canvass, nor did he claim that he was not competent to understand the proceedings and enter the plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant.

 

1063 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Southington v. Pierce


No. 10620


Appellate Court of Connecticut


29 Conn. App. 716; 617 A.2d 929; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 450


October 26, 1992, Argued  
December 15, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from continuing to operate a commercial parking lot in violation of a cease and desist order issued by the plaintiff zoning enforcement officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain, where the defendants filed a counterclaim; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Wagner, J., which granted a temporary injunction, and the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant owners appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain (Connecticut), which, on request of plaintiffs, Town of Southington and its zoning enforcement officer, enjoined them from using their property for commercial parking purposes, gave them time to comply with its order, and ordered that the injunction remain in effect until appropriate curative action was put into effect.


OVERVIEW: In response to a motion for articulation filed by the property owners, the trial court stated that "appropriate curative action" would include the modification of the existing cease and desist orders or of the temporary injunction granted. On appeal, the court held that the injunction issued by the trial court was a temporary injunction and thus there was no final judgment for appeal purposes. The court noted that, although the parties had recognized the jurisdictional considerations, they sought to argue their claims. However, the court held that appellate jurisdiction could not be conferred on the court by agreement. The court held that neither of the circumstances under which an interlocutory order was appealable pertained. The trial court's order neither terminated a separate and distinct proceeding, nor so concluded the rights of the parties that further proceedings could not affect them. A decision affecting the merits of a controversy could not be separate and distinct and the rights of the parties had not been concluded, so any further proceedings would necessarily affect them. Further, the owners had asserted an unresolved counterclaim for damages.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

 

1064 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


No. 11056


Appellate Court of Connecticut


29 Conn. App. 683; 617 A.2d 918; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 445


October 2, 1992, Argued  
December 15, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of risk of injury to a child, breach of the peace and assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the court, Ripley, J.; judgment of guilty of risk of injury to a child and breach of the peace, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk, Geographical Area Number Twenty (Connecticut), that convicted him of risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53:21, arguing that the statute was unconstitutionally vague as applied to his case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his wife were undergoing an antagonistic divorce. After defendant's wife dropped their child off at defendant's home and left with her boyfriend, defendant placed the child in his car, chased the couple's vehicle, and rammed his vehicle into theirs three times. Although no one was injured, defendant was charged with risk of injury to a child under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21. The trial court rejected defendant's argument that the collision was accidental, and defendant was convicted of the charged offense. Defendant appealed, challenging the statute under the void for vagueness doctrine. In affirming, the court concluded that the first part of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 proscribed conduct evidencing deliberate indifference to or the creation of situations that could be harmful to the minor's physical welfare. Where defendant placed the child into his car, pursued another vehicle at a high speed, and then rammed into that other vehicle, the possibilities for injury to the child were significant. Whether the incident was accidental or intentional was a question for resolution by the trier of fact, and that determination would not be disturbed on appeal.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. Erzen


No. 10858


Appellate Court of Connecticut


29 Conn. App. 591; 617 A.2d 177; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 422


October 1, 1992, Argued  
December 1, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of injury or risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the court, Ripley, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which convicted him of two counts of risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of risk of injury to a child in violation of § 53-21 after he exposed himself to two children in the park. Defendant appealed his conviction, arguing that § 53-21, as applied to the facts of his case, was so vague and indefinite as to violate the due process provisions of Conn. Const. art. I, § 8 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court held that indecent exposure was a criminal offense at common law, and also by virtue of statutory provision. It was clear that exposing oneself to a child was an act that was "likely to impair the morals" of that child. Defendant's actions led the court to the conclusion that he knew what he was doing was prohibited because he lured the children to a secluded area, asked them if anyone was coming, and asked them to act as guards. Defendant had fair notice that the conduct in which he engaged would subject him to the penalties of the risk of injury statute and thus did not meet his heavy burden of demonstrating that, as applied to his case, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1066 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rose


No. 10471


Appellate Court of Connecticut


29 Conn. App. 421; 615 A.2d 1058; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 396


September 21, 1992, Argued  
November 10, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in each case, charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Flanagan, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of two counts of robbery in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4), on a jury verdict. Defendant was sentenced to prison for 20 years on the first count and 5 years on the second count, with the sentences to run consecutively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant complained that the trial court failed to suppress identification evidence, declined his request for an in-court lineup, and did not sever the offenses. He argued that the photographic array shown to the victims was impermissibly suggestive because his photo was the only one that matched the victims' full description of the robber. The court noted that the victims had ample opportunity to view the unmasked defendant at close range, in sufficient lighting, and they focused on the robber as he pointed a gun at them. Further, the victims gave accurate, detailed descriptions and were certain in selecting defendant's photograph. The court held that, under the totality of the circumstances, the trial court did not err in finding that the out-of-court identifications were reliable. Thus, the in-court identifications were also reliable, and defendant was not entitled to an in-court lineup. Finally, there was no error in trying the offenses together. The two robberies were similar events, the State's presentation was comprehensible to the jury and organized chronologically by separate incident, and the trial court's instructions emphasized that there were two separate crimes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Spence


No. 10608


Appellate Court of Connecticut


29 Conn. App. 359; 614 A.2d 864; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 386


September 14, 1992, Argued  
October 20, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drugdependent and conspiracy to distribute narcotics, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and presented to the court, Damiani, J., on a plea of guilty of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to vacate his plea and rendered judgment of guilty of the sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) that denied defendant's motion to vacate his plea and rendered defendant guilty of the sale of narcotics by a person who was not drug-dependent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a guilty plea to the charge of sale of narcotics by a person who was not drug-dependent. The trial court accepted the plea after determining that it was made knowingly and voluntarily in accord with Conn. Gen. Prac. Book §§ 711 and 712. Defendant subsequently filed a motion to withdraw his plea, which was denied. The court affirmed, holding that based on the record, defendant was not misled or coerced by the trial court's statements regarding sentencing. In fact, the trial court explained the full range of possible sentences facing the defendant. Therefore, the trial court substantially complied with § 711 and did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea. The court also found that defendant's guilty plea was made knowingly and voluntarily as was required by Conn. Gen. Prac. Book §§ 712, 720, and 721. Defendant failed to establish that the trial court's statements caused him to plead guilty involuntarily or unknowingly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the sale of narcotics by a person who was not drug-dependent after denying defendant's motion to vacate his guilty plea.

State v. Indrisano


No. 10659


Appellate Court of Connecticut


29 Conn. App. 283; 613 A.2d 1375; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 364


June 11, 1992, Argued  
September 22, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of disorderly conduct, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the court, Ripley, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk, Geographical Area Number Twenty (Connecticut), which convicted him of disorderly conduct, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182, and fined him $ 250. The charges against defendant resulted from his attempt to effect a peaceful, self-help repossession of a copy machine, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42a-9-503.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182 was unconstitutionally vague on its face and as applied to the facts. The court noted that, while defendant's challenge was not distinctly raised at trial, it fell within the parameters of Golding and warranted appellate scrutiny. However, because the record was inadequate for a fair consideration, the court declined to review the claim. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction because the State showed that defendant resorted to cursing, screaming, and physical force in attempting to repossess the machine. His alternative was to await the lessees' momentary return and discuss the matter. The court was unconvinced by defendant's claim that the physical force was a necessary incident to a perceived larceny. The court opined that the controlling lease was not within the express language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-119(13)(A), and that the trial court properly rejected defendant's asserted legal justification. The court found that the trial court erred in finding that statements proffered to show their effect on defendant were hearsay. However, no prejudice or injustice inured to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Sanchez v. Prestia


No. 10669


Appellate Court of Connecticut


29 Conn. App. 157; 612 A.2d 824; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 356


May 6, 1992, Argued  
September 15, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Class action in two counts to recover damages for, inter alia, the defendants' violation of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Pactices Act, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Housing Session at New Britain, where the court, Goldstein, J., granted the plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment as to count one of the complaint and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Susco, J., on the issue of damages; judgment awarding damages to the plaintiffs; subsequently, the court, Berger, J., granted the named defendant's motion to open and vacate the judgment and ordered a new trial, and the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action for violation of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 42-110a through 42-110q, plaintiff low income tenants sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Housing Session at New Britain (Connecticut) granting defendant landlord's objection to the late filing of a judgment as violative of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-183b and ordering a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the tenants and held a trial on the issue of damages. The landlord moved for a new trial under § 51-183b when the trial court did not enter a written judgment within 120 days after the conclusion of the trial. On review from an adverse judgment, the tenants argued that § 51-183b was unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers provision under Conn. Const. art. II, that it was inapplicable to actions under the CUTPA, and that no provision for setting aside a judgment was provided as a remedy in the statute. The court affirmed the judgment and concluded that § 51-183b did not violate the separation of powers provision of the Connecticut Constitution because it was a statute relating to the jurisdiction of the courts, a subject that is exclusively a province of the legislature under Conn. Const. art. V, § 1. Moreover, the court found that although no remedy existed in the statute, it had been created judicially by prior decisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Sawyer


No. 9728


Appellate Court of Connecticut


29 Conn. App. 68; 614 A.2d 471; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 353


January 15, 1992, Argued  
September 8, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Byrne, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which denied defendant's request for a lesser included offense and reasonable efforts instructions, and which upheld a jury verdict that found defendant guilty of manslaughter in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant saw his girlfriend hug and kiss another man, who became defendant's victim. Defendant found a gun and retained possession of it. Defendant saw the victim sitting in a car with another male. Defendant entered the rear seat of the car and pointed the gun at the victim's neck and demanded to be taken where his girlfriend was located. The victim bowed his head slightly and the gun discharged, killing the victim. Defendant was charged with manslaughter in the first degree. The trial court denied defendant's request for a lesser included offense (reasonable efforts instruction) jury instruction, instead instructing the jury that it had to unanimously find defendant not guilty of the greater offense before it may consider a lesser included offense (acquittal first instruction). The court reversed the conviction and remanded the matter, holding that failing to give proper instructions on lesser offenses constituted reversible error, if a defendant was convicted of a greater offense. Neither the reasonable efforts nor the acquittal first instructions were wrong as a matter of law, however, defendant was to be given a choice as to the instruction given.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's first-degree manslaughter conviction and remanded the matter.

Connecticut Health Facilities, Inc. v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


No. 10651


Appellate Court of Connecticut


29 Conn. App. 1; 613 A.2d 1358; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 345


June 8, 1992, Argued  
September 8, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant denying the plaintiffs' application for a special permit to construct a nursing home and child day care center on certain of their real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, Dean, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city zoning board of appeals appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which sustained plaintiff property owners' appeal of the board's decision and granted certification to the property owners for the construction of a nursing home and day care center on certain real property.


OVERVIEW: The board denied the property owners' application for a special exception to build a nursing home and day care center in a single-family residential district. The trial court sustained the property owners' appeal, holding that the city zoning regulations were impermissibly vague. The court held that the burden of showing vagueness and unconstitutionality was the burden of the property owners; whereas here, the trial court raised the vagueness issue sua sponte. The court concluded that the standards set forth in Stamford, Conn. Zoning Regulations § 19.3.2 were intelligible, not vague, and easily applied to the facts of the case. The board had substantial evidence to sustain the reasons it gave for denial. There was no need for an additional nursing home in the area; the location was far from general hospitals; property values would be adversely affected; and the streets were inadequate for increased traffic. On the basis of the record, including the board's members' knowledge of the area, the court held that the board did not act arbitrarily in determining that the property owners did not meet the standards set forth in the regulations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with direction to render judgment dismissing the property owners' appeal of the board's decision to deny the property owners' special exception application.

Collins v. Goldberg


No. 10718


Appellate Court of Connecticut


28 Conn. App. 733; 611 A.2d 938; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 331


June 11, 1992, Argued  
August 25, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the defendant suspending the plaintiff's license to operate a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Schaller, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff suspended driver sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which dismissed the driver's appeal of the administrative suspension of the driver's operator's license by defendant commissioner of motor vehicles.


OVERVIEW: A driver was directed by a police officer to pull over onto the side of the road because the officer observed him driving in an erratic manner. The driver was uncooperative and refused to take a field sobriety test. The driver was taken to a police station, where he ultimately consented to a breathalyzer test. The test indicated that the driver had a blood alcohol content of .131. A written report of the arrest and test results were forwarded to the department of motor vehicles in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b(c). The commissioner of motor vehicles informed the driver that his operator's license would be suspended because his blood alcohol content had exceeded the level set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b, the implied consent law. The suspension was upheld administratively. The driver contended that the police document was improperly admitted hearsay. The court affirmed the suspension, holding that the plain language of § 14-227b(c) authorized either the individual who administered the test or the individual who caused the test to be administered to sign the oath on the police report, thus the police report was properly submitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the administrative suspension of the driver's operator's license.

State v. Jackson


No. 10116


Appellate Court of Connecticut


28 Conn. App. 721; 613 A.2d 846; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 330


June 15, 1992, Argued  
August 25, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree and hindering prosecution in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before McKeever, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted after a jury trial in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven of robbery in the first degree as an accessory, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, and hindering prosecution in the first degree. Defendant sought appellate review.


OVERVIEW: The court held that defendant's challenged statements, made when he was being routinely booked, were properly admitted into evidence. The court held that defendant failed to preserve as issues on appeal the denial of his right to cross-examine the victim as to his prior convictions, the jury instructions as to circumstantial evidence, and the alleged failure to properly charge the jury on circumstantial evidence, and to give a specific unanimity instruction on the conspiracy and hindering counts. Defendant also claimed that his double jeopardy rights were violated when he was convicted both as a principal on robbery charges and for hindering prosecution. Although the issue was not preserved for appeal, because of its constitutional implications, the court examined the record and found that there was no double jeopardy in the case at bar because robbery required proof of larceny, whereas hindering prosecution required proof of criminal assistance to another who committed a class A or B felony. The court held that the charged crimes did not arise out of the same act or transaction. The court denied defendant's claims of error and affirmed his convictions.


OUTCOME: The court held that defendant failed to preserve many of his allegations of error at trial. The court found that statements made by defendant during routine booking were not protected under Miranda. The court also held that the charged crimes that defendant contended violated the Double Jeopardy Clause did not arise out of the same act or transaction. The court affirmed the trial court's judgments of conviction and dismissed defendant's appeal.

State v. DeWitt


No. 10100


Appellate Court of Connecticut


28 Conn. App. 638; 611 A.2d 926; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 324


June 10, 1992, Argued  
August 18, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of cocaine with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of possession of cocaine with intent to sell, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Fairfield, which entered a verdict and judgment finding defendant of guilty of possession of cocaine with intent to sell.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was apprehended while standing in an area known for high narcotics trafficking and was in possession of a large quantity of narcotics packaged in a manner used by street dealers. When police officers approached, defendant hid the narcotics in his mouth. Defendant was convicted possession with intent to distribute, and appealed. Defendant claimed that the trial court incorrectly denied his motion for a judgment of acquittal, which was based upon insufficiency of the evidence, and charged the jury on the issue of reasonable doubt. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The jury could have reasonably concluded that the amount possessed by defendant was not intended for his personal use. A trier of fact could have reasonably concluded at the close of the State's case, without any consideration of defendant's evidence, that the State had proven beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant possessed narcotics with an intent to sell them. The jury instructions adequately informed it that defendant was presumed innocent until the State proved otherwise and that it was the State's burden to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court convicting defendant of possession of cocaine with intent to sell.

State v. Johnson


No. 10042


Appellate Court of Connecticut


28 Conn. App. 645; 612 A.2d 799; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 325


June 1, 1992, Argued  
August 18, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree and assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Heiman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him of robbery in the first-degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4), conspiracy to commit robbery in the first-degree under §§ 53a-134(a)(4), 531-48(a), and assault in the second-degree under § 53a-60(a)(2). He was sentenced to 23 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant received a 23-year sentence for robbery and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first-degree and assault in the second-degree. On appeal, he alleged that the trial court improperly admitted testimony concerning a pretrial identification of him and the denial of his motion not sever his trial from those of his codefendants. The court affirmed the judgment. The court ruled that there were no requirements that the witness should have been shown a certain number of photographs. The court held that defendant failed to establish that a constitutional violation existed and deprived him of a fair trial. Therefore, the pretrial identification procedure was found not to be unnecessarily suggestive. The court upheld the denial of defendant's motion to sever because defendant failed to specify what, if any, evidence was admitted at the joint trial of defendants that would not have been admissible at his separate trial. The fact that defendant was the only codefendant to present an alibi defense did not render the denial of his motion an abuse of discretion. His alibi was not antagonistic to his codefendant's claims of innocence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence for robbery in the first-degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first-degree, and assault in the second-degree.

Appellate Court of Connecticut
