State v. Chapman


No. 10624


Appellate Court of Connecticut


28 Conn. App. 360; 610 A.2d 1328; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 288


April 29, 1992, Argued  
July 21, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before John F. Walsh, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(1). Defendant appealed from a judgment by the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London (Connecticut), which convicted and sentenced him to 14 years suspended after seven years.


OVERVIEW: The victim told police that defendant had asked her to enter an office where he ripped off her pants, pushed her back on the floor, and sexually assaulted her. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court's charge to the jury improperly enlarged the offense of sexual assault in the first degree. The trial court instructed the jury that it could convict defendant if it found that he had compelled the victim to engage in sexual intercourse by either the use of force against her, or the threat of use of force. Although § 53a-70(a)(1) created liability under both theories, the substituted information alleged that defendant had violated the statute only by the use of force. The State conceded that there was no evidence on the threat of use of force. The court concluded that the jury was improperly charged. Ten months before trial and following an examination, defendant was found competent to stand trial. Although he claimed that his amnesia impaired his ability to assist counsel in the preparation of his defense, he failed to renew his claim or to request a contemporaneous examination at the time of his trial. Thus, he did not meet his burden of proving his lack of competence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial.

State v. Ephraim

July 21, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information, in each case, charging the defendants with six counts each of the crimes of larceny in the first degree and conspiracy to commit larceny in the first degree and with the crimes of larceny in the second degree, conspiracy to commit larceny in the second degree, attempt to commit larceny in the third degree and racketeering, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Barry, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, in the first case, of three counts each of larceny in the first degree and conspiracy to commit larceny in the first degree and of larceny in the second degree, conspiracy to commit larceny in the second degree and racketeering, and verdict and judgment of guilty, in the second case, of six counts of larceny in the first degree, three counts of conspiracy to commit larceny in the first degree, and of larceny in the second degree, conspiracy to commit larceny in the second degree, attempt to commit larceny in the third degree and racketeering, from which the defendants filed separate appeals to this court, which were consolidated.  [***2]



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions in consolidated trials before the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) for larceny, conspiracy to commit larceny, and racketeering.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' convictions arose out of their alleged fraudulent acquisition of money and goods from victims in exchange for fortune-telling, spiritual advice and combating evil spirits. Defendants appealed, claiming that the prosecution of them was "inherently unfair" and was "barred" by constitutional free exercise clauses and the trial court improperly admitted certain statements and lifestyle evidence under the co-conspirator exception to the hearsay rule. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. Defendants' free exercise claim was not preserved for review. The record was inadequate, and there was ample evidence on which the jury reasonably could have concluded that defendants did not sincerely believe the representations that they made to the victims regarding fortune-telling and other metaphysical matters. Defendants' lack of sincerity prevented any religious protection. Defendants' claim of improperly admitted evidence failed because they failed to show any prejudice arising from the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court convicting them of larceny, conspiracy to commit larceny, and racketeering.

Hoffman v. Inland Wetlands Com.


No. 10235


Appellate Court of Connecticut


28 Conn. App. 262; 610 A.2d 185; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 278


March 23, 1992, Argued  
July 14, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the defendant denying the plaintiffs' application to conduct certain regulated activities within a designated wetlands area, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Aurigemma, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought review of a decision by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal of a decision by defendant, a town wetlands commission, that denied their request for a permit pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-39(h) to construct a dwelling and driveway within the wetlands.


OVERVIEW: The commission denied the permit requested because the proposed plan would have a significant impact on the wetlands. The owners also had two other lots, one adjacent to the lot in question and one across the street. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court determined that the owners had the burden of proving that a feasible and prudent alternative to their construction plan did not exist. The court found that one commissioner's questioning of the existence of an alternative was not equivalent to a finding that no alternative existed. With respect to the commission's consideration of the adjacent lot, the court held that the commission did not exceed its authority under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183(j)(6) because whether the owners had an interest in an adjoining lot was relevant to a determination of whether a permit should be granted. Although the owners alleged an unconstitutional taking of their property, the court found that that claim could not be reached until a final authoritative decision by the commission had been made because a future application with a different excavation and construction plan could be granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Pickles

Appellate Court of Connecticut

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of misconduct with a motor vehicle and with failure to obey a state traffic control sign, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number eight, where the first count was tried to the jury before Zoarski, J., and where the second count was tried to the court; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of negligent homicide with a motor vehicle and judgment of guilty of failure to obey a state traffic control sign, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

Ducci Electrical Contractors, Inc. v. DOT


No. 10755


Appellate Court of Connecticut


28 Conn. App. 175; 611 A.2d 891; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 267


May 4, 1992, Argued  
July 7, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for breach of contract, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, A. Aronson, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court, Purtill, J., granted the plaintiff's motion to open the judgment and rendered judgment dismissing the action in accordance with a stipulation of the parties; subsequently, the court, A. Aronson, J., denied the plaintiff's motion to reopen the judgment, and the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractor appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted a motion by defendant, state department of transportation, to dismiss the contractor's motion to reopen, pursuant to 1991 Conn. Acts 91-284, § 2, a 1988 judgment of dismissal against the contractor in its action for breach of contract against the department.


OVERVIEW: The contractor entered a contract with the department for certain traffic signal improvements. When the contractor filed an action against the department for a dispute under the contract, the department alleged immunity and the suit was dismissed by a joint stipulation of the parties that recited that the dismissal was because the action was not within the scope of the version of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-61 that was effective on the date of the contract with the department. In 1991, 1991 Conn. Acts 284, § 2 was passed and the contractor filed a motion to reopen the dismissal. The trial court granted the department's motion to dismiss the motion to reopen on the basis that the motion to reopen was premature. The contractor appealed and the court reversed. The court held that the contractor satisfied the statutory requirement to petition the court within 90 days of the effective date of § 2, because the contractor's motion was pending on July 1, 1991, and was thereafter heard and determined by the trial court on September 2, 1991, within the statutory period. The fact that the judgment of dismissal was rendered in accordance with the stipulation of the parties was of no significance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of the department's motion to dismiss the contractor's motion to reopen a previous judgment of dismissal against the department.

Zarembski v. Warren


No. 10353


Appellate Court of Connecticut


28 Conn. App. 1; 609 A.2d 1039; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 245


March 30, 1992, Argued  
June 23, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for, inter alia, a writ of mandamus to compel the defendants to issue a certificate of occupancy for certain of the plaintiffs' real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Thim, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife landowners, appealed the judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), in favor of defendants, a town's zoning enforcement officer, its planning and zoning commission, and its building inspector, on the landowners' suit to compel defendants to issue an occupancy permit to allow the husband's parents to live in the landowners' accessory building.


OVERVIEW: The landowners built a caretaker's house on their property for the use of the husband's parents. The town's building inspector and zoning officer found that the parents' occupancy of the house violated Town of Easton, Conn., Zoning Regulation art. IV, § 4.2.9 and refused to issue a certificate of occupancy, and the board of zoning appeals issued a cease and desist order. The landowners sued defendants to prevent the enforcement of art. IV, § 4.2.9, and the trial court entered judgment in favor of defendants. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that art. IV, § 4.2.9 permitted only full time, unrelated, employees of the landowners to occupy the house. Because the husband's father worked only three hours for the landowners and did not receive a salary, and because there was no evidence that the mother worked for the landowners, the parents were not full time employees as defined in Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 5-196(1)(q) and 32-9j(f).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in all respects.

State v. Lago


No. 9866


Appellate Court of Connecticut


28 Conn. App. 9; 611 A.2d 866; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 244


February 21, 1992, Argued  
June 23, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of arson in the first degree, arson in the second degree and insurance fraud, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Barnett, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of arson in the second degree and insurance fraud, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him on a jury verdict of arson in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-112(a) and insurance fraud in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-215(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: On review, the court found that the trial court properly admitted the resemblance testimony as circumstantial evidence. Despite any impermissibly suggestive identification procedure used by the police, the testimony was reliable. The court adopted a standard for the admission of resemblance testimony when improper identification procedures occurred, and that standard was identical to that applied to identification testimony that is the product of improper police procedure, whether the testimony was reliable based on an examination of the totality of the circumstances. The court then found that the identification testimony did not violate defendant's due process rights because it was reliable. The court also concluded that there was legally sufficient evidence presented at trial for the jury to find defendant guilty of insurance fraud because he listed items on his claim that had not been destroyed in the fire, even though he had not sought reimbursement for the items.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of arson and insurance fraud.

Parker v. Commissioner of Correction


Nos. 10125, 10128, 10133, 10134, 10135, 10136, 10137, 10400, 10401


Appellate Court of Connecticut


27 Conn. App. 675; 610 A.2d 1305; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 221


February 14, 1992, Argued  
June 2, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition in each case for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Axelrod, J.; judgments dismissing the petitions, from which the petitioners, on the granting of certification, filed separate appeals, which were consolidated, to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, petitioners sought review of judgments from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut), which dismissed their claim that the habeas court's finding that there was insufficient evidence of disproportionate representation of their minority groups in the arrays used for selecting grand jurors at the time of their indictments and convictions was improper and violated their right to equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners argued that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to prosecute them because their indictments were obtained from unconstitutionally selected grand juries. The court found that petitioners failed to show good cause for their failure to challenge the grand jury selection process during the pretrial period or on direct appeal. Had they raised a challenge to the grand jury array during the pretrial proceedings, any possible defect could have been cured through a new indictment. This claim was a constitutional challenge to pretrial proceedings. The equal protection claim did not go to the State's power over petitioners and the charged offenses. All petitioners were indicted by a grand jury as required. Petitioners' equal protection challenges related to the composition of the grand jury and not to the grand jury's underlying power to issue an indictment. Any defect in the indictment should have been raised during the pretrial proceedings. The court therefore held that the alleged improper selection of the grand jury did not affect the trial court's subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court dismissing petitioners' claims of disproportionate representation in the grand jury array.

State v. Williams


No. 9751


Appellate Court of Connecticut


27 Conn. App. 654; 610 A.2d 672; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 204


January 13, 1992, Argued  
May 26, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which entered a jury verdict that convicted him of robbery in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(2) and assault in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1). He claimed that the trial court improperly permitted the State to comment on his pretrial silence.


OVERVIEW: After a shooting in a bar, the victim identified defendant by name as the individual who shot him. Defendant was arrested when found hiding in an attic. A jury convicted him of robbery in the first degree and assault in the first degree. The court affirmed his convictions, determining that the trial court did not err in permitting the State to cross-examine him concerning his silence before his arrest because the prohibition on the use of a defendant's pretrial silence applied only to the silence following arrest and receipt of Miranda warnings. The prosecutor's comment on defendant's postarrest silence was improper, but the isolated reference was harmless error. The trial court did not err in permitting testimony describing defendant's arrest where the circumstances of his arrest tended to show consciousness of guilt. The trial court properly instructed the jury that defendant could be convicted of assault in the first degree if they were to find that he intended to assault either the victim or a third person where there was ample evidence that at the time of the assault there were a number of individuals entering and exiting the bar as well as standing in the entrance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for robbery in the first degree and assault in the first degree.

State v. Cobb


No. 9187


Appellate Court of Connecticut


27 Conn. App. 601; 605 A.2d 1385; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 201


January 22, 1992, Argued  
May 19, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempted robbery in the first degree and carrying a dangerous weapon, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before W. Sullivan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of attempted robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49, 53a-134(a)(3) and carrying a dangerous weapon in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-206(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction. The court held that where a person might be convicted under more than one statutory alternative, the judgment could not be supported unless the evidence was sufficient to establish guilt under each statutory provision that the trier might have relied upon. The jury reasonably could have found that when defendant, while waving a knife, chased a restaurant employee after she had closed the cash drawer, he was threatening the immediate use of physical force on her for the purpose of overcoming her resistance to the taking of property, which was sufficient evidence to support its jury instruction that defined robbery under both statutory subdivisions. An indirect comment in argument to the court on a point of law was less serious than a comment in jury summation that asked the jury to infer that defendant's silence was evidence of guilt. Thus, the State's remarks were not forbidden prosecutorial comments on defendant's failure to testify. The evidence and inferences reasonably drawn therefrom provided adequate support for the State's closing argument. Defendant was fully allowed to cross-examine the witnesses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Scott


No. 9977


Appellate Court of Connecticut


27 Conn. App. 403; 606 A.2d 720; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 168


February 19, 1992, Argued  
April 21, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempted murder, assault in the first degree and carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Ford, J.; judgment of guilty of attempted murder and of carrying a pistol without a permit, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which denied his motion to suppress the results of an atomic absorption test as the fruit of an unconstitutional seizure of his person. Defendant was convicted of attempted murder and carrying a pistol without a permit.


OVERVIEW: Upon being convicted of attempted murder and carrying a pistol without a permit, defendant argued on appeal that it was error to deny his motion to suppress the results of an atomic absorption test. Defendant contended that the test results were the fruit of an unconstitutional seizure of his person because law officers did not have a warrant for his arrest prior to entering his home. The court affirmed the judgment. Specifically, the court held that where two witnesses and the victim identified defendant as being the perpetrator of the attempted murder, law officers had probable cause to arrest defendant. Furthermore, the court found that the warrantless arrest of defendant in his home was justified by exigent circumstances under the Dorman test where, among other factors, the offense of attempted murder was grave and violent, the victim had been shot while he lay injured on the ground, and the gun used for the crime was not found at the crime scene, leading to the conclusion that defendant continued to be armed with the weapon. The court also found that the officers had reasonable grounds to believe that if an immediate arrest were not made, defendant would likely flee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment denying defendant's motion to suppress the results of an atomic absorption test.

State v. Gruver


No. 9763


Appellate Court of Connecticut


27 Conn. App. 370; 606 A.2d 39; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 163


October 28, 1991, Argued  
April 14, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motor vehicle complaint charging the defendant with the crime of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, geographical area number nineteen, where the court, Smith, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter the matter was presented to the court, Klaczak, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland, Geographical Area Number Nineteen (Connecticut), which convicted him of operation of a motor vehicle while under the influence of liquor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a. Defendant had entered a conditional nolo contendere plea after denial of his motion to suppress the state's evidence pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-94a.


OVERVIEW: A store clerk concluded that defendant was inebriated and telephoned the police after he told her that he would be driving. An officer arrived while defendant was sitting in his car with the lights on. The officer parked behind his car and turned on the cruiser's overhead light. As he approached the car he detected a strong odor of alcohol. Defendant saw the officer and turned on the ignition. The officer asked him to exit and defendant failed field sobriety tests. He entered a conditional plea of nolo contendere after the trial court denied his motion to suppress. On appeal, the court affirmed. The point at which defendant was seized was not when the officer turned on the cruiser's light but when defendant turned on his ignition as if to leave. At that point, the officer had a reasonable and articulable suspicion that a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a was occurring. The facts justified defendant's detention for the limited intrusion of field sobriety testing to confirm or dispel the officer's suspicion. When defendant turned on his ignition, he committed an offense in the presence of the officer, as § 14-227a did not require that defendant actually move the vehicle.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Zoning Bd. of Appeals v. Planning & Zoning Com.


No. 9738


Appellate Court of Connecticut


27 Conn. App. 297; 605 A.2d 885; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 145


December 11, 1991, Argued  
April 7, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant amending certain zoning regulations, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Gormley, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which the named defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant planning and zoning commission (commission) appealed from the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which sustained an appeal by plaintiff, a zoning board of appeals (board), challenging the commission's adoption of an amended zoning regulation and declared the amendment invalid. Defendants, the commission's secretary and chairman, and plaintiff property owners were also originally parties.


OVERVIEW: The commission amended Wallingford, Conn., Zoning Regulations § 9.1.H.2. The amendment allowed the board to grant use variances only where the failure to do so would constitute an unconstitutional taking. The board appealed to trial court. On appeal from the trial court's decision sustaining the appeal and declaring the amendment to be invalid as a wholesale destruction of the board's statutory right to grant use variances, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The board had standing because it was classically aggrieved by the amendment, which deprived the board of its right under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-6(3) to grant use variances where a literal enforcement of regulations would result in exceptional difficulty or undue hardship. Also, the trial court properly refused to consider irrelevant case law cited by the commission in concluding that the amendment improperly eliminated the board's authority to grant use variances. Finally, the trial court did not improperly rely on the testimony of a town planner in ascertaining the commission's reasons for enacting the amendment to the exclusion of all other testimony and did not substitute its judgment for that of the commission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to sustain the appeal of the board and declaring the amended zoning ordinance to be invalid.

 

1092 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anziano


No. 10041


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


26 Conn. App. 667; 603 A.2d 415; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 78


January 7, 1992, Argued  
February 18, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics, sale of illegal drugs, conspiracy to sell illegal drugs, possession of a controlled substance and destruction of evidence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Meriden, geographical area number seven, where the court, Reilly, J.; granted the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; subsequently, the court granted the state's motion to dismiss with prejudice and rendered judgment dismissing the information, from which the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed, with permission of the trial court, a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Meriden (Connecticut), which dismissed with prejudice the charges against defendant of possession of narcotics, sale of illegal drugs, conspiracy to sell illegal drugs, possession of marijuana, and destruction of evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged possession of narcotics, sale of illegal drugs, conspiracy to sell illegal drugs, possession of marijuana, and destruction of evidence. Prior to trial, the trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress all the evidence obtained pursuant to a search warrant because the affidavit upon which the search warrant was issued failed to establish the citizen informant's reliability, veracity, or basis of knowledge. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court held that after considering the totality of the circumstances described in the affidavit, the affidavit presented a substantial factual basis on which the magistrate could conclude that probable cause existed for issuance of the search warrant. The court further held that the detail provided by the citizen informant indicated a reliable basis of knowledge and permitted a reasonable inference that the information was derived from personal knowledge and observation. The court held that this detail, together with all the other information and circumstances contained in the affidavit, presented sufficient objective indicia of reliability to justify the issuance of the warrant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that granted defendant's motion to suppress and that dismissed the criminal charges against defendant. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

1093 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Estrada


No. 9360


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


26 Conn. App. 641; 603 A.2d 1179; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 75


December 5, 1991, Argued  
February 18, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with four counts of the crime of unlawful restraint in the first degree and with the crimes of burglary in the first degree and assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before S. Freedman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of burglary in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-101(a)(1), assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1), and unlawful restraint in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-95(a). He was convicted by a jury and sentenced to 25 years of incarceration.


OVERVIEW: The incident occurred when defendant and two other men forced their way into an apartment, locked the females present in a bathroom, and shot one of the males. Initially defendant was charged as an accessory, but the State filed an amended complaint that charged defendant as a principal. In its charge to the jury, the trial court instructed on accessory liability. The testimony of the victim reasonably supported the conclusion that defendant was not the principal, but rather an aider or abettor. There was substantial evidence presented at trial to support the instruction on accessory. A witness testified that defendant told her that he did not shoot her brother. When she accused defendant of being present at the shooting, defendant made no response. The court found that defendant's failure to respond to the accusation was an admission by silence. Thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by allowing the testimony as an admission of guilt. The trial court properly denied defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal as to the charge of assault in the first degree because the jury could reasonably have found that the victim suffered serious physical injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of burglary, assault, and unlawful restraint and sentenced him to 25 years of incarceration.

Henin v. Henin


No. 9660


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


26 Conn. App. 386; 601 A.2d 550; 1992 Conn. App. LEXIS 19


October 2, 1991, Argued  
January 14, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Barall, J.; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief, from which the defendant appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to dissolve a marriage and for other relief brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), defendant wife appealed time-limited alimony and plaintiff husband cross-appealed the order requiring payment to defendant of a promissory note upon remarriage.


OVERVIEW: After the dissolution of a marriage by the trial court, defendant wife appealed her time-limited alimony, and plaintiff husband cross-appealed the order requiring payment to defendant of a promissory note upon plaintiff's remarriage, claiming that it violated his constitutional right to marry. On appeal, the court held that a court may find a party's mental condition and consequent behavior was the cause of a marital breakdown and, in this case, found that defendant's illness was the cause of the breakdown of the marriage. The court held that the finding regarding the cause of the breakdown did not improperly infect the financial awards. The court also found that because the particular duration of the award was rational in that it coincided with the maturity of a note that could support defendant, the time-limited alimony was proper. Finally, the court found there was nothing unconstitutional in requiring plaintiff to pay defendant upon his remarriage.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed where the court held that defendant's mental illness was the cause of the marital breakdown, but that such a finding did not improperly infect the financial awards and that it was not unconstitutional to require plaintiff to pay defendant upon his remarriage.

State v. Falcon


No. 9554


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


26 Conn. App. 259; 600 A.2d 1364; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 427


September 19, 1991, Argued  
December 17, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Mulcahy, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm and assault in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) convicted defendant of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm and assault in the third degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The bouncer in a bar was killed by a single gunshot would to the chest when defendant pulled out a gun during a struggle with the bouncer and shot over his shoulder. Defendant was charged with murder and assault in the third degree. Defendant alleged that he shot in self-defense. Defendant also alleged that the trial court improperly instructed the jury that the crime of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm was a lesser included offense of the crime of murder. The court held that the trial court erred in including the use of a firearm to the lesser included offense of manslaughter. The information did not allege the use of a firearm. Manslaughter with a firearm required proof of an additional element that was not a necessary element of the crime of murder and violated defendant's right to know the exact nature of the charges against him. Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in restricting defendant's presentation of his defense by prohibiting him from questioning defense witnesses as to whether they knew why defendant carried a gun. The court held that the trial court properly excluded the evidence as impermissible hearsay irrelevant to the self-defense claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of manslaughter with a firearm and remanded to the trial court. The court directed the trial court to render a judgment of acquittal on the charge of manslaughter with the use of a firearm and to render a judgment of conviction for manslaughter and to resentence defendant. The court affirmed defendant's conviction of assault in the third degree.

Homart Dev. Co. v. Planning & Zoning Com.


No. 9967


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


26 Conn. App. 212; 600 A.2d 13; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 424


September 23, 1991, Argued  
December 10, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the named defendant denying the plaintiff's application for a zone change, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the court, Kulawiz, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developer sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which dismissed the developer's appeal from the denial of its zone change application by defendant, a town's planning and zoning commission.


OVERVIEW: The developer submitted an application to the commission to have its land re-designated as a planned regional shopping district (PRSD) zone. The commission denied the developer's application. The developer claimed that the commission was not entitled to deny its application based on its desire to amend the PRSD regulations in the future. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the PRSD zone was a "floating zone," that an application for a floating zone constituted a request for a zone change, that the commission was not bound to grant the developer's application based on it having met all of the PRSD requirements, and that the commission was acting legislatively. The court also held that no moratorium was at issue, that the commission denied the developer's application for a specific reason, that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2h did not apply, that the evidence supported the commission's decision that the PRSD zone was inadequate to protect the interests of the town and its citizens, and that the commission's decision was reasonably and fairly exercised.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the developer's appeal.

 

1098 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Vincenzo v. Warden, State Prison


No. 9593


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


26 Conn. App. 132; 599 A.2d 31; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 391


September 19, 1991, Argued  
November 12, 1991, Decided  
November 12, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Axelrod, J.; judgment dismissing the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut), which dismissed the prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner claimed that his habeas corpus petition was improperly dismissed because the trial court failed to find that the state board of parole was subject to the rule-making provisions of the Uniform Administrative Procedure Act (UAPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-166 et seq. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that because no liberty interest was implicated by the prisoner's claims, the trial court lacked jurisdiction over the subject mater and properly dismissed the petition. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125 created no protected constitutional or statutory liberty interest in parole release that gave rise to a claim of illegal confinement in a habeas action. The statute vested board discretion in the judgment of the parole board. It did not give an inmate any right to demand or even apply for parole. It did not require that a parole board actually consider any inmate's eligibility for parole if he fulfilled the statute's two requirements. Although the prisoner alleged that his confinement was illegal because the parole board did not adhere to the UAPA's procedures for rule-making, no such liberty interest could arise.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which dismissed the prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

State v. Arline


No. 8453


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


25 Conn. App. 653; 596 A.2d 7; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 338


April 30, 1991, Argued  
September 3, 1991, Decided  
September 3, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Quinn, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), that convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree. The crime was defined by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70. The trial court had refused to allow defendant access to the victim's hospital alcohol-treatment records and a related psychiatric evaluation.


OVERVIEW: The victim proffered during trial that approximately a year after the assault he went into a 30-day alcoholism program at a hospital and had a psychiatric interview as part of the program. Defendant contended that the denial of the hospital records and the stymieing of a line of questioning about the record violated his right to confrontation as he could not show the witness' mental condition, which might reasonably have affected that witness' credibility. Relevant was a witness' mental soundness at the time of trial and at the time of the incident about which the witness was to testify. There was no evidence that the victim was inebriated at the time of the crime. Defendant did not ask whether or not the victim had been drinking heavily at or about the time of trial or on either of the two days on which he gave testimony. His hospitalization was remote in time from the time of the assault. The court ruled that defendant had failed to make a preliminary showing that there was a reasonable probability that the hospital records were material, and, thus, no further steps such as an in camera inspection of the records with the victim's permission were required.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Payne


No. 8993


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


25 Conn. App. 428; 594 A.2d 1035; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 281


December 4, 1990, Argued  
August 13, 1991, Decided  
August 13, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of burglary in the first degree, two counts of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree and two counts of the crime of robbery in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and presented to the court, Damiani, J., on a plea of nolo contendere to two counts of burglary in the first degree and two counts of robbery in the second degree; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) for burglary in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-101(a)(2) and robbery in the second degree in violation of § 53a-135(a)(1). Defendant based his appeal on the standard of probable cause under the Connecticut Constitution and the trial court's finding of a "good faith" exception to the exclusionary rule.


OVERVIEW: Police searched defendant's apartment pursuant to a warrant that had been issued in connection to several area burglaries. The affidavit attached to the warrant included a statement that a known and reliable informant had named defendant as an individual who had been burglarizing the homes. Defendant filed a motion to suppress, the State rebutted contending that while the warrant was not adequately supported by the affidavit, the police officers relied on the warrant in good faith. The trial court found for the State and defendant pleaded nolo contendere and appealed. The State contended that the Gates standard applied to warrants based on informant information, and that the Gates standard should apply where an investigation already existed and the informant only identified a suspect or corroborated facts. The court held that the totality of the circumstances analysis of Gates was sufficient to guarantee defendant's constitutional rights and where the affidavit inferred that sufficient probable cause existed to execute the search, the inadequacy of the affidavit did not render the search unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

State v. Lucci


No. 8394


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


25 Conn. App. 334; 595 A.2d 361; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 266


May 3, 1991, Argued  
July 23, 1991, Decided  
July 23, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, attempted sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the third degree, threatening, and with two counts of the crime of injury or risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Miano, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of sexual assault in the first degree, attempted sexual assault in the first degree, threatening and risk of injury to a child, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which found him guilty of sexual assault, injury or risk of injury to, or impairing the morals of, a child, attempted sexual assault, and threatening.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sexually assaulted a 13 year-old babysitter, prevented her from leaving, and threatened to kill her. Defendant claimed that he was deprived of a fair trial by the trial court's failure to sua sponte order a new trial. The court affirmed. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting and later striking prejudicial evidence. Stricken testimony was cumulative in nature, curative instructions were very thorough, and the trial court's actions followed defendant's request. Defendant's right to a fair trial was protected. Two requirements were met that entitled the State to a missing witness charge: (1) the witness was available; and (2) he was a witness whom the party would naturally produce. When those two conditions existed, the court held that an inference could be drawn that the testimony of that witness was unfavorable to the party's cause. Defendant failed to show that a single misstatement regarding the charge affected the verdict. The court held that alleged prosecutorial misconduct was not severe and counsel for defendant neither objected to the remarks nor asked for a curative instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of sexual assault, injury or risk of injury to, or impairing the morals of, a child, attempted sexual assault, and threatening.

State v. Owens

APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of two judgments of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of larceny in the first degree and of carrying a weapon in a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly stole a friend's rental car and swapped it for another car, in which two guns were discovered upon his arrest. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly instructed the jury and allowed extraneous facts to be presented that prevented the jury from fairly reviewing the relevant evidence. Also, the court did not find that any extraneous facts arose from the consolidation of defendant's two informations for trial because defendant failed to meet his heavy burden of demonstrating that substantial prejudice resulted from the joinder.

1104 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


D'Addario v. Planning & Zoning Com.


No. 6854


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


25 Conn. App. 137; 593 A.2d 511; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 222


March 19, 1991, Argued  
June 25, 1991, Decided  
June 25, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal, in each case, from a decision by the defendant approving a zone classification change as to certain real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the court, Fuller, J.; judgments sustaining the appeals, from which, on the granting of certification, the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant planning and zoning commission appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), that determined that the commission's action in rezoning plaintiff landowners' property from commercial property to residential property amounted to a taking of property without just compensation in violation of both the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court framed the issue as whether or not the zoning regulation as applied to the landowners' properties was so unreasonable and confiscatory as to be for all practical purposes a taking of private property for public use. A balancing test was used to decide whether or not a taking had occurred. That balancing test required that the trial court consider the degree of diminution in value of the particular piece of property and the nature and degree of the public harm to be prevented and the realistic alternative uses available to the landowners. The court found that balanced against the finding that the properties were substantially diminished in value and that there were no realistic alternative uses other than use as residential lots, which would cause the diminution, was the finding that there would be minimal harm if any to the public if the zoning change were not effected. The court ruled that the trial court's finding that the zoning change as applied to the landowners was unreasonable and confiscatory was supported by ample evidence and thus could not be disturbed.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the landowners and against the commission, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Geisler


No. 6934


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


25 Conn. App. 282; 594 A.2d 985; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 264


April 17, 1991, Argued  
June 24, 1991, Decided  
June 24, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the second degree with a motor vehicle, evading responsibility and driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the jury before, Lewis, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court, which reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case with direction to render a judgment of not guilty of driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and for a new trial on the charge of assault in the second degree with a motor vehicle. On petition by the state to the United States Supreme Court for a writ on certiorari, that court vacated the judgment and remanded the case for further consideration.



DISPOSITION: Judgment ordering a new trial affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which convicted him of assault in the second degree with a motor vehicle, evading responsibility, and driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed defendant's convictions and remanded the case with direction to render a judgment of not guilty of driving while under the influence and for a new trial on the charge of assault with a motor vehicle. The United States Supreme Court vacated the court's judgment and remanded the case for further consideration. The court had to decide whether evidence derived from a warrantless entry and arrest in defendant's home should have been suppressed by virtue of the right to be free from unreasonable searches or seizures guaranteed by Conn. Const. art. I, § 7. The court held that the state exclusionary rule, as derived from § 7, barred the state from using evidence acquired outside defendant's home following a violation of the rule that searches and seizures inside a home without a warrant were presumptively unreasonable. However, the exclusionary rule did not bar the state from using the evidence if the taint resulting from the violation was sufficiently attenuated from the initial entry into the home. The unlawful entry into defendant's home was not diluted or lessened in effect by the passage of time or intervening circumstances when the evidence was obtained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for evading responsibility and driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and remanded the case for a new trial on the charge of assault in the second degree with a motor vehicle.

Levine v. Town Plan & Zoning Com.


No. 9001


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


25 Conn. App. 199; 594 A.2d 9; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 245


December 10, 1990, Argued  
June 12, 1991, Decided  
June 12, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant denying the plaintiff's application for a special permit to expand certain commercial property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Cocco, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal from which, on the granting of certification, the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant plan and zoning commission appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which sustained plaintiff motel owner's appeal of its decision denying his request for approval of his plan to build an eight unit addition on his existing motel.


OVERVIEW: The commission denied the motel owner's application for a special permit a 10 unit addition onto his motel. The trial court sustained the motel owner's appeal of the denial and ordered the commission to approve the permit application. The parties then stipulated that the motel owner would build an eight unit addition, but they never filed the stipulation with the trial court. The commission subsequently rejected the motel owner's submission of revised plans to it for an eight unit addition. The trial court sustained the motel owner's appeal of that decision. The commission appealed. The court held that the parties could not settle their prior litigation without trial court approval and as such, the trial court's original decision was still in effect at the time the motel owner submitted revised plans to the commission. Moreover, an application conforming with applicable zoning regulations at the time of its filing could not be disapproved for its failure to comply with subsequent zoning changes and thus, the fact that zoning rules had changed while the litigation was pending did not bar enforcement of the regulations in force at the time of the motel owner's original application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and it remanded the case to the trial court for entry of a judgment directing the commission to issue a special permit in accordance with the motel owner's revised plans for an eight unit addition to his motel.

 

1107 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Laufer v. Conservation Com. of Fairfield


No. 9456


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


24 Conn. App. 708; 592 A.2d 392; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 188


March 18, 1991, Argued  
June 4, 1991, Decided  
June 4, 1991, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a decision by the named defendant denying the plaintiff's application for a permit to conduct certain activities in a designated wetlands area, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Jones, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which dismissed his appeal from the action of defendant town conservation commission in denying his application for permission to construct a stream crossing within a wetland and a watercourse area. The owner's action also named as defendants, the town clerk and the state commissioner of environmental protection.


OVERVIEW: The owner sought to resubdivide a lot into two separate parcels and build a second house on one of the parcels. The application at issue sought permission to install two box culverts to create a driveway crossing a stream. The owner appealed on the grounds including that the commission abused its discretion in failing to approve the application. In affirming the judgment, the court held that the commission did not abuse its discretion by virtue of its failure to adopt the recommendation of the staff of the town's inland wetlands agency to conditionally approve the owner's application. The statutory scheme for the resolution of permit applications, including Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22a-42(c), 22a-42a(c), (d), and 22a-41, envisioned that the authorized agency itself shall be the decision maker. Further, the trial court correctly found that the commission's denial of the owner's application was not clearly erroneous. The stream crossing was found to be unnecessary because upland access on the lot was feasible and prudent. Finally, there was no evidence to support the owner's claim that the commission's action constituted an unconstitutional taking of property without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing his appeal of the commission's action in denying his permit application.

State v. Willis

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine with intent to sell and of possession of marihuana. State v. Rivera


No. 8462


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


24 Conn. App. 670; 591 A.2d 440; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 177


September 12, 1990, Argued  
May 28, 1991, Decided  
May 28, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of unlawful sale of narcotics under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of the unlawful sale of narcotics by a person who was not drug-dependent under § 21a-278(b). On appeal, he alleged that the trial court's instructions to the jury relating to circumstantial evidence violated his constitutional right to present a defense and his right to due process. The court affirmed the conviction. The court, in noting that defendant raised no affirmative statutory defense that would have placed a burden of proof on him, held that the jury was properly instructed on the presumption of innocence afforded defendant and on the State's burden to prove every element of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. The court ruled that the trial court's charge that the basic facts leading to the inferences must have been proven beyond a reasonable doubt was incorrect. However, the incorrect charge constituted harmful error because it was cured by other portions of the charge. The court concluded that the circumstantial evidence was so insignificant compared to the direct evidence, that it was clear beyond a reasonable doubt that the incorrect instruction did not affect the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence of unlawful sale of narcotics.

State v. Bowens


No. 8912


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


24 Conn. App. 642; 591 A.2d 433; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 167


March 18, 1991, Argued  
May 21, 1991, Decided  
May 21, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent and possession of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review after the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) convicted him, after a trial by jury, of the crimes of sale of narcotics by a person who was not drug-dependent and possession of narcotics by a person who was not drug-dependent, both in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278 (b).


OVERVIEW: A police officer watched three black males; one was defendant and the other two were reputed drug dealers. The officer observed a successive pattern in which seven persons approached defendant on foot and entered the hallway with him for two or three minutes before exiting and leaving. After a white male entered and left, the officer arrested him. Defendant fled. Another officer spotted defendant and found 29 small glassine envelopes containing a white powder substance, later identified as heroin. The white suspect could not identify defendant as the person who had sold drugs to him. A jury convicted defendant. The court affirmed. To convict defendant, the State had to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that a sale occurred and that it was defendant who delivered the heroin. Although the officer had not observed an actual sale because of defendant's use of a darkened hallway, the circumstances he observed that night clearly supported his opinion of a sale, by logical inference. The court did not consider some appellate issues because defendant had not preserved the issues and the unpreserved claims were not of constitutional magnitude alleging the violation of a fundamental right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Anderson


No. 9088


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


24 Conn. App. 438; 589 A.2d 372; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 107


November 7, 1990, Argued  
April 16, 1991, Decided  
April 16, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motor vehicles complaint charging the defendant with the crime of operating a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number twelve, and presented to the court, Sferrazza, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Conn.), which convicted him, following a conditional plea of nolo contendere, on a charge of driving while his license was under suspension in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-215. Defendant claimed an anonymous telephone tip corroborated by independent police work was unreliable and did not warrant an investigatory stop.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted, after his conditional plea of nolo contendere, of driving while his license was under suspension in the trial court. In affirming the conviction, the court held that defendant's Fourth Amendment rights were not violated by the investigatory stop. The court concluded that the officer had reasonable articulable suspicion and conducted himself within the scope of his authority under § 14-217 in stopping defendant to determine his identity and his license status. The court reasoned that the state had a compelling interest in making sure only drivers with valid licenses operated vehicles on the public roads. The court noted the stop was minimally intrusive because defendant got out of his vehicle on his own initiative and was not searched or arrested. The court found that the anonymous tip provided a clear and detailed description of the garbage truck, its location, and the location of the occupants. The court concluded that the details of the tip were corroborated because the caller's prediction about defendant's future behavior was enough to establish the caller's reliability, that he was informed, and the information was not an inarticulable hunch.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Palangio


No. 8610


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT

March 26, 1991, Decided  
March 26, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of risk of injury to a child, in the first case, and with two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, in the second case, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Murray, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut) that convicted defendant of three counts of risk of injury to, or impairing the morals of, children in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21.


OVERVIEW: Based on a search warrant in connection with a burglary investigation, police officers seized film belonging to defendant that included nude and seminude pictures of minors. After the department of children and youth services made a complaint to the police department, defendant's cameras and film were seized. Defendant was subsequently charged and convicted of three counts of risk of injury to, or impairing the morals of, children. The court affirmed, holding that § 53-21 was not unconstitutionally vague and overbroad as applied to defendant and that the trial court did not improperly deny defendant's motion to suppress. The statute provided defendant with fair notice that he need not physically touch a child to violate § 53-21 and that the photographing of nude and seminude children was prohibited. The trial court's denial of his motion to suppress the photographs was proper because the officers executing the warrants, acted in good faith, and their reliance upon the warrants was objectively reasonable. The department's complaint constituted an independent source sufficient to establish probable cause.

Tufaro v. Pepperidge Farm, Inc.


No. 9257


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


24 Conn. App. 234; 587 A.2d 1044; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 73


January 11, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
March 12, 1991, Decided  
March 12, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the workers' compensation commissioner for the seventh district requiring the defendant to continue to provide medical insurance coverage for the plaintiff's dependents, brought to the compensation review division, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed an order of the compensation review division (Connecticut), which upheld a decision requiring the employer to continue providing group insurance coverage for the dependants of plaintiff employee while the employee was receiving workers' compensation benefits. The employer contended that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-284b had been preempted by federal law and applied only to the employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee injured her hand while working for the employer. While the employee was on medical leave, the employer continued to provide group insurance coverage for the employee and her dependents. A physician informed the employer that the employee would not be able to return to her job and recommended light duties. The employer subsequently terminated the employee and the benefits for her dependents. The employee filed a complaint which sought group benefits for her dependents. At the time the employee was receiving workers' compensation benefits. The commissioner relied on Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-284b and ordered the employer to provide benefits. The compensation review division affirmed. The employer appealed and contended that the statute was unconstitutional since it was preempted by federal law, and if it applied, it applied only to the employee. The court affirmed and held that neither the commissioner nor the review division had the authority to consider constitutional issues, which was a question of federal law. The court held that recent federal decision held that the statute was not preempted. The court also held that the statute applied to the dependents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

State v. Hart


No. 7913


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


23 Conn. App. 746; 585 A.2d 103; 1991 Conn. App. LEXIS 11


October 4, 1990, Argued  
January 15, 1991, Decided  
January 15, 1991, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sale of cocaine by a person who is not drug-dependent, sale of cocaine, conspiracy to sell cocaine and possession of cocaine, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, and tried to the jury before Ripley, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of sale of a narcotic substance by a person who was not drug-dependent under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b), sale of a narcotic substance under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a), conspiracy to sell a narcotic substance under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-48(a), 21a-277(a), and possession of a narcotic substance under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(a).


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of sale of a narcotic substance by a person who was not drug-dependent under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b), sale of a narcotic substance under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a), conspiracy to sell a narcotic substance under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-48(a), 21a-277(a), and possession of a narcotic substance under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(a). On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment in part and reversed it in part as to the conviction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b). The court found that the trial court's instruction improperly permitted the jury to make the initial determination of whether defendant had produced sufficient evidence of drug dependency to place the burden on the State to prove that she was not drug-dependent. The court concluded that the burden shifted to the State to prove the absence of drug dependency beyond a reasonable doubt because defendant introduced substantial evidence of drug dependency. The court further concluded that the State failed to meet its burden to show the absence of drug dependency and that double jeopardy precluded a second trial on the count for violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment with respect to defendant's conviction for sale of a narcotic substance by a person who was not drug-dependent. The court remanded the case with direction to render a judgment of acquittal on that charge and to resentence defendant on her convictions for sale of a narcotic substance, conspiracy to sell a narcotic substance, and possession of a narcotic substance.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in each case, charging the defendant with failing to provide a fire alarm system in a rooming house, failing to provide self-closing doors for sleeping rooms in a rooming house, and failing to maintain a fire detection system in a rooming house, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number twelve, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Terence Sullivan, J.; verdict and judgments of guilty of failing to provide a fire alarm system in a rooming house, and failing to maintain a fire detection system in a rooming house, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain, Geographical Area Number Twelve (Connecticut), which was entered upon a jury verdict finding him guilty of failing to provide a fire alarm system in a rooming house and failing to maintain a fire detection system in a rooming house.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the owner of three rooming houses. The local fire marshal conducted an inspection of the properties pursuant to Conn. Gen. DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of interfering with an officer, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a, and the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury (Connecticut) entered a judgment on the verdict. Defendant sought review of the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Two police officers were dispatched to a housing development to respond to a domestic dispute. Defendant's brother was involved in the dispute. The officers wrestled him to the ground and, while they were attempting to handcuff him, defendant placed one of the officers in a choke hold and pulled him backward. Defendant was subsequently found guilty of interfering with an officer. The court reversed defendant's conviction, finding that the trial court's jury instruction on the offense of interfering with an officer relieved the state of its burden of proving that defendant acted with the requisite specific intent. Accordingly, the court concluded that defendant was denied the presumption of innocence and that her due process rights had been violated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter for a new trial.

State v. Lang


No. 8559


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


23 Conn. App. 272; 580 A.2d 71; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 327


April 30, 1990, Argued  
September 18, 1990, Decided  
September 18, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of lobster fishing while his license was under suspension, with seven counts of the crime of stealing lobsters and with two counts of the crime of fishing lobster pots without biodegradable escape vents, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex and tried to the court, D. Dorsey, J.; judgment of guilty of lobster fishing while his license was under suspension, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut), which convicted him of lobstering while his commercial fishing license was under suspension in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 26-61(d).


OVERVIEW: While his commercial fishing license was suspended, conservation officers saw defendant and another man engage in lobstering activities on defendant's boat. Defendant claimed that his activities were authorized by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 26-142a(a) in that he was assisting a licensed fisherman. The trial court found that defendant was not acting as a mere assistant, but was in joint control of the boat with the other man. The court held that there was ample evidence to conclude that defendant was in control of the lobstering activities. The definition of § 26-142a was not vague and without standards for enforcement, and defendant was not without fair notice that his activities would not qualify as assisting. The court found no unconstitutional vagueness in the provisions of § 26-61(d) or 26-142a(a), and no unconstitutional conflict in the statutory scheme. One who had his fishing license suspended could never, during the period of suspension, be classified as one "not licensed" for the purposes of the assistant exception in § 26-142a(a). Defendant was not an unlicensed person; he was a person with a suspended license and did not, therefore, come within the exemption of § 26-142a(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.
