State v. Slater


No. 8258


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


23 Conn. App. 221; 579 A.2d 591; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 317


June 12, 1990, Argued  
September 11, 1990, Decided  
September 11, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Byrne, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a verdict and judgment of guilty from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut) of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his conviction. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of the rape shield laws was unpreserved. The court refused to review of the claim because it was a challenge to the constitutionality of an action of the legislature and not a challenge to an action of a trial court. Therefore, the court concluded that defendant was not entitled to review. Further, the court ruled that defendant was not clearly deprived of a fair trial. The court held that the trial court properly excluded the offered evidence of the victim's prior complaints of sexual assault. The court found that defendant failed to establish that either of the victim's other complaints were false because the man in the first complaint pleaded guilty and the second case was still pending. Therefore, the evidence was irrelevant and properly excluded. Moreover, the court ruled that the trial court properly allowed the State to file a second substitute information after the close of evidence but before the start of counsels' arguments to the jury because it did not prejudice defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that found defendant guilty of sexual assault in the first degree.

State v. Tuszynski


No. 8212


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


23 Conn. App. 201; 579 A.2d 1100; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 324


April 6, 1990, Argued  
September 11, 1990, Decided  
September 11, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crime of burglary in the third degree, and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with burglary in the third degree and larceny in the fourth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, geographical area number nineteen, where the cases were consolidated and presented to the court, McWeeny, J., on a plea of guilty; judgments of guilty thereafter, the court, granted the defendant's motion for modification of sentence, and the state, upon granting of permission, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut) that modified a five-year sentence previously imposed on defendant for defendant's conviction for burglary in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-102, burglary in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-103, and larceny in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-124.


OVERVIEW: After defendant pleaded guilty and was convicted burglary in the second degree, burglary in the third degree, and larceny in the third degree, defendant was sentenced to a total effective sentence of five years. The trial court subsequently granted defendant's modification request and reduced the period of incarceration to time served and increased the probation period to three years. The State's motion for reconsideration was denied. The court reversed, holding that defendant's sentence was not illegal because he was not prejudiced by the clerk's failure to give written notice of defendant's right to apply for sentence review, as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-195. Defendant's sentence was clearly legal at the time it was imposed in that it was within the permissible range for the crimes charged. The jurisdiction of the trial court terminated when the sentence was imposed. Because the sentence was for more than three years, the modification statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-39, was not applicable. The trial court had no jurisdiction to modify or correct defendant's original sentence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the modification of defendant's sentence.

State v. Santiago


No. 8555


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


22 Conn. App. 683; 578 A.2d 668; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 286


June 13, 1990, Argued  
August 21, 1990, Decided  
August 21, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of hindering prosecution and two counts each of the crimes of interfering with an officer and failure to assist a peace officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Vasington, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of the crime of failure to assist a peace officer, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which convicted him on two counts of failure to assist a peace officer in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167b(a) after the trial court allowed the State to amend its information on the morning of trial by adding these two counts.


OVERVIEW: Police officers saw a suspect run into defendant's apartment. Defendant refused to admit the officers, telling them that he needed to calm the suspect. The suspect escaped. Defendant was charged with hindering prosecution and interference with a peace officer but was only convicted of failure to assist in violation of § 53a-167b(a). Defendant's due process rights were not violated by these counts being added on trial day. Under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 623, additions were allowed prior to trial, and criminal trials did not begin until voir dire. Defendant's sole theory against the other charges was that he was actually assisting the officers, and this defense was relevant to the added charges. Defendant's record was not adequate to review his claim that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167b(a) was vague and overbroad. The trial court did not err in refusing to read U.S. Const. amend. IV to the jury because defendant's liberty guarantees were not at issue according to his defense. The jury could have found that the officers were authorized to demand assistance because they were entitled to enter private premises when in hot pursuit of a fleeing felon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on two counts of failure to assist a peace officer.

State v. Monar


No. 7397


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


22 Conn. App. 567; 579 A.2d 104; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 278


May 1, 1990, Argued  
August 14, 1990, Decided  
August 14, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of a narcotic substance with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, transporting a narcotic substance with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and conspiracy to violate the dependency producing drug law, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of conspiracy to violate the dependency producing drug law, from which the defendant appealed to this court; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to correct her sentence, and the defendant filed an amended appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted her of conspiracy to violate the dependency producing drug law in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-48.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of conspiracy to violate the dependency producing drug law in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-48. Defendant appealed, challenging the denial of her motion for judgment of acquittal and the denial of her motion to correct sentence. On appeal, defendant claimed that: (1) the trial court did not instruct the jury on the elements of the substantive offenses when giving instructions on the conspiracy charge; (2) the wording of the conspiracy charge failed to advise her adequately of the nature and cause of the accusations against her; (3) remarks by the state's attorney during closing argument deprived her of a fair trial; (4) the court should not have admitted evidence of a sum of money found in the defendant's purse; (5) the third count of the substitute information was fatally defective because it charged three offenses in the disjunctive; and (6) the trial court should not have denied her motion to correct sentence. The court rejected all of defendant's arguments on appeal and affirmed the conviction. The court held that if the jury was confused, that confusion could have only benefitted the defendant by making her conviction less likely.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Riley v. Bridgeport


No. 7681


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


22 Conn. App. 402; 577 A.2d 1099; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 246


May 9, 1990, Argued  
July 24, 1990, Decided  
July 24, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a writ of mandamus to compel the defendant to place the plaintiff on a permanent civil service roster, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Jacobson, J.; judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which denied a writ of mandamus to direct appellee city to place the employee on the permanent civil service roster. The denial also covered the employee's alternative request to enjoin the city from compelling her to take the civil service examination.


OVERVIEW: The employee was an accounting clerk and her status was changed to provisional civil service employee. She signed a provisional declaration sheet acknowledging that her provisional appointment had to be approved by the civil service commission, and that her employment was terminable either upon the establishment of an appropriate examination list or at the discretion of the appointing authority. The employee was notified that she would be terminated unless she met the certification requirements after taking the open competitive examination for the accounting clerk I position. The trial court denied the employee's writ of mandamus to direct the city to place her on the permanent civil service roster, or in the alternative request to enjoin the city from compelling her to take the civil service examination either permanently or until a final decision was rendered on her pending arbitration. The court held that the employee failed to establish that she has a clear legal right to circumvent the competitive examination procedures. The court noted that the policy behind competitive civil service examinations was to fill positions on the basis of merit and fitness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied a writ of mandamus to direct the city to place the employee on the permanent civil service roster. The denial also covered the employee's alternative request to enjoin the city from compelling her to take the civil service examination.

 

1123 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Fleischman v. Connecticut Bd. of Examiners in Podiatry


Nos. 7407, 7752


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


22 Conn. App. 193; 576 A.2d 1308; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 230


January 3, 1990, Argued  
July 3, 1990, Decided  
July 3, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal in the first case from a decision by the named defendant suspending the plaintiff's license to practice podiatry, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Wagner, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.

Appeal in the second case from a decision by the named defendant suspending the plaintiff's license to practice podiatry, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Wagner, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff podiatrist appealed judgments of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which upheld two separate suspensions of his license by defendant Connecticut Board of Examiners in Podiatry.


OVERVIEW: In each of two separate hearings, the Board suspended the podiatrist's license. In his appeal, the podiatrist claimed that the Board abused its discretion by ignoring the testimony of his expert witness and that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-59 constituted an unlawful delegation of legislative authority. The court rejected both arguments and affirmed the judgments. Because the Board was made up of experts, it was permitted to disregard the testimony of an expert witness if it wished to do so. The court held that the podiatrist failed to meet his burden of establishing the unconstitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-59 beyond a reasonable doubt. Legislative power could be delegated so long as the statute declared a legislative policy, established primary standards for carrying it out, or laid down an intelligible principle to which an administrative body had to conform. The court held that the standards set out in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-59 for the discipline of podiatrists were not constitutionally defective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments.

 

1124 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Downey v. Retirement Bd. of Waterbury


No. 8130


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


22 Conn. App. 172; 576 A.2d 582; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 208


February 7, 1990, Argued  
June 26, 1990, Decided  
June 26, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the named defendant denying the plaintiff's application to be reinstated to his former position with the Waterbury fire department, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the court, Hartmere, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a city's retirement board, appealed the judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which reversed the board's decision denying the application of plaintiff, a firefighter, to be removed form the board's disability pension rolls and to be reinstated to his former position pursuant to City of Waterbury, Conn., Charter and Related Laws § 2746.


OVERVIEW: Nearly five years after the board granted a firefighter a disability pension on the basis of the firefighter's heart condition, the firefighter applied to be removed from the disability rolls and to be reinstated to his former position. The board denied the application, but the trial court reversed the board's decision. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and held that the trial court properly found that the firefighter was aggrieved by the board's decision because the decision caused the firefighter to lose his life insurance policy, to become unable to obtain medical insurance, and to be deprived of his career employment. The firefighter presented uncontroverted medical evidence from three doctors that he was not disabled. Thus, under City of Waterbury, Conn., Charter and Related Laws § 2746, the firefighter had a right to be reinstated. The 1962 civil service amendment in the 1962 Home Rule Act referendum to the city's charter (1962 civil service amendment) was enacted before the amendments to City of Waterbury, Conn., Charter and Related Laws § 2746 and did not cover retirements. Thus, § 2746 was not implicitly repealed by the 1962 civil service amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which reversed a city's retirement board's decision denying a firefighter's application to be removed from the board's disability pension rolls and to be reinstated to his former position.

Schaghticoke Indians of Kent, Inc. v. Potter


No. 7919


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


22 Conn. App. 229; 577 A.2d 719; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 233


November 2, 1989, Argued  
May 16, 1990, Decided  
May 16, 1990, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from continuing a logging operation on the plaintiff's Indian reservation and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where the court, Pickett, J., granted the motion by the state of Connecticut et al. to intervene; thereafter, the court rendered judgment dismissing the action as to the defendant Alan Russell, and the intervening plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervening plaintiff state challenged the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut), which rendered judgment dismissing an action to enjoin a logging operation on plaintiff Indian tribe's reservation as to defendant tribal chief. The action alleged that a contract for the sale of timber between defendant logger and the tribal chief had resulted in substantial damage to the tribal reservation.


OVERVIEW: The tribal chief's motion to dismiss contended that the trial court lacked civil jurisdiction over an Indian tribal dispute. The trial court granted the motion and characterized the dispute as concerning whether the tribal chief was actually the chief, with authority to enter into contracts on behalf of the Indian tribe. The Indian tribe, however, did not deny in its complaint that he was the tribal chief, but alleged only that, as chief, he failed to obtain the consent and approval of the tribal counsel before entering into the contract. The court reasoned that the basis of the state's statutory rights and obligations to manage tribal lands and to recover misappropriated tribal property, were civil-regulatory in nature and, therefore, were preempted and rendered invalid by federal law. The court dismissed the state's appeal, holding that it followed that the state lacked aggrieved party status because it did not derive a recognizable interest in this case.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the state's appeal, which challenged the dismissal of the tribal chief as a defendant in the action brought by the Indian tribe to enjoin a logging operation on the reservation.

State v. Tirado

Appellate Court of Connecticut


21 Conn. App. 449; 574 A.2d 252; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 143


September 13, 1989, Argued  
May 8, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of injury or risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before McKeever, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which found him guilty of two counts of risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the female victim's paternal uncle. For a period of two years, there was a continuing course of sexual conduct between defendant and the victim in the victim's home. The victim claimed that defendant first began touching her sexually when she was less than nine years old. Defendant was tried and found guilty of two counts of risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21. Defendant appealed and the court affirmed. The court held that evidence of his prior sexual misconduct with his victim was admissible to prove a pattern of criminal activity, and that the probative value of such evidence outweighed its prejudicial effect. The court found that the evidence was admissible for the limited purpose of showing defendant's pattern of criminal sexual activity with the victim. The court held that while the statute of limitations protected defendant against prosecution for crimes committed beyond its reach, it did not serve as a limitation on the admissibility of otherwise admissible evidence probative of a course of criminal activity with the victim.


OUTCOME: The court found no error and affirmed the decision of the lower court, which found defendant guilty of two counts of risk of injury to a child.

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of larceny in the fifth degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-125a and of being a persistent larceny offender in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(c). OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court wrongfully intervened in the prosecutorial function and that the trial court instigated the original Part B persistent offender information in retaliation for defendant's refusal to accept a coercive plea bargain. Defendant also asserted that the trial court improperly put defendant to plea on the original information in violation of Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 647. The court affirmed the judgment, finding no error. The court found no trace in the record of any instigative or vindictive conduct by the trial court. Although the court agreed that defendant should not have been put to plea on the original Part B information, the court found that defendant was not prejudiced or unfairly surprised by the violation because ultimately the State proceeded before a different trial judge under a substitute Part B information about which defendant was properly advised. The court held that the trial court did not err by permitting the State to file the substitute Part B information because defendant did not move to strike the substitute information. Finally, the court rejected defendant's contention that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(h) was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of larceny and of being a persistent larceny offender.

Sweet v. Sumnerbrook Mill Dev. Corp.


Nos. 5793, 5794


Appellate Court of Connecticut


21 Conn. App. 191; 572 A.2d 385; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 98

April 10, 1990, Decided

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff creditor appealed the order from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex (Connecticut), which granted defendant corporation's motion to dissolve ex parte prejudgment real estate attachments against real property it had transferred to defendant wife of the corporation's president. The creditor claimed that the trial court erred in finding that the evidence was insufficient to support his claim of fraudulent conveyance.


OVERVIEW: The creditor filed a successful action for an ex parte prejudgment real estate attachment on a condominium, alleging that the corporation was indebted to him and that it and the wife of the corporation's president conspired to have the corporation transfer property to her in order to avoid certain debts to him. The corporation then successfully sought to dissolve the attachments. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the corporation had presented evidence that the wife paid the corporation $ 65,000 for the property and that she took the property subject to a mechanic's lien in the amount of $ 20,000. Further, the corporation showed that the condominium had suffered $ 1000 in water damage from a leaking sprinkler and was missing appliances worth approximately $ 1000. The creditor presented no witnesses; he merely rested on the affidavits filed with his ex parte action. The court concluded that the creditor had failed to sustain his burden of showing that either the corporation had conveyed the property for less than substantial consideration and was thereby rendered unable to pay the alleged debts or that the conveyance was made with a fraudulent intent that the wife shared.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting the corporation's motion to dissolve attachments to certain real estate it had transferred to the wife of its president.

Leoni v. Water Pollution Control Authority


No. 7823


Appellate Court of Connecticut


21 Conn. App. 77; 571 A.2d 153; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 78


January 2, 1990, Argued  
March 20, 1990, Decided

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant water pollution control authority challenged a ruling from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield (Connecticut), which granted the motion for summary judgment of plaintiff property owner and declared a certificate of taking filed by the authority a nullity. Plaintiff property owner had filed a declaratory judgment action against the authority seeking a declaration that the certificate of taking was null and void.


OVERVIEW: A town drained a certain highway runoff through a drainage swale located on the condemnees property, and then installed sewer lines along the highway, causing the flow of water onto the property to increase. The authority later instituted a condemnation proceeding to obtain and pay for the right to increase the water flow on the land, and the condemnees appealed from the statement of compensation to determine the fair market value of their land. Then, the condemnees filed a declaratory judgment action for a declaration that the certificate of condemnation was invalid. OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's ruling, which had granted the summary judgment motion of the property owner and declared the authority's certificate of taking null and void.

Ossen v. Wanat


No. 7575


Appellate Court of Connecticut


21 Conn. App. 40; 571 A.2d 134; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 71

March 13, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Summary process action, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Housing Session at Meriden, and tried to the court, Gaffney, J.; judgment awarding possession to the plaintiff; thereafter, the court awarded costs and attorney's fees to the plaintiff, and the defendants appealed to this court; subsequently, the court, Ripley, J., denied a motion for exemption from judgment filed by Laura Ellis, and the defendants filed an amended appeal.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tenants appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven, Housing Session at Meriden (Connecticut), which awarded possession to plaintiff owner and awarded costs and attorney's fees to the owner.


OVERVIEW: The owner and one of the tenants entered into a written lease agreement for a lot in a mobile home park. The owner served the tenants with a notice to quit, terminating an alleged oral month-to-month agreement. Thereafter, the owner filed a summary process action in the superior court, alleging termination of the oral lease and demanding immediate possession. The superior court entered judgment awarding possession to the owner and taxed costs and expenses in favor of the owner because of the tenants' weak case and abusive pleadings. The tenants appealed. The record also contained ample evidence from which the superior court could reasonably have concluded that the parties began an oral month-to-month tenancy at the termination of their written lease. The court held that the tenants did not have the right, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21-79, 21-80(b)(1)(A), or 21-80(b)(4), to sell their mobile home to pay rent arrearages once the summary process began.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the superior court's judgment.

In re John C.


No. 7549


Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 694; 569 A.2d 1154; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 49


December 15, 1989, Argued  
February 20, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to adjudicate the defendant to be a delinquent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Juvenile Matters at Hartford, and tried to the court, Brenneman, J.; judgment adjudicating the defendant to be a delinquent, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain, Juvenile Matters at Hartford (Connecticut), which found him to be delinquent for having committed the offense of risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21. Defendant claimed that the statute was unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts of his case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was 13, was discovered in a bedroom with his penis exposed, attempting to have an eight year old girl whom his mother baby-sat perform oral sex on him. Although sexual assault charges were dismissed, evidence showed that defendant's penis touched her lips. The court found that the phrase "any person" contained in Conn. Gen. State v. Aleksiewicz

Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 643; 569 A.2d 567; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 36

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Maloney, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) convicted defendant of robbery in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4). The defendant appealed, challenging the sufficiency of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: After the victim withdrew money from an automated teller machine, defendant approached the victim and said, "Give me that money or you're dead." The court found that the victim offered no testimony to show that a firearm was used or that the victim pretended to use a firearm. The court held that the evidence was insufficient to support a conviction for robbery in the first degree, which required the use of a firearm. The court found that the evidence warranted a modification of the judgment to the lesser charge of robbery in the third degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-136. In rejecting defendant's other claims, the court found that defendant's statements subsequent to the alleged criminal act were admissible to show consciousness of guilt. The court found no error in the consciousness of guilt instruction because it did not unconstitutionally shift the State's burden of proof. The court held that the trial court's decision to admit the photo array did not violate defendant's due process rights; an array composed of different individuals necessarily contained differences.


OUTCOME: The court found error in part. The court set aside the judgment of conviction of robbery in the first degree. The court remanded the case to the trial court with direction to render a judgment of conviction of robbery in the third degree and to resentence defendant accordingly.

State v. Steinmann


No. 7665


Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 599; 569 A.2d 557; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 25


November 16, 1989, Argued  
January 30, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute informations charging the defendant with simple trespass, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, geographical area number eighteen, and tried to the court, Moraghan, J.; judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Litchfield Superior Court (Connecticut), which convicted him of simple trespass pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §53a-110a.


OVERVIEW: A conflict arose between defendant and the church. Because defendant allegedly was bothering women parishioners and using the church for personal meetings, the church asked him to stop attending church services. Three times, defendant attended church services and was issued a misdemeanor summons for criminal trespass. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that defendant's claim that the evidence was insufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he had the requisite knowledge that he was not licensed to enter church property was without merit. Defendant entered the church property as a knowing trespasser. Defendant had been unequivocally informed and understood that his privilege to attend church services had been revoked. A business invitee could be charged with simple trespass in areas open to the public as long as there was evidence that he entered with knowledge that he was not privileged to do so. The State could discriminate between simple and criminal trespass because there was some natural and substantial difference germane to the subject and purposes of the legislation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision convicting defendant of simple trespass.

 

1135 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ryerson


No. 7257


Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 572; 570 A.2d 709; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 24


October 18, 1989, Argued  
January 30, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Hendel, J., rendered judgment revoking the defendant's probation; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to correct an illegal sentence, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial by the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London (Connecticut) of his motion to correct an illegal sentence, which he alleged arose out of the trial court's revocation of his probation pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-32. He argued that the trial court exceeded its statutory authority and violated his federal due process rights and his double jeopardy rights under the state and federal constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The effect of the resentencing by the probation revocation sentencing court was that defendant had to serve 16 years in prison. On appeal, the court held that the revocation sentencing court had the statutory authority to impose a sentence for the underlying offense that ran consecutive to the sentence for intervening offense of robbery. The revocation sentencing court was neither limited to the imposition of a concurrent sentence nor prevented from imposing a longer effective sentence than originally could have been imposed. Because defendant raised the issue for the first time on appeal, his claim that his state double jeopardy rights were violated by the procedure could not be considered. Further, the doctrine of double jeopardy did not apply to revocation proceedings. Defendant's federal due process rights were not violated; his original 10 year sentence was reimposed, not a more severe sentence. Further, the revocation sentencing court did not act vindictively. Although defendant's claim that his due process rights were violated by the consideration of erroneous information was reviewable, he had not shown that the revocation sentencing court relied on that information.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the proceedings.

State v. Sinclair


No. 7293


Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 586; 569 A.2d 551; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 429


October 12, 1989, Argued  
January 30, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of burglary in the second degree and larceny in the fourth degree, and, in the second part, with being a persistent serious felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Gormley, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a plea of guilty of being a persistent serious felony offender; judgment of guilty, and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of burglary in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-102 and larceny in the fourth degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-125. Defendant also challenged a judgment that convicted him of being a persistent serious felony offender in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(b).


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of burglary in the second degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-102 and larceny in the fourth degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-125, and the trial court convicted him of being a persistent serious felony offender under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(b). On appeal, the court found no error in the judgments. The court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying a motion to strike the testimony of the victim because of the State's failure to produce her statement. The provisions of Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 752 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-86b applied to the tape recording, but the State's routine mishandling of the tape was not tantamount to bad faith and defendant's case was not prejudiced by its loss. The court determined that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for a mistrial and his request for a curative instruction because the State's remarks during closing argument did not shift the burden of proof. The court concluded that the trial court's jury instructions on circumstantial evidence adequately conveyed the requirement that the essential facts had to be proved beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment that convicted defendant of burglary in the second degree and larceny in the fourth degree or the judgment that convicted him of being a persistent serious felony offender.

 

1137 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


In re Grand Jury Investigation by Schaller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 447; 567 A.2d 1255; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 1


September 19, 1989, Argued  
January 2, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application for disclosure of the finding, transcripts and records of a certain grand jury investigation, brought to the investigatory grand jury panel, which denied the application, and the petitioner filed a petition for review with this court.



DISPOSITION: Further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inspector sought a judgment by the court (Connecticut) for the disclosure of the finding, transcripts, and records of a certain grand jury investigation, so that he could defend himself from defendant's lawsuit, and answer defendant's motion for disclosure and production. The inspector applied to the grand jury panel for the release of the documents, but was refused without a hearing or an explanation.


OVERVIEW: The inspector petitioned the court for the disclosure of grand jury records, findings, and transcripts so that he could defendant himself against defendant's lawsuit. The inspector initially applied to the grand jury panel, but was refused without either a hearing or an explanation. The court noted that the inspector raised the issue of which amendment to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-47 governed his petition, the standard for release of the transcripts, and in the event of release the conditions of release. The court noted that the standard of release was embodied in 1985 Conn. Acts 611, § 6. The court found that the grand jury panel, by majority vote, could disclose its finding and record when such disclosure was deemed to have been in the public interest. The court found that the determination of whether to disclose findings and documents was left to the grand jury panel. The court noted that the grand jury panel was in a better position to determine what public interest required regarding the inspector's petition because of its prior familiarity with the judicial inquiry ordered by it, and remanded the petition for a determination of whether the public interest required disclosure.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the inspector's petition to the grand jury panel for a determination of whether disclosure was in the public interest.

State v. De Martin


No. 6980


Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 430; 568 A.2d 1034; 1990 Conn. App. LEXIS 3


October 20, 1989, Argued  
January 2, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of manslaughter in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before S. Freedman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of manslaughter in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of manslaughter in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-56(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Two groups became embroiled in a series of altercations at a bar. When the victim started toward a melee that included defendant's sister, defendant struck him with a pool cue. Defendant claimed that he was justified in using force to defend his sister. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred in its charge to the jury on justified physical force in defense of a third person as defined by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-19 by incorrectly defining "initial aggressor" so as to eliminate defendant's justification if the jurors found that the victim had threatened imminent physical harm but defendant had been the first to strike a blow. Defendant failed to file a relevant request to charge and failed to object to the charge as given. The court held that defendant's claim of an erroneous jury instruction was not truly of constitutional proportions, and that the instructions as a whole fairly presented the case to the jury so that no injustice was done to defendant's legal rights. The court also declined to review the unpreserved claim under the doctrine of plain error, finding that the definition of initial aggressor did not result in an unreliable verdict.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

State v. Spears


No. 7117


Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 410; 567 A.2d 1245; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 377


October 17, 1989, Argued  
December 26, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and accessory to murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Gaffney, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree as an accessory, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Waterbury District (Connecticut), which convicted him of manslaughter in the first degree as an accessory.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a friend killed the friend's mother to help fund their crack habit. Defendant was charged with murder and accessory to murder and was convicted of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree as an accessory pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-8. He appealed on various grounds. The court affirmed, holding that defendant's challenge to a jury instruction regarding presumption of innocence, which was not raised at trial, failed to reach constitutional proportions for purposes of review. The instruction that the law was made to protect society and the innocent and not the guilty did not dilute the presumption of innocence because it was used in conjunction with a clear instruction both as to the presumption of innocence and as to the duty of the state to prove beyond a reasonable doubt defendant's guilt. Defendant's challenge to another jury instruction, also not raised at trial, failed because he simply put a constitutional label on a nonconstitutional claim. The court evaluated the questioned jury instruction in context and found it to be proper. The court did not disturb the sentence because it was within statutory limits and had a reasonable basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Vaughn


No. 7890


Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 386; 567 A.2d 392; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 372


October 17, 1989, Argued  
December 19, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of sale of heroin by a person who is not drug-dependent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of the sale of heroin. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in permitting the State to file an amended information deleting the language that the sale was made by a person who was not drug-dependent after the defense had rested and immediately prior to closing arguments.


OVERVIEW: Defendant offered to sell heroin to an undercover officer. The officer purchased the heroin, initialed and dated the packet, and had it field-tested. The officer identified defendant's picture from a photo array. Defendant was subsequently arrested and charged with the sale of heroin by a person who is not drug-dependent. The defense rested its case without presenting evidence on the issue of drug dependency. Prior to closing arguments, at the request of the trial court, the State filed an amended information that deleted the reference to a person who was not drug-dependent. Defendant was convicted of the sale of heroin. In affirming on appeal, the court held that: (1) where both the original and amended information charged defendant with the sale of heroin in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b) and the deletion of any reference to defendant's drug-dependency did not change the offense, defendant was not deprived of his right to fair notice of the charge; and (2) the prosecutor did not abuse his discretion by charging defendant with a violation of § 21a-278(b) to obtain a harsher sentence instead of charging him under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(b), sale of narcotics.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the trial court, which convicted defendant of sale of heroin.

State v. Kennedy


No. 7012


Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 354; 567 A.2d 841; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 374


October 6, 1989, Argued  
December 19, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of larceny in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Purtill, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London (Connecticut) of larceny in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-122(a)(2). On appeal, he argued that the trial court erred in denying his two amended motions to suppress, in admitting the testimony of an incompetent witness regarding the value of the items allegedly stolen, and in denying his motion for judgment of acquittal.


OVERVIEW: Acting pursuant to a search warrant, two teams of police entered defendant's father's home trying to find defendant relative to outstanding charges. While looking for him, the police found and seized certain items related to a recent museum break-in. On appeal, the court noted that the State conceded that defendant had standing to raise the issues. The court agreed that defendant had shown that his subjective expectation of privacy in the basement garage of his father's home was reasonable and was an expectation that society would also recognize as reasonable. But, the court held that there was no clear error in the trial court's factual findings that one team of police officers, entering the house through a basement garage, had found in plain view the items seized before they learned that defendant, hiding in the attic of the home, had been located by the other team. A museum docent was properly allowed to testify as to the value of stolen museum artifacts; she was properly qualified and her reliance on an inventory for details about the artifacts was proper. The State met its burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that the value of the artifacts exceeded $ 10,000.


OUTCOME: The court found no reversible error.

State v. Middleton


No. 7208


Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 321; 566 A.2d 1363; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 369


October 17, 1989, Argued  
December 12, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Informations charging each defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics, possession of drug paraphernalia in a drug factory situation, use of drug paraphernalia and possession of a controlled substance, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number thirteen, where the cases were consolidated; thereafter, the court, Susco, J., following a probable cause hearing, rendered judgment dismissing the charges against the defendants, from which the state, on granting of permission, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain, Geographical Area Number Thirteen, that dismissed the informations brought against defendants. The dismissals were based on a finding that no probable cause to arrest defendants had existed. The trial court made the dismissals at a preliminary hearing.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the trial court had applied the exclusionary rule to suppress evidence and make a dismissal based on that suppression at a preliminary hearing conducted pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Sup. Ct. § 650. The court ruled that the trial court had erred by considering in a hearing held via § 650 whether or not the evidence had been procured as the result of an unreasonable search and seizure. A motion to suppress evidence required a constitutional adjudication, and a hearing conducted via § 650 could be ex parte and was not an adversarial hearing. The court rejected the argument that the State had waived its right to an adversarial proceeding on the suppression of evidence. The court found that the trial court had not told the State that it was making the probable-cause hearing into a suppression hearing. On a separate jurisdictional issue, the court rejected the contention that the State had failed to comply with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-96.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the State and against defendants, the court found error and set aside the trial court's judgment of dismissal and remanded the cases for further proceedings.

 

1143 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


No. 7111


Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 271; 566 A.2d 436; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 359


October 18, 1989, Argued  
November 28, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of larceny in the second degree and assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number thirteen, and tried to the jury before Klaczak, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of larceny in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain, Geographical Area Number Thirteen (Connecticut) convicting him of larceny in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-123. Defendant argued that an out-of-court identification and an officer's opinion testimony were improperly admitted and that his requested jury charge on eyewitness identification was denied in error.


OVERVIEW: The victim could not immediately identify the man who snatched her purse from a photo array because she was so upset. She was later shown the same array with two additional pictures and calmed down enough to identify defendant as the perpetrator. The inclusion of defendant's photograph in two arrays viewed eight days apart was not impermissibly suggestive. Police did not visually, verbally, or demonstratively emphasize defendant's photograph. The trial court properly did not reach the reliability of the identification procedure. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing an officer to testify about the comparative reliability of crime victims' identifications because it was opinion testimony based on her professional experience. Defendant's failure to object to the State's further questioning of the officer did not preserve any alleged error for review and defendant's point of error was not of constitutional proportion to merit review of the unpreserved claim. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's requested charge on the reliability of eyewitness identifications because the trial court's instructions adequately covered the dangers of misidentification.


OUTCOME: There was no error.

State v. Tappin


No. 7075


Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 241; 566 A.2d 709; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 351


September 14, 1989, Argued  
November 21, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of narcotics, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Cretella, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven, Geographical Area Number Six (Connecticut) convicting defendant of possession of a narcotic substance in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(a). Defendant cited error in a peremptory challenge of a black venireperson and a jury charge on reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court's failure to compel the State to articulate a nondiscriminatory reason for its peremptory challenge of a black venire person violated his rights to equal protection and an impartial jury under U.S. Const. amend. VI, XI ,and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 20. The court conducted a Batson inquiry to determine whether the trial court could reasonably conclude that defendant failed to make a prima facie showing of discriminatory abuse of the challenge. The State conducted voir dire of nine panelists before questioning a black venire person, who was asked the same questions as other venire persons but gave equivocal or confused answers. While the first Batson factor was satisfied, i.e., the defendant was black and the State exercised a peremptory challenge to remove a him, the record did not support a reasonable inference that the State exercised the challenge for a racially discriminatory purpose. Defendant's claim that the jury charge on reasonable doubt was overly beneficial to the State was not reviewed because defendant's trial objection was imprecise and because the claim the claim was not of constitutional proportion.


OUTCOME: There was no error.

State v. Blackwell


No. 7037


Appellate Court of Connecticut


20 Conn. App. 193; 565 A.2d 549; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 338


September 13, 1989, Argued  
October 31, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a) and sexual assault in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant sexually assaulted a 15-year-old boy who frequented an amusement arcade where defendant was employed. The court held that first and second degree sexual assault were separate crimes for which defendant could be prosecuted and punished without violating the prohibition against double jeopardy. Defendant did not show that the legislature intended that sexual assault in the first degree and sexual assault in the second degree be two crimes, nominally distinct for which only one penalty could be imposed. The trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress pornographic materials seized when executing a search warrant for a knife where the materials, found in a drawer in a night table next to defendant's bed, were discovered inadvertently during a legal search. The seizure was lawful under the plain view doctrine because the police did not know that pornographic material was in the night table and went there intending to seize it, using the search warrant for the knife as a subterfuge, and the material was relevant to the charge of injury or risk of injury to a child.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

The conviction arose in connection with certain sexual acts allegedly perpetrated against his older daughter.

State v. Lamme


No. 7108


Appellate Court of Connecticut


19 Conn. App. 594; 563 A.2d 1372; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 303


May 9, 1989, Argued  
September 5, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and operating a motor vehicle with a suspended driver's license, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before Geen, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in a jury trial before the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227(a) and operating a motor vehicle with a suspended driver's license in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-215(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was asked to leave the lobby of a hotel by a policeman. Shortly thereafter, defendant was stopped by another officer for driving in the dark without headlights. That officer administered a field sobriety test, which defendant failed. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in failing to suppress the evidence derived from the roadside sobriety test, in admitting certain opinion testimony, and in instructing the jury on reasonable doubt. The court disagreed, holding that: (1) the police legally detained defendant on a reasonable suspicion that he was driving under the influence; (2) the roadside sobriety test, which did not involve long delay or unreasonable intrusion, was justified by that reasonable suspicion; (3) the expert testimony of the officer who administered the field sobriety test was not inadmissible as an opinion regarding an issue of ultimate fact because it was based in great part on knowledge and skill beyond the ken of the average juror and was helpful to the jury; (4) the lay opinion testimony of the officer in the hotel lobby was admissible because it was limited to the issue of intoxication; and (5) the reasonable doubt instruction was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

State v. Redente

Appellate Court of Connecticut


19 Conn. App. 521; 563 A.2d 1365; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 279


June 19, 1989, Argued  
August 29, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of violation of election laws and one count of the crime of larceny in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Quinn, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) of receiving cash contributions, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 9-348k(9), 9-348l (1983), and one count of larceny in the third degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-124(a)(1), 53a-121, 53a-119(1). On appeal, he argued, inter alia, an election law expert was improperly allowed to testify on the ultimate issues and checks payable to cash were not cash contributions.


OVERVIEW: As defendant, representing an incumbent mayor up for reelection, returned contributions to contributors because they had been ruled improper, he requested cash or checks payable to cash in return. On appeal, the court noted that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-335(14), (15) were not very clear and the expert's testimony was properly allowed as an aid for the jury. A tape recording of a conversation between defendant and an inspector from the State's Attorney's office was properly admitted. The court held that the denial of defendant's motion for a continuance was not error. Counsel had time to prepare a defense and no claim was made that the lack of a continuance substantially impaired his effectiveness.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

State v. Rose


No. 7118


Appellate Court of Connecticut


19 Conn. App. 423; 562 A.2d 583; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 274


June 14, 1989, Argued  
August 22, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, geographical area number three, and tried to the jury before Moraghan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction entered by the Superior Court for the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut), for robbery in the first degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-133(1), 53a-134(a)(3). Defendant contended that the trial court's instruction permitted the jury to convict him of robbery in the third degree instead of robbery in the first degree because the jury was not required to find that he used a dangerous weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice entered a taxi and defendant held the driver down while the accomplice held a knife at his throat. Defendant was charged with robbery, and the trial court charged the jury by stating the information accused defendant of committing the crime in one or two ways: by use or threatened use of a dangerous instrument and by the use of force for overcoming resistance in the taking of property. Defendant was convicted of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-133(1), 53a-134(a)(3). Defendant appealed and contended that the trial court's instruction permitted the jury to convict him of robbery in the third degree instead of robbery in the first degree because the jury was not required to find that he used a dangerous weapon. The court set aside the conviction and remanded for a new trial. The court held that the trial court improperly informed the jury that it could convict defendant on the basis of two theories, only one of which involved the use of a dangerous weapon, and there was a possibility that the state was able to gain a conviction without having to prove one of the elements of the crime charged.


OUTCOME: The court set aside defendant's conviction for robbery in the first degree and remanded for a new trial.

 

1151 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jennings


No. 6962


Appellate Court of Connecticut


19 Conn. App. 265; 562 A.2d 545; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 249


March 15, 1989, Argued  
August 1, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of cocaine with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before McKeever, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of possession of cocaine with intent to sell by a person who was not drug-dependent. Defendant argued, among other things, that the money found on his person should have been suppressed as the product of an unconstitutional search and seizure.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the police failed to articulate the specific facts that focused their general suspicion of criminal activity in the area upon him in particular. Without a specific focus to justify the investigative stop, the defendant reasoned that the money should have been suppressed. The court disagreed. The trial court expressly found that the officers were aware of various facts that satisfied the "reasonable and articulable suspicion" standard necessary to justify a Terry stop. The officers were sent to an area known for frequent narcotics sales on the basis of information that drug sales were occurring. The officers observed defendant discard a paper bag and, from their training and experience, had reason to believe the bag contained drugs. Each of these circumstances had been held to be a valid basis for assessing the reasonableness of police action. The court concluded that the facts were sufficient to justify the investigative stop. The police had probable cause to make the arrest having found what appeared to be narcotics in a bag tossed away by defendant. The search of defendant's person and the seizure of the money were incident to the lawful arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine with intent to sell by a person who was not drug-dependent.

Bleidner v. Searles


No. 6802


Appellate Court of Connecticut


19 Conn. App. 76; 561 A.2d 954; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 213


March 14, 1989, Argued  
July 11, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for a new trial on the petitioner's adjudication, pursuant to a stipulated judgment, as the father of the respondent's child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where the court, Pickett, J., rendered judgment dismissing the petition, from which the petitioner appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner alleged father appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut), which dismissed his petition for a new trial pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-270, in respondent mother's paternity action against the alleged father. Pursuant to a stipulated judgment, the alleged father was adjudicated as the biological father of the mother's child.


OVERVIEW: The mother filed a paternity action against the alleged father. Thereafter, the alleged father stipulated to paternity and agreed to provide financial support for the child. Subsequently, the alleged father signed an acknowledgement of paternity. Later, the alleged father initiated an action for a new trial. The trial court dismissed the alleged father's petition. The court found no error in the trial court's judgment of dismissal, and held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion. The court determined that the alleged father did not have an absolute right to be reheard on the issue of paternity pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-172(b) (1982). The alleged father had the opportunity to litigate the issue of paternity, but chose instead, to stipulate to a judgment that was approved by the trial court. Throughout the entire proceeding, the alleged father was represented by counsel. The court thus presumed that the alleged father was aware of the consequences of his decision. The alleged father was not deprived of a fair opportunity to have his case heard on appeal so as to constitute "reasonable cause" pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-270.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment that dismissed the alleged father's petition for a new trial.

 

1153 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Seymour Housing Authority Tenants Asso. v. Housing Authority of Seymour


No. 6322


Appellate Court of Connecticut


18 Conn. App. 393; 558 A.2d 1002; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 147


November 10, 1988, Argued  
May 16, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a judgment declaring null and void the statute that establishes criteria for determining maximum income limits for tenants of certain moderate income housing, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and tried to the court, Kulawiz, J.; judgment in part for the plaintiffs, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a public housing association and some of its members, appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut), which denied plaintiffs' request for the payment of alleged overcharges against defendant housing authority pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-72a (Rev. to 1983), although it granted plaintiffs' request to enjoin eviction proceedings.


OVERVIEW: After some members of the association received eviction notices from the housing authority, plaintiffs filed suit on grounds that the housing authority arbitrarily set the maximum allowable income limits for residence in the moderate income housing project in violation of § 8-72a and sought refunds for overcharges. The trial court enjoined the eviction proceedings after the undisputed evidence showed that the housing authority did not consider the average wage for the surrounding town in its computation of the maximum income limits as required by § 8-72a, but rejected plaintiffs' claim for an accounting. On appeal of the latter ruling, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the trial court erred because even though plaintiffs were not entitled to an accounting in its strict sense, their complaint and the evidence clearly showed that they merely sought a computation of the amount of the overcharges in aid of their claim for damages in light of the complicated formula that the housing authority was required to prepare under § 8-72a.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court, which had denied plaintiffs' request for an accounting in aid of their claim against the housing authority for a refund of overcharges paid.

Statewide Grievance Committee v. Presnick


No. 6232


Appellate Court of Connecticut


18 Conn. App. 316; 559 A.2d 220; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 137


January 3, 1989, Argued  
May 9, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Presentment of the defendant on allegations of attorney misconduct, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Purtill, J.; judgment remanding the defendant and suspending him from the practice of law for one year, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant attorney appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) that suspended him from practicing law for one year on a petition brought by plaintiff bar association grievance committee.


OVERVIEW: Upon proof that the attorney acted in a manner that reflected on his fitness to practice law in a loud and obstreperous confrontation with child protection workers near a courtroom and that he attempted to obtain an elderly client's property at a price that was $ 50,000 lower than the appraised value by misrepresenting his relationship with the client, the trial court reprimanded the attorney for the former offense and suspended him for the latter. On appeal, the attorney made many claims of error, none of which were sustained by the court. Thus, the court ruled that the attorney's challenge to the jurisdiction of the trial court on constitutional grounds was without merit; no proof of corrupt motive or evil intent was required as a prerequisite to suspending the attorney, nor was the trial court in error in failing to utilize the "beyond a reasonable doubt" standard of proof for suspension. Further, the attorney's statements to the social workers were not privileged under constitutional guarantees of free speech as attorneys were not exempt from the laws limiting speech that were applicable to all citizens, and the attorney failed to prove any impairment due to the hearing site.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment of suspension.
