State v. Rogers


Nos. 6910, 6911


Appellate Court of Connecticut


18 Conn. App. 104; 556 A.2d 1030; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 107


December 21, 1988, Argued  
April 11, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crime of possession of a narcotic substance, and information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of sale of narcotics and interfering with an officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, geographical area number five, where the court, Curran, J., granted the defendants' motions to suppress certain evidence and rendered judgments dismissing the charges, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: With the permission of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, geographical area number five (Connecticut), the State appealed that court's grant of defendants' motions to suppress certain evidence and its judgments dismissing charges of illegal possession of narcotics, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(a), illegal sale of drugs, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278, and interfering with an officer, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a.


OVERVIEW: Detectives, acting without a search warrant and without announcing that they were police officers, kicked in a door to defendants' home and secured the premises while a search warrant was being obtained. The State argued that, because the evidence had been seized after the search warrant was obtained, the inevitable discovery doctrine obviated application of the exclusionary rule. On appeal, the State asserted the independent source doctrine, another exception to the exclusionary rule. The court held that the latter claim was reviewable under the plain error doctrine, because neither the Supreme Court of Connecticut nor the court had previously had occasion to consider the independent source doctrine in the context presented. Thus, the issue was of importance to the development of the law of the state and was vital to the proper resolution of the case. But, because whether the evidence was illegally seized was, in the first instance, a factual question, which the trial court had not yet considered, and, further, because defendants had to be given a chance to challenge the validity of the search warrant, the court remanded the case to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the superior court for further proceedings in accordance with the court's opinion.

 

1156 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Daniels


No. 6407


Appellate Court of Connecticut


18 Conn. App. 134; 556 A.2d 1040; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 109


October 4, 1988, Argued  
April 11, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, conspiracy to commit sexual assault in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Sullivan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of sexual assault in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) of sexual assault in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70. On appeal, he argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in permitting the prosecutor to make improper remarks during closing argument in violation of defendant's constitutional rights to a fair trial and due process.


OVERVIEW: During the State's case-in-chief, a police officer was allowed to testify, over defendant's objection, as to defendant's failure to respond to the victim's repeated question: "Why did the both of you do this to me?" On appeal, the court held that the victim's statement carried sufficiently accusatory implications to call for a response. But, given the facts, the trial court erred in allowing the officer to testify that defendant remained silent in the face of the victim's accusation. Under the circumstances, that defendant remained silent was too unreliable as evidence of assent to the statement to be admissible as an admission by silence. However, the court held that its admission was harmless error. The court held that the trial court's failure to charge the jurors that they had to unanimously agree on whether defendant employed "use of force" or "the threat of use of force" did not violate his right to a unanimous verdict in a six-member jury trial. Because defendant failed to object to the prosecutor's remarks when they were made, and because the remarks did not deprive him of a fundamental constitutional right or a fair trial, the court did not review that claimed error.


OUTCOME: The court found no reversible error in any of the issues defendant raised.

 

1157 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Manchester v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


No. 6861


Appellate Court of Connecticut


18 Conn. App. 69; 556 A.2d 1026; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 88


January 19, 1989, Argued  
April 4, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant zoning board of appeals revoking a building permit that had been issued to the plaintiffs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, Ryan, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to the court.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which dismissed their appeal from a decision of defendant zoning board of appeals that had revoked a building permit allowing the landowners to build on a nonconforming lot that had previously been issued to them by the town zoning enforcement officer.


OVERVIEW: The landowners owned a triangular parcel of land in a residential district that was smaller than one acre. They also owned a four-acre parcel across the road from the triangular parcel. Zoning regulations adopted in 1950 provided for one-acre residential zoning, and as amended in 1970 for two-acre residential zoning. The town zoning enforcement officer found that the triangular parcel was a nonconforming lot because it had been separately owned since the zoning regulations were adopted, and he issued a building permit allowing the landowners to build on the parcel. The landowners' neighbors appealed and the zoning board reversed the enforcement officer's decision without explanation. The court held that the trial court did not err when it dismissed the landowners' appeal from the board's decision. The parcel was not owned in separate ownership when the zoning regulations were adopted, and the land records did not show the parcel as a separate lot until after the regulations were adopted and amended. Moreover, the parcel was part of the four-acre tract on the other side of the road until 1968. Accordingly, the board did not act arbitrarily, illegally, or in abuse of its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no error.

State v. Manfredi


No. 5693


Appellate Court of Connecticut


17 Conn. App. 602; 555 A.2d 436; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 61


November 7, 1988, Argued  
March 7, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Corrigan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of manslaughter in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the conviction and sentence for manslaughter in the first degree that the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) adjudged against him based upon a jury verdict.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that he was entitled to relief due to constitutional, evidentiary, instructional, and procedural errors arising from his assertion of defenses grounded mental disease or defect. The prosecution prevailed. Defendant placed his mental status in issue by filing notice of his intent to rely on defenses based upon mental disease or defect, and by his trial testimony. Defendant thereby waived his constitutional privilege against compulsory submission to psychiatric examination and exposed his mental processes to reasonable examination by the prosecution. Defendant suffered no prejudice by compulsory psychiatric examinations that he underwent before formally filing his notice of intent to rely on defenses grounded in mental disease and defect. Defendant's assertions of error in this regard were speculative and not preserved for appellate review. Defendant was properly cross-examined based upon the examining physician's testimony. Defendant did not show plain error in the trial court's jury charge regarding the uses to which the psychiatric testimony could be put. Defendant had no constitutional right to counsel's presence during the psychiatric examinations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Thompson


No. 6656


Appellate Court of Connecticut


17 Conn. App. 490; 554 A.2d 297; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 50


December 7, 1988, Argued  
February 21, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of robbery in the first degree, three counts of the crime of unlawful restraint in the first degree and with the crimes of illegal possession of a sawed-off shotgun and burglary in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Hendel, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut) of robbery in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4), unlawful restraint in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-95, possession of a sawed-off shotgun, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-211, burglary in the third degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-103(a), and of being a persistent dangerous felony offender, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to police that he was one of two persons involved in an armed robbery of a restaurant. He admitted that he was carrying a shotgun. Several witnesses confirmed parts of his confession. Defendant presented no evidence at trial. On appeal, even though he had not requested an instruction on the issue, the court reviewed for plain error his claim that the trial court erred in its jury instructions by failing to follow the mandate of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-84(b) regarding his failure to testify. The court held that there was no error. The trial court's deviation from the language of § 54-84(b) was not the type that, in the context of the entire charge, would mislead the jurors by suggesting that it was permissible for them to consider defendant's silence in deciding the case. Although the trial court's instruction concerning the jury's consideration of circumstantial evidence was erroneous, the court held that it was not reasonably possible that the jury was misled by the language, so any error was not harmful beyond a reasonable doubt. Similarly, although an instruction concerning accessory culpability was erroneous, the error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court found no error requiring reversal of defendant's convictions.

State v. Santiago


No. 6672


Appellate Court of Connecticut


17 Conn. App. 273; 552 A.2d 438; 1989 Conn. App. LEXIS 3


October 13, 1988, Argued  
January 3, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of larceny in the sixth degree and possession of narcotics with intent to sell, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the jury before Lewis, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which convicted him of possession of narcotics with intent to sell in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a).


OVERVIEW: While arresting defendant for a larceny charge, the police officer observed him hide something under the seat of his automobile. Another officer seized a quantity of drugs from under the seat. On appeal from his conviction for drug possession, defendant argued that the drugs should have been suppressed, that the evidence was insufficient to convict, and that the trial court erred in its jury instruction. In finding no error, the court ruled that the search was incident to a lawful arrest and was not limited in its scope to the evidence of the larceny. The court also ruled that, where defendant was established as the driver of the vehicle and was observed hiding something under the seat where the drugs were found, the jury could have reasonably concluded, upon the facts established and the reasonable inferences drawn therefrom, that the cumulative effect of the evidence was sufficient to justify the verdict of guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the trial court's use of the word "must" was not an improper direction to convict, because the jury instructions, read in their entirety, did not direct or advise the jury how to decide the matter.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

State v. Oliver


No. 6755


Appellate Court of Connecticut


17 Conn. App. 108; 550 A.2d 316; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 445


October 13, 1988, Argued  
November 22, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell, possession of narcotics and possession of a controlled substance, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number fourteen, and tried to a jury before Barry, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of possession of narcotics with intent to sell and possession of a controlled substance, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted him of possession of narcotics with intent to sell in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a) and possession of a controlled substance in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(c).


OVERVIEW: Based on a tip of drug activity in the area, a police officer put an apartment building under surveillance. The officer observed what appeared to him to be a drug transaction between defendant and another man. When a second officer approached in his cruiser, defendant and the other man dashed off in opposite directions prompting each police officer to chase one of them on foot. At no point did the officer command defendant to stop. During the chase, defendant dropped a pouch that was picked up by the pursuing officer. Upon being apprehended, defendant was arrested and the pouch was opened, revealing a quantity of heroin, cocaine, and marijuana. In affirming defendant's convictions, the court held that the pursuit of defendant did not constitute a seizure. The court held that, applying the reasonable person test, it could not be said that a reasonable person would feel that his liberty was restricted in any way. The court concluded that the officer's pursuit and seizure of the pouch did not violate defendant's Fourth Amendment rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

Beacon Falls v. Posick


No. 6357


Appellate Court of Connecticut


17 Conn. App. 17; 549 A.2d 656; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 431


September 14, 1988, Argued  
October 21, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from operating a private landfill, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and referred to Hon. Joseph J. Chernauskas, state trial referee; judgment for the plaintiffs, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellees filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut), which granted appellees, town and its zoning and planning commission, a permanent injunction against the landowner's operation of a private landfill in the town and ordered the landowner to pay a civil penalty, costs, and attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The landowner operated a private solid waste disposal landfill in the town pursuant to a permit from the department of environmental protection (DEP), but in violation of the town's zoning ordinance prohibiting such use of property. The court found that the trial court erred in granting the town a permanent injunction against the landowner's operation of his landfill and made the following holdings: (1) The general zoning authority granted the town by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2 did not extend to the enactment of zoning regulations that conflicted with DEP permits because the Solid Waste Management Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22a-207 through 22a-221, preempted conflicting local zoning regulations. (2) The town's ordinance was a "prohibition" on the business of operating a private landfill and went beyond the power of "regulation" conferred by § 8-2. (3) The landowner was not required to exhaust his administrative remedies by appealing to the town's zoning board of appeals because the board's jurisdiction under § 8-7 did not include determining the legality of zoning regulations.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment granting the permanent injunction against the landowner's operation of a private landfill and charging the landowner with a penalty, costs, and attorney fees. The court remanded the case to the trial court and directed it to enter judgment for the landowner.

State v. Mankus


No. 6288


Appellate Court of Connecticut


16 Conn. App. 184; 547 A.2d 84; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 349


June 9, 1988, Argued  
September 13, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the first degree and burglary in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Armentano J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of burglary in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) of burglary in the third degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-103 (Rev. to 1977). On appeal, he argued that the trial court erred in instructing the jury that it could convict him of burglary on the basis of his remaining unlawfully in a building where the State charged him with having committed the unlawful entry form of burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the instruction unconstitutionally enlarged the burglary offense as stated in the information, thereby permitting the jury to convict him on the basis of an uncharged portion of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-103 in violation of his rights under U.S. Const. amend. VI and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8. Although defendant failed to raise that claim at trial and failed to take an exception to the trial court's charge, the court reviewed the claim under State v. Evans, because it implicated his constitutional right to be informed of the nature and cause of the accusation against him and because the court had granted such review for a similar claim. But the court refused to review his claim that he was prejudiced because his trial defense of a right to enter the building as a guest was insufficient to meet the enlarged offense. The record did not support that portion of his claim. The court held that defendant's theory of defense presented at trial that he never intended to commit a crime in the building was not prejudiced by the erroneous instruction. The court concluded from the verdicts that the erroneous charge manifestly did not affect the verdict, so the error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court found no reversible error.

State v. Chapman

Appellate Court of Connecticut


16 Conn. App. 38; 546 A.2d 929; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 330

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in each case, charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of robbery in the first degree and one count of criminal attempt to commit robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Schaller, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty, from which the defendants filed separate appeals to this court.

The appellant in the first case filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted each of them of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4) and of criminal attempt to commit robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49 and 53a-134(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendants of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4), and of criminal attempt to commit robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49 and 53a-134(a)(2). Defendants appealed. The court held that the trial court properly admitted into evidence the in-court identification testimony of a witness where there had been no pre-trial identification by the witness. The court ruled that the trial court properly refused to grant defendant one's request for a recess to prepare further cross-examination of a witness where defendant one failed to identify any particular way in which he would have been aided had he been given further time to prepare his cross-examination. The court determined that the trial court did not violate defendants' rights of confrontation by a refusal to admit into evidence, for impeachment purposes, tape recordings of telephone conversations that involved a witness where both defendants were permitted to question the witness at length regarding his character, his habitual lying, and his strong motive for testifying for the State.


OUTCOME: The court held against defendants and found no error as to either defendant.

State v. Washington


No. 6060


Appellate Court of Connecticut


15 Conn. App. 704; 546 A.2d 911; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 320


April 21, 1988, Argued  
August 30, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and attempted assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, geographical area number five, and tried to the jury before Curran, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of attempted assault in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, Connecticut, of attempted assault in the first degree. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: After defendant put a gun to the victim's head and demanded money, the victim struggled with him, and the gun fired once. Defendant forced the handgun towards the victim's midsection. The victim heard a "click," which he believed was the gun's hammer being cocked. Defendant fled, police caught him, retraced his route, and found an unexploded .38 caliber bullet with a dented primer. An expert testified that the dented primer was probably caused when the gun misfired. The instant court held that the evidence was sufficient to prove defendant intended to cause the victim serious physical harm under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1), and that he committed an act that constituted a "substantial step" toward the commission of first degree assault under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-49(b). After an Evans review of alleged instructional error, to which defendant had not objected, the instant court found a technical error in the trial court's charge on attempt to commit a crime under § 53a-49(b). However, this error was harmless, as the instructions, taken as a whole, properly guided the jury in their determination of whether the essential elements of the crime had been proven.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Ortiz


No. 6107


Appellate Court of Connecticut


15 Conn. App. 749; 546 A.2d 338; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 326


June 7, 1988, Argued  
August 30, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of carrying a pistol without a permit and criminal possession of a revolver, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before Maiocco, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of conviction, after a jury trial in the lower court (Connecticut), of carrying a pistol without a permit in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35 and criminal possession of a revolver in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217.


OVERVIEW: Each of defendant's claims had recently been addressed and rejected by the court. Defendant's argued that the trial court erred in refusing to sever the criminal possession of a revolver charge, which required proof of a prior felony conviction, from the charge of carrying a pistol without a permit. The court disagreed and found that defendant failed to sustain his heavy burden of showing that the denial of his motion to sever resulted in substantial injustice or prejudice. Defendant also claimed that the trial court's failure to bifurcate, sua sponte, the trial of the criminal possession of a revolver charge for separate jury consideration of the two elements of the crime, amounted to plain error. This claim was without merit. Defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217(a) was raised for the first time on appeal. Defendant's conviction of carrying a pistol without a permit in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35, and his conviction of criminal possession of a revolver in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217(a), did not violate the protection against multiple punishments for the same offense under the Double Jeopardy Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

In re Rafael A.


No. 6290


Appellate Court of Connecticut


15 Conn. App. 641; 545 A.2d 1162; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 312


April 14, 1988, Argued  
August 23, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to adjudicate the respondent minor child a delinquent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, Juvenile Matters at Hartford, and tried to the court, Brenneman, J.; judgment adjudicating the respondent a delinquent child, from which the respondent appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent sought review of a decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain, Juvenile Matters at Hartford (Connecticut), which adjudicated him a delinquent child following the trial court's finding that he had committed the crimes of larceny in the fourth degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-125 and breach of the peace in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181 while he was on probation.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was found to be a delinquent and ordered to live at a state owned psychiatric hospital for adolescents as a condition of probation. A breach of peace charge arose when he struck a staff member. Subsequent to that incident, he was released. While he was still on probation, he was found to be in possession of stolen property. On appeal of his adjudication as a delinquent, the court affirmed. The court held that although he was charged in the petition with unlawfully taking property and adjudicated a delinquent for possession of stolen property, his defense was not prejudiced. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-119, proof of the receipt of stolen property was sufficient proof of larceny in the fourth degree regardless of whether respondent was charged with wrongfully taking, or obtaining, or withholding the property from the owner. Further, the trial court could reasonably have inferred a criminal connection with the property from his possession of it shortly after it was stolen. Respondent's right to cross-examine the complainant in the breach of the peace charge was not unconstitutionally restricted, as the line of questioning excluded was irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1169 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reddick


No. 5421


Appellate Court of Connecticut


15 Conn. App. 342; 545 A.2d 1109; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 281


February 9, 1988, Argued  
August 2, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the first degree and criminal possession of a pistol or firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Falsey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him, after trial to a jury, of burglary in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-101(a)(1), and criminal possession of a firearm in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217.


OVERVIEW: Defendant first argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence seized during a search of an apartment because the search exceeded the scope of a valid search incident to an arrest. The court held that the seizure of the gun was simultaneous with defendant's arrest and the police had adequate justification. Next, defendant asserted that his statements made regarding the weapon should have been suppressed. The court decided there was no error in admitting the statements because they were made after defendant knowingly and intelligently waived his rights under Miranda. Defendant further contended that admission of another individual's statement into evidence was erroneous because it was hearsay. The court disagreed and held that there was a hearsay exception that applied and the trial court did not abuse its discretion. Defendant also argued that the jury instructions were invalid. The court determined that the jury was not misled, any error was harmless, and there was no confusion. Finally, defendant claimed that there was pervasive prosecutorial misconduct but the court noted that the remarks did not warrant reversal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

Skinner v. Angliker


No. 5519


Appellate Court of Connecticut


15 Conn. App. 297; 544 A.2d 246; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 268


December 10, 1987, Argued  
July 26, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for wrongful discharge from employment, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex and tried to the jury before Hon. Harry W. Edelberg, state trial referee; verdict for the plaintiff; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiff's motion for counsel fees and costs and rendered judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a director of a state mental health facility and the commissioner of the department of mental health, appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut), which denied defendants' motion to dismiss, based on sovereign immunity, plaintiff former employee's claim that he was wrongfully discharged from employment at the state mental health facility and awarded damages to the employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee was employed by the department of mental health as a forensic treatment specialist at the state mental facility. The employee was discharged a few days after notifying officials ranked higher than his immediate supervisors of his complaints regarding the abuse of patients. The employee instituted an action against defendants for wrongful discharge from employment and alleged that he was discharged and disciplined by defendants because he exercised his First Amendment rights and that defendants' action was in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-51q. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss based on the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The trial court denied the motion and determined that the employee was entitled to a trial by jury. Defendants appealed the verdict in favor of the employee, and the court set aside the judgment and remanded the matter. The court held that, while Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-51q waived the sovereign immunity by its expressed terms, the employee was not entitled to a jury trial in the action under § 31-51q. The court held that the employee had no right to a jury trial under the state constitution or Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-215.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment in favor of the employee and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Mancinone


No. 5046


Appellate Court of Connecticut


15 Conn. App. 251; 545 A.2d 1131; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 258


March 2, 1988, Argued  
July 19, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a minor, two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the second degree, and one count of the crime of possession of marihuana, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Lavery, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of risk of injury to a minor and one count of possession of marihuana, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him of two counts of risk of injury to a minor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 and illegal possession of marihuana in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279. He was sentenced to concurrent terms of six years, eight years, and one year imprisonment, respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant offered a 13-year old girl and 14-year old girl alcohol and marihuana in exchange for sexual activities. Defendant engaged in sexual activities with the two victims on several occasions. He was subsequently convicted of two counts of risk of injury to a minor and possession of marihuana. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held the State's failure to prove the dates of the risk of injury did not violate his constitutional right to present a defense. The court stated defendant placed the victims in a situation likely to injure their health over a period of more than two years and the threat was continual in nature. The court also held the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions and evidentiary rulings were correct. The court ruled evidence of sexual conduct between defendant and an adult friend of the victims was admissible and the trial court properly denied a motion to suppress marihuana seized at defendant's home. The court further stated a unanimity instruction and other jury instructions correctly stated the law and the trial court did not commit errors in sentencing defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of two counts of risk of injury to a minor and illegal possession of marihuana, and sentenced him to concurrent, respective terms of six years, eight years, and one year imprisonment.

 

1172 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Banta


Nos. 4814, 4831


Appellate Court of Connecticut


15 Conn. App. 161; 544 A.2d 1226; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 373


February 9, 1988, Argued  
July 12, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in each case, charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and criminal possession of a pistol, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Schaller, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of both crimes in the first case and verdict and judgment of guilty of robbery in the first degree in the second case, from which the defendants filed separate appeals to this court.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with robbery in the first degree and criminal possession of a pistol. After denying their motions for severance that requested both separate trials for defendants and separate trials on the charges, the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) convicted the first defendant of both crimes and convicted the second defendant of robbery in the first degree. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the denial of their motions to sever and to order separate trials and the jury instructions on drawing inferences from circumstantial evidence. The court affirmed. First, the trial court gave adequate consideration to the potential for prejudice caused by the joinder of the charges. In light of the numerous references to the second defendant's prior felony convictions and incarceration, the court could not conclude that any substantial injustice resulted from the refusal to order separate trials on the two offenses. Any prejudicial effect to the first defendant, who did not testify at trial, caused by the joinder of the two counts was minimal. His prior conviction was presented to the jury by stipulation, but the cautionary instruction was complete and emphatic. Second, despite defendants' failure to except to the charge, the claim was reviewable because the instruction was erroneous. However, it was not reasonably possible that the erroneous instruction misled the jury on the state's burden of proof on the robbery charge because the jury's verdict depended not on circumstantial evidence but upon the credit it gave to the complainant's direct testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions.

 

1173 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Boone


Nos. 5703, 5840


Appellate Court of Connecticut


15 Conn. App. 34; 544 A.2d 217; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 235


March 10, 1988, Argued  
June 21, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Dranginis, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of assault in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed; thereafter, the court rendered judgment revoking the defendant's probation, and the defendant filed a separate appeal.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of assault in the first degree and revoked defendant's probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-14 clearly required that to be afforded the benefit of the defense of duress, defendant must have engaged in the proscribed conduct because he was coerced. There was no evidence of such coercion produced at defendant's trial, and thus, the trial court did not have to instruct the jury as to the duress defense. The State did not err in using defendant's pre-arrest silence to impeach the credibility of his self-defense claim. The State's comment regarding defendant's post-arrest silence were improper, but it was clear beyond a reasonable doubt that the jury would have returned a guilty verdict without the impermissible questioning and impermissible comment. The pre-trial identification of defendant through a photographic line-up was proper. The record did not reveal that the trial court's demeanor or conduct denied defendant a fair trial, thus a mistrial was not warranted. While the State did make improper comments about defendant, the impropriety was not so egregious as to deny defendant a fair trial. The trial court's action in revoking defendant's probation was within its sentencing limits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant.

 

1174 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Warren


No. 4450


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


14 Conn. App. 688; 544 A.2d 209; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 496


November 18, 1987, Argued  
June 14, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and conspiracy to commit sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Kremski, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which entered a judgment of guilty against defendant on the State's charges of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a) and conspiracy to commit sexual assault in the first degree in violation of § 53a-70(a) and of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-48(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on the elements of first degree sexual assault and that its refusal to admit evidence of the victim's prior conduct denied his Sixth Amendment rights. On appeal, the court found no reversible error. The jury instruction was an accurate statement of law because the plain language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a) imposed liability for sexual assault on anyone who compelled another to engage in sexual intercourse by the use of force regardless of with whom the sexual act was performed. Likewise, evidence of the victim's prior sexual conduct was properly excluded because it did not tend to show that the victim lied about her prior experiences. Further, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in limiting defense counsel's cross-examination of the victim about her prior rape complaint by prohibiting questions collateral to the issue of the victim's reliability, and defendant failed to show that he was prejudiced by the limitation. Finally, the Sixth Amendment was satisfied where defense counsel was allowed to question the victim about the prior complaint so as to put the issue of her reliability before the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision adjudging defendant guilty of the crimes charged.

Kraus v. Newton


No. 5143


Appellate Court of Connecticut


14 Conn. App. 561; 542 A.2d 1163; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 205


December 1, 1987, Argued  
June 7, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained as a result of the defendant's alleged negligence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain and tried to the jury before Higgins, J.; verdict and judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim challenged a judgment, after a jury trial in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), in favor of defendant landlord in an action for injuries sustained in a fall on an icy stair. He also contested the denial of a motion to set aside the verdict, asserting that the trial court erred in marking an exhibit for identification posttrial and in instructing the jury on the duty of care.


OVERVIEW: The victim slipped and fell while descending the stairs of the landlord's premises during a freezing rain, and brought negligence action to recover for his personal injuries. The trial court rendered judgment for the landlord and denied the victim's motion to set aside the verdict. He appealed, asserting that the trial court erred in marking an exhibit for identification after the trial, and in instructing the jury as to the landlord's duty of care. The court disagreed and affirmed. It explained that, when requested by the victim, the trial court failed to mark for identification a written statement of the landlord that was in the possession of the landlord's counsel. Posttrial the trial court acknowledged this error and marked the statement for identification. The court noted the rule that all exhibits offered had to be marked for identification, and held that the trial court should have had the proffered statement marked. But, as the statement contained nothing useful for impeachment, even had it been admissible, the victim had not been harmed by the omission. The jury charge, as to a landlord's duty to remove snow and ice within a reasonable time after a storm, was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the landlord in a negligence action by the victim, who slipped and fell on an icy stair.

State v. Rado

Appellate Court of Connecticut


14 Conn. App. 322; 541 A.2d 124; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 163

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of bribe receiving, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before L. The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of three counts of the crime of bribe receiving in violation of Conn. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of an investigating grand juror, challenged the denial of his motion to dismiss, and challenged the denial of his motion for access to grand juror transcripts.

The court held defendant had no standing to raise a claim that it was unconstitutional for a judge to act as a grand juror. The court held that even if it chose to review defendant's claim that it was unconstitutional for a judge to act as a grand juror, defendant's claim failed. The court held that former Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-148(a) where defendant should not have been charged under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-161b because § 53a-161b penalized contractors, not public officials.

State v. Golding


No. 5107


Appellate Court of Connecticut


14 Conn. App. 272; 541 A.2d 509; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 158


November 6, 1987, Argued  
May 3, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of larceny in the second degree, conspiracy to commit larceny in the second degree, fraud in obtaining aid and conspiracy to commit fraud in obtaining aid, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Vasington, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of larceny in the second degree and fraud in obtaining aid, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted her of larceny in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-123(a)(4), and of general assistance fraud in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-282 (Rev. to 1983), and which ordered restitution and 200 hours of community service as conditions of her probation.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of larceny in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-123(a)(4), and of general assistance fraud in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-282 (Rev. to 1983). The trial court ordered restitution and 200 hours of community service as conditions of her probation. Defendant appealed. The court held that the conviction of defendant for violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-123(a)(4), 17-282 did not violate Conn. Const. art. 1, § 8 where, although the offenses arose out of the same transaction, they constituted separate offenses. The court held that the trial court did not err in its instructions to the jury on an element of defrauding a public community under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-119(6)(1) and (2) where the jury instruction was consistent with a theory that defendant had committed a single crime. The court decided that the trial court properly sentenced defendant to restitution under Conn. Const. art. 1, § 8 where the amount of restitution ordered was related to the offense and had sufficient indicia of reliability to satisfy due process.


OUTCOME: The court held against defendant and found no error.

In re Steven G.


No. 5613


Appellate Court of Connecticut


14 Conn. App. 205; 540 A.2d 107; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 133


November 18, 1987, Argued  
April 19, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to adjudicate the respondent minor a delinquent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Juvenile Matters at New Haven, where, after the commencement of trial, the court, Ottaviano, J., granted the state's motion to amend the petition; thereafter, the matter was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere; judgment adjudicating the respondent a delinquent, from which the respondent appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which denied his motion to dismiss certain charges against him and his subsequent adjudication as a delinquent following his plea of nolo contendere to a reduced charge of conspiracy to commit robbery in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-48 and 53-136.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was charged with criminal liability for robbery in the second in connection with a theft that occurred at a store. After the cross-examination of an accomplice was complete, the State, over the juvenile's objection and exception, was permitted to amend the petition of delinquency to include four additional charges, including conspiracy to commit robbery in the second degree. Accordingly, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

In re Saba P.


No. 5753


Appellate Court of Connecticut


13 Conn. App. 605; 538 A.2d 711; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 118


December 16, 1987, Argued  
March 8, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition by the commissioner of children and youth services to terminate the parental rights of the respondent mother in her minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, Juvenile Matters at Uncasville, and tried to the court, Koletsky, J.; judgment granting the petition, from which the respondent appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother challenged a judgment from the Superior Court, Judicial District of New London, Juvenile Matters at Uncasville (Connecticut), which granted a petition brought by petitioner Commissioner Of Children And Youth Services to terminate the parental rights of the mother in her minor child.


OVERVIEW: The mother voluntarily placed her child in foster care. The child was subsequently adjudicated an uncared for child and committed to the Department of Children and Youth Services. The Commissioner filed a petition to terminate the parental rights of the child's parents, which was subsequently amended to reflect that the father was deceased. The trial court found that it was in the child's best interest to terminate the mother's parental rights. On appeal, the court found no error. Whether the grounds for termination existed for not less than one year, as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-43a(b), was a question of fact. The child's mother suffered from a long history of mental illness, diagnosed as chronic schizophrenia, undifferentiated. Her prognosis was poor and the child would clearly have been at risk if placed in her care. Visits between the mother and child failed to establish a positive bond. The child had no emotional ties to the mother and had developed a warm and loving relationship with her foster parents. There was ample support for the trial court's finding that the grounds for termination of the mother's parental rights were in existence for not less than one year.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the termination of the mother's parental rights.

 

1181 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Peay


No. 5523


Appellate Court of Connecticut


13 Conn. App. 578; 538 A.2d 708; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 114


November 18, 1987, Argued  
March 8, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of larceny in the sixth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number sixteen, and tried to the jury before Smith, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain, Geographical Area Number Sixteen (Connecticut), convicting defendant of larceny in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-125b.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for larceny on the grounds that the trial court erroneously instructed the jury on the issue of circumstantial evidence. The trial court instructed the jury that an inference could be drawn if it were more probable than not that the fact to be inferred was true. The court found error and remanded the case for a new trial. The court held that in order to prove a larceny, the state had to prove that defendant intentionally took possession of a television set that was offered for sale and that defendant did not pay the purchase price of the television. The state presented no direct evidence on either of these points. Defendant admitted being in the store. There was no direct evidence that a television set was purchased that evening, nor was there any direct evidence that the television set carton that was observed outside next to defendant contained a TV set or was from the victim. This was not a case where circumstantial evidence was used to bolster the direct evidence; rather, it was a case in which circumstantial evidence was used to prove essential elements of the crime charged. The jury instruction contributed to the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The court found error and set aside defendant's conviction. The case was remanded for a new trial.

 

1182 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. De Matteo


No. 5201


Appellate Court of Connecticut


13 Conn. App. 596; 538 A.2d 1068; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 117


December 1, 1987, Argued  
March 8, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the third degree and larceny in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Gray, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty on both counts, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven, Geographical Area Number Six (Connecticut) of robbery in the third degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-136, and larceny in the second degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-123. On appeal, he argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in instructing the jury regarding drawing inferences from circumstantial evidence and in denying a motion to correct an illegal sentence.


OVERVIEW: Although a robber had a nylon stocking over his face, the victim was able to give the police a description of his age, height, race, build, facial features, and clothing. Three days later, after viewing numerous persons in the parking lot at defendant's place of employment, including about seven white males, the victim identified defendant, a white male, as the robber. On appeal, the court held that the identification procedure was not impermissibly suggestive. Therefore, the denial of defendant's motion to suppress the victim's in-court and out-of-court identifications was proper. The jury charge on the issue of identity was balanced as to the respective functions of the judge and the jury and it did not direct or advise the jury on how to decide the matter. No injustice was done to defendant. Although the charge on circumstantial evidence was error, considering the overall charge and its likely effect on the jury, it was not reasonably possible that the jury was misled, so the error was not reversible. Defendant's convictions for larceny in the second degree and robbery in the third degree did not violate his double jeopardy rights, and the separate sentences imposed were proper.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

1184 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vega


No. 6115


Appellate Court of Connecticut


13 Conn. App. 438; 537 A.2d 505; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 51


November 13, 1987, Argued  
February 16, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the third degree, threatening and larceny in the sixth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, and tried to the jury before Susco, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the defendant pleaded nolo contendere to the charge of being a persistent serious felony offender and the court rendered judgment of guilty on all counts, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him after a jury trial of burglary in the third degree, threatening, and larceny in the sixth degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was identified by a police officer as being the person that he saw exiting through the broken window of a pharmacy that was burglarized. The officer confronted and pursued the fleeing man. The court affirmed defendant's convictions, holding first that it was not error for the trial court to deny defendant's motion to suppress the identification because, although the officer's viewing of defendant in a single photo was unnecessarily suggestive, the resulting identification was reliable under the totality of the circumstances. Second, the court did not err in giving a Ledbetter jury instruction, because the officer had a good look at defendant when he threatened the officer at the scene and the officer was able to provide a good description. Third, the trial court's instructions on the presumption of innocence were sufficient and defendant was not deprived of a fair trial thereby. Finally, the evidence was sufficient to prove that defendant was guilty of the crimes charged beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that there was no error in defendant's trial for burglary in the third degree, threatening, and larceny in the sixth degree.

Hartford Federal Sav. & Loan Ass'n v. Tucker


No. 4628


Appellate Court of Connecticut


13 Conn. App. 239; 536 A.2d 962; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 20


October 14, 1987, Argued  
January 19, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose mortgages on certain properties owned by the named defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Vasington, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for appointment of a receiver of rents, and the court Barall, J., rendered judgment of strict foreclosure; thereafter, the court, Hennessey, J., denied the named defendant's motion for permission to sue the receiver of rents and the court, A. Aronson, J., awarded fees and expenses to two committees of sale, and the named defendant appealed and the committee of sale William L. Ankerman cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error on the appeal; cross appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant borrower appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed the borrower's claim against a rent receiver appointed to manage certain property subject to plaintiff lender's action to foreclose four separate mortgages and rejected the borrower's challenge to the award of fees and expenses to the committees of sale pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-25.


OVERVIEW: The lender sought to foreclose on four separate properties. The borrower hotly contested the lender's actions. The trial court appointed a rent receiver for certain properties and appointed committees of sale for certain properties. Before the trial court approved proposed sales of the latter properties, the borrower filed an appeal that resulted in a reversal, which caused the trial court to abort the sales. The borrower filed suit against the rent receiver for mismanagement. The trial court, after a full hearing, dismissed the borrower's suit and awarded fees and expenses to the committees of sale even though the sales had not been completed. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the borrower received due process of law because he was given a full hearing. The court also held that the trial court properly awarded fees and expenses for the aborted sales under § 49-25 because the use of the phrase "of such sale" did not require confirmation by the trial court of the sale as a condition precedent to the allowance of costs and fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which had dismissed the borrower's claim against the rent receiver for mismanagement and had awarded fees and expenses to the committees of sale.

 

1186 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Shelby Mut. Ins. Co. v. Bishop, Kirk & Saunders, Inc.


No. 4540


Appellate Court of Connecticut


13 Conn. App. 189; 535 A.2d 387; 1988 Conn. App. LEXIS 16


October 15, 1987, Argued  
January 5, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for breach of contract, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Lewis, J., assigned the matter to David Albert, court approved arbitrator, who found the issues in favor of the plaintiff; thereafter, the court, Cioffi, J., rendered judgment in accordance with the arbitrator's findings, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a party to the contract in dispute, brought an action to recover damages for breach of contract against defendant insurance company. The insurance company appealed a decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which rendered judgment in accordance with the court-appointed arbitrator's findings in favor of plaintiff, and denied its motions for a trial de novo and to reopen the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The court referred the action to an arbitrator, but neither the insurer nor its counsel appeared. The trial court adopted the arbitrator's decision, and the sole issue presented was whether the right of the insurer to trial by jury under the Connecticut Constitution was violated. The court affirmed and held that the right was not violated. A party who challenged a statute on constitutional grounds had no easy burden; every intendment would be made in favor of constitutionality, and invalidity had to be established beyond a reasonable doubt. The right to a jury trial could be subjected to reasonable conditions, and provision by the legislature for an alternative means of dispute resolution through the use of arbitrators to hear cases claimed for jury trial was part of an effort to alleviate court congestion. The right to a trial by jury in such cases was preserved inviolate by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-549z and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 546S; however, only a party who had appeared at the hearing could claim a trial de novo. The insurer did not attend the hearing before the arbitrator, and the objection to its motion for trial de novo was properly sustained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that adopted the findings of the court-appointed arbitrator in a contract dispute brought by plaintiff against the insurer.

State v. Biggs

On appeal defendant's major assertion was that the lower court erred when it denied his motion to suppress. The court found no error. State v. High


No. 5051


Appellate Court of Connecticut


12 Conn. App. 685; 533 A.2d 1217; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 1130


September 30, 1987, Argued  
December 8, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of attempted larceny in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Gray, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial district of New Haven, Geographical Area Number Six (Connecticut), which had convicted him of attempted larceny in the second degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-123(a)(3) and 53a-49.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred (1) in failing to inquire into his and defense counsel's claims of breakdown of the attorney-client relationship, and (2) in denying defense counsel's request that new counsel be appointed. At trial, defendant did not ask that alternate counsel be appointed. The court addressed defendant's concerns and instructed him to discuss his concerns further with his attorney, and was advised that he could get a new lawyer only if he retained private counsel. Following a recess, the trial resumed, at which time the assistant public defender orally moved that alternate counsel be appointed to represent defendant, on the basis of defendant's earlier complaint and on counsel's own representation of a breakdown in the attorney-client relationship. After a brief colloquy, the court denied the motion. The trial continued, and defendant was found guilty. The court held that the trial judge's failure to inquire into defendant's request for new counsel, where defendant had already made known the reasons for his request, was not error. It was not an abuse of discretion for the trial court to have refused to appoint alternate counsel.


OUTCOME: The court found no error and affirmed.

 

1190 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Taylor


No. 4557


Appellate Court of Connecticut


12 Conn. App. 427; 531 A.2d 157; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 1081


May 13, 1987, Argued  
September 22, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and passing in a no passing zone, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, geographical area number nineteen, and presented to the court, Klaczak, J., on a plea of nolo contendere; after the charge of passing in a no passing zone was nolled, judgment of guilty of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland, Geographical Area Number Nineteen (Connecticut), which denied his amended motion to suppress two breathalyzer tests upon entry of a plea of nolo contendere to the charge of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the results of the breathalyzer tests were inadmissible on the grounds that his consent to the tests, after being warned of the possible loss of his license if he refused to take the tests, did not constitute the voluntary consent to a search required by U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court rejected defendant's contention, finding that defendant chose to engage in a regulated activity, that of driving a motor vehicle, and thereby became subject to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b. Further, the court found that the choice between consent to a breathalyzer test or refusal with the possible loss of license did not vitiate consent if no force, deception, or coercion was used or threatened. The court determined that the denial of defendant's motion was warranted whether the denial was analyzed in terms of statutory implied consent or in terms of the reasonableness of the search in view of exigent circumstances. Thus, the court concluded that the trial court properly denied the motion to suppress because there was no unreasonable search.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment that denied defendant's motion to suppress the results of breathalyzer tests.

State v. Bondi


Nos. 5390, 5391, 5410


Appellate Court of Connecticut


12 Conn. App. 417; 531 A.2d 151; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 1080


June 3, 1987, Argued  
September 22, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Infractions complaints, issued against the defendants for their operation of unregistered and unnumbered vessels, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the court, Buzaid, J.; judgments of guilty, from which the defendants filed separate appeals to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In separate cases, two defendants appealed from the judgments of the Stamford-Norwalk Superior Court (Connecticut) that imposed fines upon each of them for operating their respective vessels in Connecticut waters for more than 60 days without being properly numbered and registered, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 15-144(h).


OVERVIEW: Both of the vessels owned by defendants were used for pleasure and neither vessel had been numbered or registered in Connecticut pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 15-142 to 15-144. They were cited for and found guilty of violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 15-144(h) after a boat patrol officer observed their vessels docked in Connecticut waters for more than 60 days. Defendants appealed. In affirming, the appellate court ruled that credibility of witnesses was for the trier of fact and the evidence was sufficient to find the vessels were in Connecticut waters for the requisite number of days. There was no authority for defendants' claims that their Sixth Amendment rights to cross-examination had been violated and the court declined to consider their argument that the statutory scheme violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, because there was no evidence that their vessels were engaged in interstate commerce. Payment of a use tax was not necessarily a precondition to registration and defendants' claims that the use tax was tonnage duty, in violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 3, was not ripe for adjudication.


OUTCOME: The judgments imposing fines upon defendants were affirmed.

State v. Trujillo


No. 4059


Appellate Court of Connecticut


12 Conn. App. 320; 531 A.2d 142; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 1168


May 12, 1987, Argued  
September 15, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the second degree and risk of injury to or impairing the morals of a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, geographical area number five, and tried to the jury before Rottman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of assault in the second degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-60, and risk of injury to a child, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21.


OVERVIEW: The victim testified at trial that he received the iron burn as an accident. However, the victim had previously told police that defendant burned him to punish him for a mini bike accident. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in its charge to the jury on the offense of risk of injury to a minor. In a bill of particulars, the state specified that defendant was charged only with committing an act directly on the minor that was injurious to his moral or physical well-being. However, the jury instructions referred to another alternative under the statute that dealt with willfully or unlawfully permitting a child to have been placed in a situation where it's life or limb was in danger. Defendant's defense was directed to the specific act alleged in the bill of particulars. The evidence which defendant might have offered had he been charged with the entire risk of injury statute, however, would logically have differed from that which he did present to defend against the portion of the statute with which he was charged. The court concluded that defendant met his burden of proving that he was prejudiced in the presentation of his defense by the trial court's charge to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court set aside defendant's conviction for assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child. The court remanded for a new trial.

State v. Mention


No. 5153


Appellate Court of Connecticut


12 Conn. App. 258; 530 A.2d 645; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 1063


June 2, 1987, Argued  
September 8, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the infractions of creating a public disturbance and simple trespass, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the court, Bassick, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of creating a public disturbance in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181 and simple trespass in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-110a.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was standing in a busy passageway of a mall food court when he was asked by a private security guard to move along. Defendant verbally attacked the security guard and director of security and challenged them to arrest him. There was no evidence that defendant entered the mall with the intent to trespass or knowledge that he was trespassing. The court reversed as to the simple trespass charge and affirmed as to the public disturbance charge. The court held that defendant was a business invitee that was not required to make a purchase. The court found that in the absence of evidence that defendant knowingly entered as a trespasser, there could be no trespass unless the possessor revoked the business invitee status. The court held that defendant's words and conduct fell within the fighting words exception to constitutionally protected speech as it served no purpose other than to challenge the security personnel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the public disturbance conviction. The court set aside the conviction for simple trespass and remanded with directions to render judgment for defendant on that count.

State v. Diorio


No. 4244


Appellate Court of Connecticut


12 Conn. App. 74; 529 A.2d 1320; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 1048


March 31, 1987, Argued  
August 18, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of tampering with a witness, breach of the peace and bribery, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before Burns, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of breach of the peace, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which entered judgment on the jury's verdict that found defendant guilty of aiding and abetting a breach of the peace in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-8 and 53a-181.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aiding and abetting a breach of the peace in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-8 and 53a-181. The court affirmed holding that (1) defendant's Sixth Amendment rights were not prejudiced where defendant was permitted the latitude to expose facts from which the jurors could have appropriately drawn inferences relating to the reliability of the witness; (2) the trial court properly limited cross-examination regarding a witness's prior acts because the acts were remote in time, had a tendency to confuse the jury, were not supported by sufficient evidence, and did not have probative value concerning veracity sufficient to outweigh the potential for prejudicial effect; (3) the trial court properly barred cross-examination regarding prior convictions because defendant was unable to demonstrate any convictions by the witness which were punishable by imprisonment for more than one year; (4) being an accessory to a breach of the peace was a cognizable crime under Connecticut law; and (5) the court's charge regarding reasonable doubt, reviewed in light of the instruction as a whole, was adequate to guide the jury and protect against injustice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of Superior Court, Danbury District (Connecticut), which convicted him of burglary in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen.
