Defendant chiefly claimed speedy trial, notice, evidentiary, and jury charge errors.


OVERVIEW: After being identified as running from the scene of a burglary carrying a box, defendant was convicted of third degree burglary, third degree larceny, and being a persistent serious felony offender. Defendant appealed, claiming: (1) denial of a speedy trial; (2) a faulty jury charge on accessory liability; (3) a faulty jury charge on larceny; (4) insufficient evidence of larceny; (5) admission of uncharged misconduct; (6) failure to dismiss the charge of being a persistent serious felony offender, and (7) no fair notice of sentence enhancement on both felony counts. State v. Vilhotti


No. 4087


Appellate Court of Connecticut


11 Conn. App. 709; 529 A.2d 235; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 1036


March 5, 1987, Argued  
August 4, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and tried to the jury before Allen, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of robbery in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of robbery in the first degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court erred in not charging the jury properly and in failing to suppress several out-of-court and in-court identifications. The court upheld defendant's conviction. The court ruled that the charge given by the trial court involving specific intent was specifically requested by defendant. The section of the charge defendant claimed was erroneous was precisely what he requested; therefore he was not entitled to review. The court held that photographic identifications by the State's witnesses were not impremissively suggestive. The identification of defendant by one of the witnesses was unexpected. The procedure used by the police accidentally aided in defendant's identification. The court concluded that the photographic array was reliable and supported by sufficient evidence. All the witnesses' had the opportunity to get a view of defendant and all three witnesses' description matched.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of robbery in the first degree.

 

1197 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Malines


No. 4594


Appellate Court of Connecticut


11 Conn. App. 425; 527 A.2d 1229; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 999


February 6, 1987, Argued  
July 7, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of manslaughter in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before McKeever, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted her upon a jury verdict of manslaughter in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-56.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's husband attempted to take a gun from defendant during a domestic dispute. The gun fired and fatally wounded the husband. Defendant claimed that the trial court's instruction on circumstantial evidence was erroneous. The court remanded the action for a new trial, finding error in the trial court's jury instruction. Because defendant's state of mind was the principal disputed issue in the instant case, the court concluded that the trial court's charge was subject to the court's close scrutiny. The court held that the charge impermissibly diluted the State's burden of proof at trial because it informed the jurors that an inferred fact could be drawn from a proven fact if the jurors found that such proven fact made it more probable than not that the fact to be inferred from the evidence was true. The court rejected defendant's claim that there was insufficient evidence for the jury to find beyond a reasonable doubt that she caused her husband's death. The court could not find as a matter of law that the decedent's conduct constituted a sufficient intervening cause of his own demise so as to break the chain of causation.


OUTCOME: The court found error in the trial court's jury instruction. The court set aside the judgment that convicted defendant of manslaughter and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

1198 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kristy


No. 3856


Appellate Court of Connecticut


11 Conn. App. 473; 528 A.2d 390; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 1004


January 5, 1987, Argued  
July 7, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of manslaughter in the second degree with a motor vehicle while intoxicated, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, geographical area number five, and tried to the jury before Rottman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of misconduct with a motor vehicle, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant and the appellee filed motions for reargument which were denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut), which denied defendant's motion to suppress the blood-alcohol test results of two blood samples and one urine sample and convicted defendant of two counts of misconduct with a motor vehicle in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-57.


OVERVIEW: Defendant crashed his car while driving under the influence of alcohol. Two passengers died in the crash. Defendant consented to the hospital's release of a blood-alcohol test and consented to a blood-alcohol and urine test performed by the police. The State later charged defendant with two counts of manslaughter in the second degree. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress the test results, which showed that he was drunk, and instructed the jury on misconduct with a motor vehicle in violation of § 53a-57 as a lesser included offense. The jury convicted on the lesser included offense. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the blood and urine test results were properly admitted, even though defendant was not under arrest at the time they were taken, because he gave consent. However, the court held that misconduct with a motor vehicle was not a lesser included offense to manslaughter in the second degree because conviction of misconduct with a motor vehicle required proof of the mental state involved in criminal negligence, which was not an element of manslaughter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which had convicted defendant on the alleged lesser included offenses of misconduct with a motor vehicle based on the State's charges of manslaughter in the second degree.

 

1199 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mackor


No. 5129


Appellate Court of Connecticut


11 Conn. App. 316; 527 A.2d 710; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 979


April 1, 1987, Argued  
June 23, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, geographical area number seventeen, and tried to the jury before, Maloney, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70.


OVERVIEW: Defendant ditched two of the victim's friends, drove the victim to the woods on a pretense, and forcibly raped her before driving her to her friend's house. Defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of § 53a-70. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that § 53a-70(a) was not void for vagueness because a person of ordinary intelligence could understand what a "threat of the use of force" meant and because defendant failed to show any spatial or temporal disjunction that could have truncated his use of force from the ensuing sexual intercourse. The court also held that the trial court properly denied defendant's requested instruction on consent or resistance because the State did not have to show that defendant had to "overcome earnest resistance" as an element of the crime. The court also held that the trial court properly admitted evidence of spermatozoa and properly summarized the evidence during the charge because it also properly instructed the jury that it was its duty to assess the credibility of witnesses, weigh the evidence, and determine the facts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which had convicted defendant of sexual assault in the first degree.

 

1200 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Norwich v. Norwalk Wilbert Vault Co.


No. 4634


Appellate Court of Connecticut


11 Conn. App. 332; 527 A.2d 716; 1987 Conn. App. LEXIS 981


March 4, 1987, Argued  
June 23, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendant from operating a trucking terminal on certain premises owned by the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the court, Edelberg, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which granted appellee city's request for an injunction enjoining the company from using its premises, on which was located a cement manufacturing operation, as a trucking terminal.


OVERVIEW: The city claimed that the company was required to obtain site plan approval from the commission on the city plan before using its premises as a trucking terminal. The court affirmed the judgment, rejecting the company's contention that the trial court erred in concluding that site plan approval was required for the addition of truck storage use. The trial court concluded that the use of the company's premises as a trucking terminal was an increase in a preexisting permitted use, and it interpreted the city's zoning ordinances to require site plan approval whenever there was an increase in a permitted use of property. The court, however, determined that the company added a different permitted use to the previously permitted use on its property. The court held that the addition of a different permitted use required site plan approval to determine the effect of the use on the surrounding area. The court interpreted Norwich, Conn., Code § 10.2.2 to mean that each and every use in the heavy industrial district must be approved by the commission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that enjoined the company from using its premises as a trucking terminal.
